Delia was momentarily silent, then replied, "Thank you, much."

The manager simply dipped his head in respect but said nothing.

Delia turned and walked out followed by James, Jessie and the cat.

Outside, she turned to the trio again and said, "I don't know your names but I hope all your actions are richly rewarded."

"Thank you," Jessie answered, "Enjoy the apple butter."

The trio turned and walked away, avoiding any more conversation. Delia observed them as she thought things over, and then she turned in the opposite direction, boarded a city bus and went home.

When the Team Rocket trio were at a distance, Meowth piped up and said, "She's probably wondering how we managed it..."

"Well, most people aren't aware how our business works," answered James, "the store owner pays Rocket Enterprises for security services we persuade them to need, a.k.a. 'protection'..."

"...and now they are beholden to us," added Jessie slyly, "since they typically go into arrears in their payments."

"The debt is always collected," finished Meowth, "as the boss says... 'cash, assets or blood.' "

They all laughed; and headed towards Giovanni's office with the Poké Ball containing the Charizard.

Ecruteak's historical garden was a scenic and well-kept landscape, imbued with tradition of bygone years, with willow trees that cascaded their branches beautifully to the freshwater pond and the ancient pagoda-like temple known as the Tin Tower as a backdrop. Monks managed both the garden and the Tin Tower, which was considered sacred in Johto.

Close by was an even older tower, which had been destroyed in a fire. Archer figured it was the truest symbol of Ecruteak, and of many things in the world beside.

"The city of nostalgia. All that really means is it's the city of forlorn memories," Archer mused to himself.

He was not one to diminish such things however. Sometimes he thought too much of the past and living up to its aspirations; Team Rocket could not afford anything less than perfection in glory when the costs had been so high, and sometimes that meant even more expenditures. It was a cost-sunk fallacy in human lives. Not that Archer would ever acknowledge it.

He was reflecting on the towers when Kris hurried over to meet him. Right on schedule.

He motioned for her to follow him, and as they leisurely made their way towards the Burnt Tower, Archer asked, "How familiar are you with Johto mythology?"

"Only the basics," Kris admitted.

Archer told her the legend:

"They say long ago the tower used to be the roost of a legendary bird Pokémon known as a Ho-oh; however, the tower caught fire.

"How it happened became lost to history. Some people say it was a lightning storm. Others say it was during ancient wartime. For all we know a Charmander's tail got too close to a cask of rum. How it happened is beside the point.

"Three Pokémon perished in the blaze. They say Ho-oh revived them before it flew off, in the process sealing them into a deep slumber, and they wait somewhere for a chosen one to awaken them. You know, the typical kind of fantastical lore you hear in fairy-tales."

Completing the story, Archer turned expectantly to Kris. She stood straightly.

"You'll want me to catch the Legendary Pokémon?" she asked.

"What Legendary Pokémon? As I said, it's a fairy-tale. All you have to do is show you're nimble enough to maneuver around the debris and rubble."

"And then you'll let me into Team Rocket?" Kris prodded eagerly.

"Well...it's a start." Archer evaded her question as he went on, "Incidentally, the Burnt Tower is supposedly off-limits because it was deemed unsafe." His eyes glinted. "The floorboards are ancient and riddled with fire damage. But it's nothing too difficult for a member of Team Rocket. I'll be at a distance behind you judging how you do."

The Burnt Tower was indeed a fitting gauntlet. Charred boulders and blackened shards of wood littered what once upon a time must have been an impressive foyer. As Kris stepped gingerly ahead, Archer fell back observing her.

He did not have to wait long for her misstep; the floorboards gave way under her weight and came crashing down, and with a cry Kris plummeted to the basement level.

Archer stood at the precipice and gazed down. Seeing the outline of movement in the dark depths, he laid his hand over his face with disapproval.

"What are you doing falling into a hole?"

"I must've stepped on a weak plank of wood."

"Well, get out of there."

Kris groaned as she stumbled to her feet, feeling bruised from her fall. She was cursing how ungainly she must look when she caught sight of something on a pedestal only a few paces away. There were three large figures of stone, depictions of creatures that vaguely resembled a lion, a tiger, and a leopard.

"Look at this."

"I don't see anything," Archer replied. "It's too dark."

Curiosity brought her closer to the pedestal, and she did little beyond outstretch an arm towards the statues when suddenly a bright flare made her leap back.

As she watched, the stone crumbled away in brilliant white light. Where the three statues had once stood were now three live animals, released from their prison of stone.

The tiger's roar was like the boom of thunder, and its striped fur shimmered like electricity; the lion's was like the explosive eruption of a volcano, with a pelt that glowed as if tipped with flame. In unified exclamation, as if elated with their freedom, they bolted.

The leopard was the one to linger, as if it had taken an interest in the awed trainer. This was the most beautiful creature she'd ever seen, with fur like iridescent crystal and an aquamarine crown of horns; it enveloped itself with a sparkling mist of raindrops, and moved with surprising lightness. It threw back its head in a roar more like the high-pitched singsong of the wind, dancing about Kris in a circle, and with another joyous cry leapt out of the pit in a single bound.

Archer nearly lost his balance when the trio of Pokémon raced by him, faster than any animals he had ever witnessed: Entei the lion, Raikou the tiger, and Suicune the leopard.

Right behind them was Kris, cheering ecstatically as she clambered out of the pit. "Did you see them, Archer? Three Legendary Pokémon! Good thing I fell down that hole!"

"You were very lucky." Actually, this might be lucky for all of us. Wait till Giovanni hears about this.

Archer called Giovanni via videophone to inform him but found him less enthusiastic than he had hoped.

"So three more Legendary Pokémon now roam the planet," said Giovanni with a slight shrug, "If they're nomads, tracking them for a hunt will be expensive. Our resources would be better served elsewhere."

"But godfather..." Archer ventured, "isn't one of Team Rocket's goals to harness strong Pokémon? An organization can always use more power after all."

"Catch them if you can. Don't waste our capital on it."

Archer stayed silent, though he was in disagreement.

"If we're going to spend money on a hunt then we may as well hunt the most powerful Pokémon of all. Catching a Pokémon of that caliber first will make it easier to catch the rest as well if we then decide to."

The 'most powerful Pokémon of all', reflected Archer, was said to be extinct. Yes, they had heard rumors of such a creature surviving somewhere, yet nothing concrete.

"Tomorrow is Saturday," Giovanni mentioned. "You can take the rest of the weekend off before heading to Mahogany Town."

Mahogany Town? Archer thought. Oh no, not another itty bitty village.

"You're aware of our side project into Pokémon genetics."

"Yes, godfather," answered Archer. "It's run out of Cinnabar Island, isn't it?" Send me to Cinnabar instead. I don't care about the others; leave them here.

"Yes, but we're temporarily doing some tests away from Cinnabar."

Damn it.

"The experiment they need to run would attract too much attention there," explained Giovanni. "Dr. Colress is assisting us with his valuable research... he will be at our Mahogany base and will fill you in on what is needed."

Archer nodded obediently, and Giovanni hung up.

Chapter 4 - The Pursuit of Myth and Marvel

Mayor Evice S. Cade brushed the sweat away from his brow as he smiled to his political supporters gathered for the opening ceremony, pretending the Orrean sun was not so blisteringly hot and there was at least some relief of warm wind coming off of the desert. What he wouldn't have given for the refreshing breezes of Johto, which came off the mountain peaks and descended into peaceful, tree-filled towns.

He'd last been there – how many years ago, now?

Beside him stood Linford Rose and his wife Oleana, two Galarian transplants who owned a fortune in Orrean diamond mines. They were at their heart financial backers, not political ones, but where the two interests merged it followed that there should be some necessary crossover. And someone like Cade saw no difference in either finance or politics when it benefitted him somehow.

"Do you have the time...?" Cade asked Rose in a whisper. "I think it should've been over by now."

Rose glanced inconspicuously at the gold watch on his wrist. "The event's almost over," he answered in the same quiet tone.

"Thanks," murmured Cade, feigning another smile for the public.

Affability was Cade's cultivated image. The mayor of Phenac City was all smiles and helpfulness wherever he could be. In appearance he was unexceptional, about fifty, with a receding hairline turned grey with age and eyes turned clever by experience. Whereas Rose had once upon a time sought the pomp and pride of regional fame, Cade instead sought the charming demureness of a neighbor, someone who could be spoken of highly by civic clubs as an ideal citizen but who was never truly known in depth.

Phenac City, in his care, was pristine. It was one of the few cities of the Orre region that was a manmade oasis. Streams and cascades of glistening freshwater wove through Phenac and its sandstone streets, always bringing a coolness to the otherwise sweltering atmosphere. Cade, as its mayor, made sure it stood out as crime-free in comparison to the rest of dry and inhospitable Orre. Long forsaken by investors, the region had dwindling property values; even Pokémon had gone extinct in the wild, so Cade's tourism promotion was limited in efficacy until Mr. Rose arrived.

As the ceremony dragged on, Cade was becoming bored. He focused on the people around him instead of the long, monotonous speech being read; he found himself noticing Oleana, drawn as usual to the fine way of her motions.

Cade envied Mr. Rose greatly. Oleana's long blonde hair fell below her shoulders, accentuating a slender silhouette both tall and limber; painted eyes and lips and a coldly no-nonsense demeanor that Cade fancied held a streak of hot flame in private...

He forced himself to glance away.

Beside Oleana stood a Glaceon, an ice type Eevee evolution that was one of her Pokémon. Between her and her husband Oleana had the most Pokémon, numbering four, and occasionally expressed interest in getting a fifth, which in Orre meant having to buy one. Rose joked that it wouldn't be long before she had a full team of six like the Elite Four of most regions. Then again Cade wondered how serious she was about it, because with money like the Roses had they could afford a whole ranch.

The ribbon-cutting ceremony marked the culmination of a revitalization effort uniting city taxpayer funds with Mr. Rose's philanthropy, all for a combination casino-hotel-colosseum professed to one day be the grandest entertainment destination not only in all Orre but in all the world. Artist renderings depicted a lofty skyscraper of glass and gold, with the Pokémon stadium at the very top. Now hewn into reality, it was nothing short of magnificent.

Most important of all...there would be air conditioning, thought Cade. Despite not being far from where the present event was held, Phenac's cooler climate was far enough to make him long to return.

He picked up Glaceon and put the animal on his lap. Coolness radiated off the Pokémon, enveloping him as if he were in front of an open freezer. Glaceon flattened its ears, annoyed at being grabbed.

As the event concluded, Oleana scooped up her Glaceon, as Cade forced back a scowl.

"You're not going to stick around for the festivities?" he asked amicably.

"The truth is we have a lot to do back at Agate Town," Rose excused. The Glaceon, meanwhile, had started wriggling for Oleana to put it down.

"A pity," Cade replied. He half-watched Oleana as she obliged Glaceon by placing it on the ground, whereupon the creature immediately poked its Poké Ball open with its nose and vanished into its little sanctuary. "I was hoping we'd get to show off Zacian and Zamazenta in our opening match."

Zacian and Zamazenta were the Galar region's Legendary wolf Pokémon, two mighty steel types, of which Oleana was the trainer. It was exceptionally rare for anyone to own a Legendary Pokémon, and the fact providence had granted her two was astounding. Cade had already seen the creatures in person; he saw them frequently, in fact, whenever he paid a social visit to the Roses, but he'd only seen them in battle once.

Oleana reminded him of that accordingly. "You've seen them in a fight already. Remember the tournament in Orre's historical colosseum?"

"Of course. That's exactly why I think they'd be superb at Realgam Tower," Cade responded. "They swept through their opponents without even a struggle."

"Precisely why I'm reluctant to enter them in the colosseum match here."

"But why?"

"It wouldn't be fair to our opponent. There would be no challenge."

But all Pokémon by nature became restless without battling, even those as magnificent as Legendary Pokémon, and Oleana added clarifyingly, "Perhaps if they express motivation to fight at a later time."

He watched Rose and Oleana as they got into their limousine to depart for home. Their main residence was in Agate Town, a village on the opposite side of Orre that was a fairly long drive from here on the highway, but they owned property in Phenac too. It was then that Cade's transceiver phone rang. He glanced at the caller identification before answering.

"Mr. Silph, I didn't expect to hear from you this fine morning," said Cade, his polite alternative to asking What the fuck do you want?

"Cade, we have a slight upset." Silph sounded uneasy, which only made Cade leery, "Giovanni wants to buy us out in the Poké Ball market."

"Don't sell to him," Cade said.

There was silence.

"It'll be more profitable for you to not sell," Cade added, "How much do we pay you to manufacture and send us those modified Poké Balls?"

"You don't have to convince me about that," Silph replied, "a single shipment easily earns about triple what I'd get from a corporate buyout. But what if he finds out about our business deal?"

"So what? Silph, what can he do?"

"What can he do?" echoed Silph incredulously, "Cade, you're living in a dreamland. Everyone here in Kanto knows what Team Rocket is capable of."

"Cipher isn't exactly defenseless. In many ways we're more dangerous than Team Rocket," replied Cade calmly. "You have no need to worry about them."

"If you're sure..."

"When did he contact you?"

"A few days ago. I haven't heard anything from Giovanni since, and I've been getting very concerned what he might intend on doing."

"I'll run the situation past Mr. Rose. Keep me notified and don't sell," Cade emphasized.

Meanwhile, the limousine of Mr. and Mrs. Rose was on the highway. Whenever they went travelling, it was easy for them to notice how Orre was mostly desert, an unyielding, parched landscape so different from the region they had once called home.

"We've come a long way since the unfortunate incidents in the Galar region," reflected Mr. Rose, as he watched the sandy dunes swipe by the limousine window on the drive back to Agate Town, "I still can't fathom how easily we ended up being fooled. But that's all the past...The future is ours."

Oleana laid a hand on his. "We've remade our fortune here in Orre. Maybe it's time to let it go. We don't need to regain our old company, Macro Cosmos."

"It's not about Macro Cosmos." Rose was adamant, and he went on bitterly:

"Team Rocket took everything we built and achieved in Galar from us, and they did so through trickery. They will pay for it. It's time Giovanni accrues a few losses."

Following the incident at Mount Moon with the Charizard, things had gone uneventfully for Ash.

The gym at Cerulean, the city on the other side of Mount Moon, specialized in water types. That was Pikachu's forté, and they won with ease. His journey, all in all, had been going far more smoothly than he had imagined it would have; granted, he had been winning by luck not by skill, but with two badges to his name it hardly made a difference.

Ash and Pikachu had tried to go straight to Saffron City after having triumphed at the Cerulean gym, only to encounter the city gates blocked and a man attired in the black uniform of a Team Rocket minion, demanding a toll. Ash refused to pay the toll, which he said was literally highway robbery, so they detoured via the underpass – an underground pedestrian walkway that connected the cities of Cerulean, Celadon, and Vermillion. Ash arrived at Vermillion City by midday.

Known as "The Port of Exquisite Sunsets", Vermillion was a harbor town with plenty of interregional commerce. It was also renowned for its Pokémon gym, which specialized in electric types. The gym leader was a former military lieutenant by the name of Surge, who had fought alongside his Pokémon in the Plasma War on the Unovan side; Ash was eager to see the techniques of how a warrior would command Pokémon in battle, finding something oddly magnetic about the idea.

"Whatcha think, Pikachu? Should we head straight to the gym, or do we get a bite to eat first?"

"Piiika-chuuu," replied Pikachu, its plumed tail whisking happily as it leapt onto Ash's shoulders.

"Hey Red! Don't tell me you only just got to Vermillion?"

Ash turned upon hearing the familiar sound of his rival's voice, and even Pikachu lifted its ears. "Blue! How long have you been here?"

"Just on my way out," answered Gary.

Ash blinked with surprise. "You mean you already challenged the gym?"

"Yep," Gary said, proudly showing off the badge. The pin was a glittering orange gemstone cut into a sunburst shape, the distinctive emblem of Vermillion's Pokémon gym. "I'm off to the next town now. What took you so long to get here, Red?"

"I spent some time training with Pikachu in the tall grass around Cerulean. You know the Saffron gates were blocked," Ash couldn't help but remark with resentment.

"Yeah, but better not to mess with that." Nothing further was said about Team Rocket, and Gary changed the topic eagerly. "I've already caught like 40 kinds of Pokémon already. How many have you caught so far?"

"Well...to tell you the truth I've been focusing on training," Ash admitted. "I was actually considering doing the whole League challenge with just Pikachu."

"Red, you can't be serious! A solo run with a Pikachu?"

Ash looked defensive. "Lots of trainers do their League challenge with just one Pokémon. Over in Unova, one of their champions even won against the Elite Four with a lone Vaporeon."

"A Vaporeon is an evolved Pokémon. Unevolved Pokémon have abysmal stats and aren't good when you're in it competitive. I thought your goal was to actually win?"

"Well, I want to apply for a League job."

"They only take the best you know." Spite was written across Gary's face. "When are you getting a thunder stone to evolve your Pikachu into a Raichu, anyway?"

"Pikachu says he likes being a Pikachu."

"This is why I'm always a step ahead of you."

Pikachu was sparking angrily; Ash stroked his pet in a soothing way and tried not to become too aggravated himself by his rival's inflexible opinions.

"You know what you do when you have a weak Pokémon?" said Gary.

"Spend more time training it," Ash replied.

"Wrong. You trade it for something better."

Ash briefly found himself imagining, with more pleasure than he would have liked, letting Pikachu have at it and shock Gary. He held himself back from the temptation.

"See this Red?" added Gary, showing him a ticket with the name of some ocean liner, "Right now I've got a ticket for the ship leaving harbor, which will be making port at various regions. I heard there are different kinds of Pokémon worldwide and I'm going to spend a week catching some rare ones before returning to finish off my League challenge. With the fast progress I'm making, I can afford to take the scenic route. Smell ya later," he quipped.

He left for the pier, his stride as arrogant as his attitude. Pikachu gave a chatter that brought a small smile to Ash's face.

"Come on Pikachu...Blue might be a jerk sometimes but that's kind of crude language," chided Ash.

"Chu," the little animal replied scornfully.

The Vermillion gym was located on the waterfront overlooking the ships as they came and went. Ash signed in at the front desk and didn't have to wait long before he was met by the gym leader and ushered to the gym's battlefield.

The leaderboard off to the side displayed the two Pokémon on the battlefield, Pikachu and Raichu, together with full green lines indicating their overall strength. Special detectors in the gym floor could measure their health that way, providing an accurate manner of preventing serious injury; when the bar ran from green to yellow to a sliver of red, and finally empty, it indicated who was winning and losing the match.

Unlike the battles in Pewter and Cerulean, which had been won by luck and type advantage respectively, this was the first true challenge Ash encountered, and he realized he may have been a bit too hasty in presuming his own skill. Surge's Raichu was nimble for its size, and powerful whenever it struck. Pikachu seemed flustered and Ash found himself second-guessing his choice of moves.

"Thunder!" Ash cried.

"Flash," ordered Surge.

There was a brilliant gleam of light, and Pikachu leapt back, momentarily blinded before it could fire off its attack. It was enough for Raichu to spring, tackling Pikachu forcibly to the ground. The bar measuring Pikachu's strength shot to empty, and the leaderboard displayed Raichu as the winner.

"Very good, Raichu," said Surge, and Raichu stood upright, allowing Pikachu to shake itself off and limp free.

Ash scooped his pet up into his arms with worry. "Hey Pikachu, you okay?" he asked.

Pikachu, looking exhausted but not very injured, gave a low growl. "Pika-chuuu..."

"We'll head to the Pokémon Center. You were awesome," he said, petting the little animal.

From the Vermillion gym, Ash went straight to the Pokémon Center. He went up to the reception desk, placing Pikachu in its Poké Ball only long enough for the nurse to restore it to full health. As the restoring machine did its function and then beeped, signifying the Pokémon inside had been fully healed, Ash mulled over how the gym battle had gone and tried to figure out how he was ever going to get strong enough to beat Surge. It was an added insult somehow that it had been a Raichu to defeat them, as if it somehow ascribed legitimacy to Gary saying he should force Pikachu to evolve.

The Poké Ball was twitching as he got it back from the nurse. He immediately sent out Pikachu, which emerged with an affronted shake of its fur.

"I know you hate going in your Poké Ball, but that wasn't so bad was it?" said Ash in an assuring way.

Pikachu gave a sound somewhere between a chirp and a ffftt. Sometimes Ash wondered why Pikachu was so opposed to being carried about in its Poké Ball. Any time they'd had to go somewhere that required all Pokémon to be in their carriers – which thankfully, considering the laxity of society towards pets, was few and far between – he remembered how he had to chase Pikachu around to try and get it into its Poké Ball, an ordeal unto itself. Eventually Ash had explained to Pikachu that it was at least necessary for healing up quickly at Pokémon Centers, but it still detested it. Pikachu said it didn't like the feeling of being trapped. Ash thought it was claustrophobic.

Pikachu hopped onto his shoulder as Ash wandered over to look at the map posted on the side of the Pokémon Center lobby.

"I guess we could train some more along route 6. Meanwhile Gary's going to outpace us even further. Too bad we can't get into Saffron – those damned Rockets! – and the journey's kind of on hold unless we can beat the gym here in Vermillion..."

As he regarded the other cities on the map, he suddenly realized the folly of his supposition.

"Wait a minute. What am I saying? There's nothing that says I have to challenge them in order! And why am I going to let those Team Rocket thugs dictate whether or not I can go to Saffron City?" Besides, I already skipped the Viridian gym and will have to go back to it at some point... he thought, glancing at his Pokémon.

"What do you say, Pikachu? Do we postpone the rematch and see if we can get into Saffron from route 8?"

"Pika!" squeaked Pikachu, who was evidently happy to do whatever Ash saw fit.

"Then that's what we'll do," Ash decided. "Onward to Lavender Town!"

Globe-trotting was usually the realm of experienced trainers, not fledgling ones on their first journey to collect gym badges. To Gary's mind, however, he was certain to win his League challenge, and he had enough money to afford the excursion anyway.

The ship was going to make stops in the regions of Hoenn, Orre, and Unova, before circling round to return to Sinnoh, Johto, and Kanto. It wasn't nearly enough time in each to be a proper sampling of all they had to offer, but it was enough for a small jaunt of nearby tourist destinations, or to spend a day or so hunting region-specific species.

Of all these the least interesting to Gary was initially Orre, if only because the region lacked wild Pokémon. That said, it had other things to draw a trainer's eye; the minute he heard about the so called battling destination of Orre, Realgam Tower, it was no longer Gary's least appealing stop and instead his most awaited one. He'd spend his stay in Orre there enjoying the battles and the nightlife.

He heard that was the week of its grand opening, so Gary decided to visit.

Gary walked up to the receptionist at the check-in for the colosseum, his head held as high as if he had already won the competition. "Excuse me, I'd like to take part in the colosseum battle."

"Sorry, you just missed it. There won't be another one till tomorrow night."

"Tomorrow night?" He wouldn't be in Orre tomorrow night.

Everyone had heard of the grandeur of Orrean colosseums. Till the great stadiums in Galar had been built, Orre's had been the most magnificent in the world. The stadium here at Realgam was unique – it was a modern Orrean colosseum, designed by the financier who had built the Galarian ones. Gary had wanted very much to see it in person, from the arena, where he could show off his Pokémon. Granted he would have probably been vastly outlevelled, something he hadn't really thought of when he asked, but that was not the point.

With the colosseum closed, he decided to go see the casino located at the ground floor of Realgam Tower. That was open, to his delight.

As he walked in and took a quick glance around, he saw a familiar looking face. It was one he had seen posted around Phenac City in political advertisements: that of the mayor, Evice Cade. He was standing at the roulette table. Gary wandered over and said, "Glad to see a mayor taking interest in the businesses of his town."

"Thank you...and who might you be?"

"Gary. Gary Oak...I'm a trainer and curiosity brought me in here.

"Well Gary," replied Cade, "you saw, now leave."

Gary ignored the remark and kept talking. "Maybe if the stadium were open several more hours into the night more people would come."

"What would really attract people here would be getting to see a very rare Pokémon in a fight. Unfortunately I have no way to get a Legendary Pokémon...but I know where to find them," Cade added.

"You do?" he questioned with surprise; then, dubiously, "...why tell me?"

"You're a professional trainer, aren't you?"

The fact it had been so evident made Gary haughty. "Yeah, I am."

"Then maybe you could help me catch them." Cade spoke smoothly. "I have on good account that three Pokémon, once thought to be creatures of myth, currently run wild in the Johto region. Their names are Suicune, Raikou, and Entei."

Gary flipped out his Pokédex, bringing up the entries for each:

Suicune
Type: Water
This divine Pokémon was said to be the reincarnation of north winds. Legend states it can instantly purify filthy, murky water.

Raikou
Type: Electric
Its cry was said to sound like crashing thunder. Legend states that it carries rain clouds on its back, letting it fire thunderbolts at will.

Entei
Type: Fire
Its flames were said to be hotter than a volcano's magma. Legend states when it roars, a volcano erupts somewhere around the globe.

"Are you sure they were these Pokémon and not some others?" inquired Gary dubiously. "This reads like they haven't been seen in centuries. They don't even have a photograph on here, only an artist's rendering."

Cade was firm. "In the past few days they've been roaming around the Johto region and have already been spotted by a few people."

"The ship will be making a stop in Johto right before it returns to Kanto," Gary said contemplatively. "I could stay there and return to Kanto myself via a bird Pokémon...the two regions border each other, after all. But what makes you so sure I can find the Legendary Pokémon?"

"These creatures aren't hard to miss," assured Cade, "and I would rather take the initiative to catch them before some other ambitious trainer gets the notion to do so."

"Then why don't you go yourself?"

"My mayoral duties tend to keep me close to the Orre region. I'm willing to pay handsomely for the three Legendary Pokémon to be delivered to me."

"In all honesty," replied Gary, "what I'd really want for my trouble isn't even cash. I want a team of Pokémon strong enough to help me win against Kanto's Elite Four. I can't imagine any that would be more powerful than a Legendary Pokémon though."

"I'll find something worthwhile to trade you for them in that case," said Cade, to which Gary gave a shrug and a nod.

"If you're sure you can find something stronger...yeah, sure, I'll help you."

So when Gary left the Realgam Tower casino, it was with a skip in his step and grandiose schemes already forming as to how to catch the rare creatures.

Cade meanwhile spent the rest of the night gambling, and retired late in an upbeat mood despite having lost more than won. He had a wager still playing out: that if Gary successfully brought back the Pokémon, it would create an opportunity. The thought of how much more lucrative the new colosseum would prove was part of it, yet what Cade secretly wanted went far beyond finance.

Three legends, three families. And if Cade possessed them all, so long as there was nothing comparably stronger out there – well, then, maybe he could take his vacation to Johto early.

Chapter 5 - Mahogany Town

Mahogany Town, thought Archer with displeasure, was even smaller than Azalea.

Maybe that was not being fair to Mahogany, he reconsidered less dismissively, at least the people here were business-minded. Tourism had been the town's main income, for the adjacent Lake of Rage had once been a breeding spot for wild Gyarados, and attracted interested parties galore: fishermen, Pokémon trainers, and the curious, all of whom would stay in local lodging and eat at local restaurants and buy local chocolate called 'Rage-candybars'. Overhunting eventually decimated the regional Gyarados population, and consequently visitors to Mahogany, yet the townsfolk still straggled along with their small businesses in the frail hopes of a revival. Nowadays all there was in that lake were Magikarp and they were usually snapped up before they could ever evolve.

Their base of operations in town was a small shop nestled between shade trees and along Main Street. The former proprietor had owed Team Rocket a debt for some favor and had quite intelligently, without any need for persuasion, bartered ownership of his store as repayment.

The business sold foodstuffs and was the town's only grocery store. This meant it turned a profit, to the pleasant surprise of Rocket Enterprises. The most peculiar thing about the store was the cellar, which from what the former shopkeeper told them had once been a ninja hideout. Archer did not know if he believed the story about ninjas, however the cellar was secluded and cozy and could easily be repurposed into a hideout for Team Rocket.

Two Persian statues of white marble stood at the foyer, the forehead jewel hiding a miniature security camera that alerted them to any intruders. The cameras were a formality, like having a smoke detector; except for a police raid perhaps – and they had connections to warn them of that occurrence – the idea of intruders upon a Team Rocket fortress was ludicrous. No one was that stupid, thought Archer with a contented smirk.

Archer met Dr. Ethan Colress at the grocery store's upper level and descended to the cellar with him, past the foyer, to a laboratory area.

Dr. Colress was slim, with amber eyes framed by rectangular eyeglasses, and neat blond hair bearing a single streak of blue. He had worked for Team Plasma during the infamous Plasma War in the Unova region, and nowadays was officially a government scientist, but he moonlighted for Team Rocket to further, as he put it, "the valuable interests of Science." He and Giovanni got along well; Giovanni funded his research but allowed him to conduct experiments as he saw fit, so long as he gave him updates on the progress, which was much the same arrangement Colress had with his previous benefactor during wartime.

The scientist headed the genetic project Giovanni had been financing. The crux of their research was the effects of radio waves on the genome, to find a way to alter it to increase power and breed the world's strongest Pokémon. They drew on previous research the scientist had done, and had studied the effects of Galarian dyna-max radiation from special minerals. Discoveries in the Hoenn region had drawn their attention most recently to extinct species.

"Lately we'd been cross-breeding Rotom with Psyduck and prehistoric Pokémon cloned from fossils," explained Colress.

"And how's that going?" asked Archer, who didn't give a damn.

"Experiments have resulted in these."

'These' turned out to be flightless bird Pokémon, with blocky plumage and the blank stares of Psyduck. Colress had a flock of them, and they all evidently had decided they liked to stare at Archer – something Archer found unnerving.

"What the hell are they?"

"We call them Porygons."

"Are they even breathing?"

"They only have to breathe once every half-hour. They're hardy but, alas, not nearly as powerful as we'd hoped. Giovanni is considering selling some of them to the Space Center for use in their intergalactic exploration program, or give them out as prizes in the casinos."

Maybe as a novelty, but they look kind of useless. Archer let temptation get the better of him and decided to poke one of the Porygon. He jumped back suddenly when it responded with a static shock and a displeased chirp.

"Now Joe, one musn't immediately attack," Colress scolded the bird.

Archer rubbed his sore hand sourly. "What was it you needed?"

"We've isolated a wavelength that affects the gene responsible for inducing evolution in most Pokémon. We plan to try broadcasting it and see what happens."

"Do it."

"We are uncertain what will happen, so just in case we get the townspeople irate, having a large number of Team Rocket guards here helps."

"So you'd basically like us to stand by in case the villagers show up with pitchforks and torches."

"Precisely. Off-topic you'd better tell your people not to pester the Porygon. They're irritable before they've had their coffee."

"You're feeding these birds coffee?"

"We're seeing how the caffeine affects them. They do seem to love the taste of coffee though."

"So I take it you named them after coffee?"

"Oh no. Joe is short for Joseph, after the brilliant physicist who discovered..."

"I shouldn't have asked. Look, we'll get our guards stationed as soon as humanly possible so you can get back to your work."

They shook hands and Archer walked back upstairs leaving the scientist to his studies.

At least their job here was straightforward, even seemingly easy. What Archer had not accounted for was how idiotic the minions could get when faced with monotony.

Case in point one mid-morning when one such subordinate made an exceptional observation.

"Do you realize we're living off of trees shitting?"

Archer turned to them with a double-take. "What?"

"No really. Think about it. Plants absorb carbon dioxide, right?"

"Yes."

"And then they release oxgyen, which we breathe in, right?"

"Yes..."

"We're living off of trees shitting."

Archer decided right then and there he was fed up with listening to this morning's philosophical conversation and decided to slink off. Even listening to Kris try to convince him to let her into Team Rocket was better; at least she could hold logical conversations, even if she was hell-bent on joining the gang.

But who didn’t have an ulterior motive? figured Archer.

He left the store and wandered out to route 42, a tranquil path crisscrossed by rivers and creeks beneath the imposing shadow of Mount Mortar. This route kept a nice balance between untamed and pruned, with a wide trail beside grassy fields dotted by bushes, and lush trees beyond that grew gradually closer together till they stretched naturally off into the distance, while the singing of Taillow and Pidgey lent a peaceful soundtrack. The morning sun warmed the climate, and outlined the weaving rivers with light.

If one continued down the path, it would eventually lead to Ecruteak, but Archer had no intention to go that far. He was about to turn back when he heard a rustle in the bracken.

There was an apple orchard beyond the hedgerows and it attracted all varieties of wild Pokémon. Curious at how large this had sounded, he pushed through the bushes and discovered a small sunlit clearing.

Archer found Kris sitting under the trees, her pet Eevee curled up on her lap, and a cluster of apples she had picked beside her.

There was also the Suicune. She was feeding said Suicune the apples.

Kris, sensing someone, glanced up. "Oh hi Archer."

"What do you have here?" he remarked.

"Apples. Want some?"

He was still staring incredulously at the Legendary Pokémon hanging out like if it had been invited to a picnic. Kris offered a matter-of-fact explanation:

"Suicune likes me."

"Or it likes apples," observed Archer.

"That could be part of it," she admitted.

Suicune gave a happy little cry and, seizing another apple, dashed past Archer. "You haven't caught it with a Poké Ball then?"

"No I've been letting Suicune do its own thing. Do you think I should?"

"Oh, please do," said Archer flatly, "the sooner the better."

Kris collected the remaining apples in her bag and stood up. "I'm visiting Mahogany Town to challenge the gym. Do you know where it is?"

"Straight across from the Pokémon Center. You can't miss it."

"Thanks! Come on, Eevee," she remarked to her Pokémon, which scampered happily after her.

"Take Aspear berries in case of frostbite," Archer shouted after her, "they specialize in ice types."

Pryce was the gym leader of Mahogany and a friend of the Delavitas. He did not care that Team Rocket would be in town or what they would be up to and if anything they had his blessing. He had been on good terms with the family for many years and always repaid his debts. Most recently it helped that his granddaughter Lorelei had been promoted to be a member of the Elite Four, upon Giovanni's recommendation. Payments were in order, but gratitude was priceless.

So Archer did not expect him that afternoon, hemming and hawing as if he was uncertain about how his words should be received, and it was only with some prompting that the gym leader finally spoke his mind.

"You remember how there were only Magikarp in the Lake of Rage?" asked Pryce.

"Yes."

"Well lately they started evolving."

"Colress will be happy to hear that."

"I'm not sure if you're aware, Gyarados have a hierarchy. Because they all evolved at once they all want to claim the lake territory and become alpha."

"So?"

"They started fighting each other. So now we've got a lake full of Gyarados shooting Hyper Beams at each other. They seem to get particularly agitated when they hear that radio tune you guys are broadcasting."

"And you're here to plead for us to stop airing it."

"Plead? I'm here to thank you on behalf of all Mahogany. We've got tourists by the busload coming in to see the Gyarados rampage. The town is raking in more money than ever before. Any way you can crank up the modulation on that radio transmitter of yours and get 'em extra angry?"

Archer decided to go to the Lake of Rage and see what all the fuss was about. He'd heard tell of the wild Gyarados fighting by a fair number of people now but he hadn't witnessed the scene for himself, having had no interest till now. He saw little difference between wild Pokémon battles and League sporting ones, save for the absence of strength gauges and statistic measures that made it easier to follow the tide of the fight. There was not even the drama of expectation; wild Pokémon did not fight to the death over territory, just as League matches were never carried to the point of serious injury.

The adjoining route had two pathways to the lake. One was wild with tall grass and foliage, and was usually only traversed by trainers hunting for Pokémon. The other was a clear, wide trail of trimmed grass, which was a straight walk to the lakeshore, and which was accessed through a gatehouse that Team Rocket had shrewdly decided to overtake as a toll-booth. Team Rocket members were of course exempt from the toll, so Archer opted for the clear path; meeting up with territorial wild Pokémon while walking through the tall grass was a waste of valuable time.

He walked in to find Kris chatting with the Team Rocket guard. Her Eevee was perched on the guard's desk, and gave an alerting cry when it saw Archer approach.

"...so no matter who wins, it's a win-win. Hi Archer," she greeted.

Archer tipped his head but kept walking. "Buongiorno, Kris."

He had gone but a few pace before a second thought made him spin on his heel. "What the hell are you doing?"

"We got a bet going," explained Kris seriously.

The guard corroborated, "We're gonna ask the first pedestrian who walks through here a question, and based on their answer one of us wins."

"Wins what?"

"If she wins she doesn't have to pay the toll, and she takes my post here for the rest of the day."

"So I can show off how useful I can be to Team Rocket," explained Kris.

"...and if you win?" Archer glanced skeptically back to the guard.

"If I win she has to pay the toll, and she takes my post here for the week."

"Stop trying to shirk your duties, Wyatt," snapped Archer.

"Hold on," exclaimed Kris, "you're the first pedestrian! That means you get to answer our question."

Archer crossed his arms expectantly and stared at her, and Kris asked:

"Is an Eevee part of the cat family, or the dog family?"

She held out the little Pokémon, which squeaked.

Archer stared first at the Eevee, then at the two gamblers, and finally scowled, "What kind of stupidity is this? Everyone can see it's got the ears of a rabbit. You." He pointed at Kris and motioned. "Come with me."

"But what about the toll?" insisted the guard.

"Forget the damn toll. She's an honorary member of Team Rocket anyway, considering how we can't shake her off," replied a resigned Archer.

This made Kris' eyes light up enormously and as she hurried after Archer, she asked cheerily, "Are you going to see the Gyarados rampage too?"

"No. I'm going to see all the idiot tourists to decide how to capitalize on them."

When they got to the lakeshore Archer was unsurprised to find the small crowd milling at the water's edge, most gazing out to the center of the lake, a few picnicking on the grass, and several taking photographs. What he didn't expect was how far away the Gyarados were. Salesmen were hawking binoculars so people could get a better look at the powerful Pokémon fighting in the distance.

Archer shook his head incredulously. I was right, of course. Watching League matches on television is better. At least they give close-ups.

Kris was holding the Eevee over her head. "Can you see them, Eevee?"

The Eevee squeaked.

"All right Kris," decided Archer, "I've got another test for you if you want to join Team Rocket. Considering the results of the first one in Ecruteak weren't certain."

"I found three Legendary Pokémon," she pointed out.

"You also fell in a hole."

"Okay," she conceded. "What's the challenge?"

"Catch a Gyarados and bring it to the town grocery store. The store is owned by Rocket Enterprises so we'll be there. Here are some Poké Balls...they're all registered to me, so the Pokémon you catch with them belongs to us. Capice?"

That oughta keep her busy for a while, he figured, seeing her sprint away with the Eevee at her heels.

It was approaching dinnertime when Kris showed up at the grocery store.

"I caught a Gyarados," she announced happily, holding out the Poké Ball.

"Oh, er, thanks." Archer took the Poké Ball half-heartedly. Damn, I thought that would have kept her away longer.

"To tell you the truth it looks kind of ill," she admitted, as if having read his mind. "Maybe that's why it was so easy to catch."

"Ill in what way?"

"It's red."

"It's red?" Archer's eyes opened wide.

One of the cadets chimed in obliviously, "Maybe it's got high blood pressure?"

Archer turned to him with incredulous ire. "You idiot, don't you realize that a red Gyarados is worth a fortune? What does Giovanni pay you for?"

"So can I join Team Rocket?" Kris prompted.

"I'll think about it."

"No fair! I brought you a Gyarados."

"In Team Rocket, we're only fair when it's profitable," answered Archer. "First lesson for you. However, you're showing promise."

He had a small good-natured smile on his face nonetheless, and Kris, far from being dissuaded, returned a similarly sly smile as she left the grocery store. Glancing over to the windows, Archer noticed how both their images reflected on the glass, and he blinked with perplexity.

My...we do look similar, don't we?

Chapter 6 - Ghosts of Lavender

Field work was something James, Jessie, and Meowth had not done in a while, being mostly Giovanni's personal guard and top enforcers. So when the trio were sent by Giovanni to briefly take over management of Team Rocket's smuggling operations, they saw it as a surprising but not unwelcome change of pace.

Lavender Town was small and peaceful, a forested hamlet in a mountain cove, and would have been considered an ideal dwelling place were it not for the tremendous reverence everybody held towards it as a harbour of the spiritual. Some people did not wish to live there for fear of the ghosts said to haunt it.

Team Rocket did not mind ghosts – which in any case were mostly ghost type Pokémon, live creatures able to take the form of energy at will. They minded their business, which was more than could often be said for beings of flesh and blood.

Jessie, James, and Meowth had a group of about twenty or so lower rank agents under their supervision to aid with transporting stolen Pokémon. A semi-abandoned warehouse on the town outskirts served as a relay point for Team Rocket's activities, which went uneventfully till one of these subordinates walked in with a small cage.

He was fairly young, with green hair and eyes of a matching shade; they knew him as Krieger, a recruit who had been with the syndicate for roughly a year. Relentlessly tagging after him was a puppy Pokémon called a Poochyena, which he always seemed to ignore.

"That doesn't look like one of the animals we've been moving," Jessie observed the cage with interest.

"I trapped it out on route 10," explained Krieger haughtily.

The trio crowded around the cage dubiously. Meanwhile the young Pokémon inside huddled as far from them as it could, looking both frightened and dismal. It was a small brown creature with a horny covering that masked its face.

James voiced their unanimous thought. "This Cubone barely looks weaned."

"There was a Marowak too," said Krieger.

"A Marowak?" All three immediately lifted their heads with interest. These were the evolved form of Cubone and scarce.

"Yeah, it might've been the parent of this Cubone."

"Marowak fetch a high price," noted Jessie.

"And it's a ground type," James added, "I bet the boss would be thrilled to get one for his gym."

"Mrreow! Where's the Pokémon?" yowled Meowth.

Krieger gave a derisive laugh and said, "The damn thing wouldn't let me take its cub so I left it for dead. It's probably carrion for the Fearow now!"

He faltered when Jessie's eyes suddenly flashed with infuriated blue fire, and he could not step back before she struck out with the whip, lashing across his face and making him gasp.

"You idiot!" she nearly hissed, "Killing rare Pokémon, for no reason, when you could have caught it instead! What's the matter with you?"

Even Meowth let out an angered growl, and James, though similarly displeased, tried to mollify the situation. "Now Jessie, let's not get carried away yet. If he left it for dead, then it might still be alive, right?"

"Go back and get that Pokémon, and you'd better hope it's alive!" snapped Jessie.

Meowth punctuated Jessie's words with a hiss, and the visibly shaken minion dipped his head and left.

They did not think much of the incident after that, though James kept eyeing the Cubone's cage and complaining the infant creature would die without its parent, with Jessie responding they would bottle-feed it if it came to that – no thanks to their stupid minion, making more work for them.

Meowth meanwhile was pensive about the whole matter. He seemed to be analysing something, but did not care to discuss it with anyone, and lingered around their other subordinates watchfully.

James and Jessie let their own Pokémon out for feeding time. Jessie's violet cobra Arbok and James' buoyantly spherical Weezing were both poison types, raised to a moderately high level; they were milling about their food when Krieger and his Poochyena returned. Jessie stepped away to speak to him and came back shortly.

"The Marowak's gone," she announced flatly.

"It died?" James asked with disappointment.

No," said Jessie with frustration, "it's gone. Some Pokémon trainer passing by apparently picked it up."

"We're having a stroke of bad luck lately, aren't we," James sighed.

Meowth now wandered over, his tail lashing. "There's a fight brewing. You guys should take a look."

Before either of them could respond, there was a commotion in the adjoining room. They hurried over to find their subordinates all standing around in a wide ring, watching two other minions in a fist fight.

One, they realized, was Krieger. He had evidently placed Poochyena in its Poké Ball, perhaps refusing to accept a loss in an earlier Pokémon battle over some dispute and feeling he could beat his opponent personally. Jessie clapped her hands twice. "Arbok, break them up!"

At her signal, the large snake struck out and separated the two men, baring its long fangs menacingly as if it planned to bite the first one who moved. They backed away fearfully.

"All right," James demanded, "what was that about?"

"He's talking treason," said the first.

"You liar," Krieger countered.

One of the spectators jumped in, "I heard what he said... he said someone else might be a better leader than Giovanni. He also said he wasn't the only person in Team Rocket who thought that way and they were going to do something about it."

Jessie turned back evenly to Krieger. "Well, Krieger – is that true?"

He stumbled over his words, unable to articulate any coherent excuse. He was trapped, and in sudden panic decided to make a break for it by whipping out a revolver he had hidden.

Arbok and Weezing tensed to attack but James lifted a hand, and they held back.

Jessie, James, and Meowth observed Krieger coldly. The rest of their minions all lingered about like kittens eager to watch how full-grown wildcats dispatched prey, and seemed perplexed at their present restraint.

This was a surprise to Krieger too, but he was not about to question it. Perhaps in hindsight he should have.

"Do you really think you'll get away from Team Rocket?" Jessie posed mildly.

"You think you're all that?" Krieger gloated. "I'm forcing you to accept credit."

James responded with calculated tranquillity. "We're accepting your credit because we intend to collect with interest."

Meowth punctuated this with a hiss.

Without stopping to consider the implication of those words, Krieger raced out the door.

Shadows of looming nightfall stretched mournfully across the lonely streets of Lavender, like the foreboding of coming peril. Of course peril was a matter of perspective; it depended on who wielded it.

Jessie, James, and Meowth, in full uniform, had tracked Krieger all the way to the seedier side of town. Whereas the streets at this hour were quiet as death, the tavern was alive with the warmth of boisterous people and vibrant music.

No sooner did they step into the establishment that they noticed a familiar face rise from a table and dart inconspicuously to the back of the tavern, disappearing through a panelled wood door.

"He's escaping out the back," muttered James.

Meowth growled, yet with excitement rather than anger. "I've prowled around these parts before. I haven't found any opening in the back. The prey just trapped itself."

"We've got him just where we want him," Jessie replied, mischief in her eyes as she strode dramatically up to the bartender, faced the room and slammed her hand on the counter.

"Drinks on us throughout the night!" Jessie announced, to a hearty shout of delight from all there.

James had a smile. "I'm sorry Jessie, why are we doing this again?"

"Because the drunks will be too happy to care what happens in the back room," she replied wryly.

"This is why I like you guys," purred Meowth, "you think like cats."

With a blatant skip in her step Jessie went ahead, followed by Meowth prancing with tail held high. James lingered near the counter and handed the bartender several bills of rolled cash.

"This," explained James, "is for silence – and for the band to play all night as loud as they want. We'll make sure your tavern gets reimbursed for the rest."

"Not a problem," said the bartender, though he stammered a little nervously as he took the bills, "We got no problem with Team Rocket."

"To your health," James toasted slyly and, procuring a rose from the vase adjacent to the counter, stepped quickly after his companions.

The back of the tavern was a suitably abandoned place. A short flight of steps descended to a windowless storage cellar full of crates holding beers and wines, a wood table atop which was some kind of radio system, and a couple of chairs, but nothing more; perfectly isolated for the Team Rocket trio to hold their unexpected prisoner.

And he had gone there himself, the fool, thought James.

They found Krieger at the table, talking through the radio – or trying to. He adjusted the knobs on the antiquated device, trying to get a signal. "Hello...? This is number 27. You hear me?"

Beside him on the floor, Poochyena started yapping upon seeing the couple posed at the top of the steps. Meowth bounded soundlessly onto one of the crates and slipped up to the rafters.

"Shut up you mutt," growled Krieger, without caring to look over, "I can't hear!"

Poochyena only yapped louder.

"Buonasera," greeted James succinctly.

It made Krieger turn around in shock.

From the rafters, there came a caterwaul and a rush of cream fur; Meowth landed on Krieger's head, as if he were ambushing a Raticate, and sank his claws in.

A yelp arose, not from Poochyena but from Krieger, who nearly toppled out of the chair and, hurling the cat off him, tried to get to his feet only to be tripped by the pull of Jessie's whip. He crashed onto his back, and as James and Jessie towered over him, Poochyena was yapping frantically in the back with Meowth hissing.

"What's with this dog?" chided Meowth. "We're not gonna hurt you. When's the last time he fed you anyway? You look scrawny. Hey guys..." he turned to his friends, "we got some food for the dog?"

Poochyena stopped yapping in sudden astonishment and began wagging its tail.

"Traitor," Krieger seethed at the dog.

"Hypocrite," retorted Jessie, pulling his attention back to them.

"The boss doesn't take kindly to betrayal," added James, his green eyes as sharp as thorns. He held the rose in a showy fashion adding, "It's the worst of crimes. ...We've come to collect our interest."

Using a videophone, Jessie, James, and Meowth contacted Giovanni. When the trio told him what had transpired with Krieger and how they now held him prisoner, Giovanni listened without reaction, and only when they finished the whole story did he comment:

"And?"

"We wanted to know if you had special orders," said James.

"You know what to do," replied Giovanni, retrieving a long-stemmed rose from somewhere off-screen and turning back to the trio. "Find out how many other traitors there are within our ranks. Find out who their leader is." As he spoke, he picked the leaves, pointedly, from the rose stem one by one. His eyes never left the screen, and his voice remained pleasant.

"Afterwards... mandagli i miei saluti."

And with that he hung up.

The two elite agents and the cat all looked at each other, bearing nothing more than nonchalance.

"What time is it, James?" asked Jessie.

James glanced at the time on his transceiver. "Almost midnight."

Jessie sighed with boredom. "Let's see how long this takes."

If it had been an hour, it was a day; if it had been a day, it was a week.

Time took on agonising qualities. Maybe they would've secretly enjoyed beating him up, if only for how much of a disrespectful braggart he was, were it not for the fact they all wanted to be elsewhere. That was the problem with Giovanni ordering them to get information from someone. When the person wasn't reasonable it dragged on...and on... Though in all fairness it probably dragged on more for the victim, but that was kind of the point.

Meowth had led the Poochyena up from the cellar to the bartender, who had been instructed to feed the hungry creature. The bartender, of course, complied immediately. The cat had then returned.

"They still out there drinking away the night?" asked James as the cat hopped onto the table.

"Are you kidding? They'll be out there till dawn," purred Meowth. "A few of them have already burst into song."

"Good," said James.

Jessie meanwhile was standing directly in front of Krieger. They had tied him with rope to one of the chairs. "Is this what you used to shoot the Marowak?" she asked, examining the revolver she had taken from him.

He did not answer.

"Team Rocket only rarely issues handguns to our agents, and never to low-rank rookies," she continued. "The same person who gave you this, is the one you were trying to contact with the radio. Isn't that right?"

"Fuck you," retorted Krieger, finally opening his mouth only to say the wrong thing. James and Jessie exchanged a dubious glance.

"Cocky, isn't he?" Jessie placed the revolver aside on the table. "Considering it's not like anyone will be able to find him here."

"Now Jessie," James pacified, "Maybe we should give him one more chance."

"I think we're wasting our time," scowled Jessie.

"Well, probably," conceded James, "but...what's it going to hurt us?"

Jessie seemed to give in. "Okay."

She grabbed the revolver again and held Krieger at gunpoint, the cold muzzle straight against his skin, in between his eyes.

"Be honest and we'll be merciful."

Krieger remained smug. "Shoot, bitch. I'm not saying a word."

"I don't think you quite understood," Jessie replied, and swung savagely around, slamming him hard across the face with the heavy metal of the handgun.

If it had been a week, it was a month; if it had been a month, it was a year.

James was leaving most of the interrogation to Jessie, for now. The traitor Krieger apparently never realized the kind of temper Jessie had, and was only now discovering the ferocity that had both propelled her to high-rank and which James never ceased to admire. His proud refusal to answer her inquiries was only making it worse for him.

Jessie held the whip from her belt taut. "Well...?" she prompted, stepping around him.

"I'm not telling you shit!" Krieger countered defiantly.

She looped the whip around his throat.

Strangulation had effects not fully appreciable by the onlooker. It centered in a pressure in his head and lungs alongside panic, Krieger's perception fading swiftly for the rising whistle of blood pressure in his ears. He writhed in desperation but the restraints held firm, his chest heaving for breath uselessly, to all of which Jessie only gripped the scourge tighter and pulled it back against his neck like a garrote.

"Talk, damn it!" she ordered.

James looked bored, though he couldn't help a little smile. "Jessie," he said easily, "not to interrupt your fun, darling, but the guy can't talk if he can't breathe."

She appeared to consider this for a moment before letting the lash slacken, releasing him. "You're right. It's counterintuitive."

Krieger coughed and gasped for precious air. He was still struggling for breath when she lifted his head by the chin to face her.

"Cat got your tongue?" asked Jessie delicately.

Before Krieger could think up a good retort, Meowth had appeared on his shoulder. "Not yet," he purred, his eyes squinted.

Krieger licked his lips once, unconsciously, with the first shiver of fear.

If it had been a year, it was a decade; if it had been a decade, it was a century.

And Krieger still held fast.

James, tired of the whole charade, had procured one of the beer bottles from the crates.

"You need a drink already?" Jessie asked. She herself looked frustrated. "Actually that's a good idea. Give me one of those so we can pour it over this guy's head. No, wait; that'd be a waste of beer."

"These are one of those limited edition bottle-caps," James said appreciatively. "I don't think I have one of these."

Jessie eyed him skeptically. "Despite all the time we've been together, I still don't get why you collect bottle caps."

"I like them," was James' easy explanation, and he turned to her. "Honey, do you know where there's an opener around here?"

Jessie found it cute that he was interested in collecting bottle caps, one of the many things she liked about him. She handed him an opener before turning back to their captive with a vicious glare.

"All right, dimwit. Realized the futility of your refusal yet? You know we can only make this worse."

"Much worse," added Meowth with a snarl.

Bruised and bleeding as he was, Krieger's response was still to laugh in their faces.

Jessie and Meowth considered this and turned to James, who was tugging at the bottle of beer. It took a moment for him to have a double-take.

"No Jessie... I took care of the last one," James said.

"The last time we had this problem, you made the guy talk," insisted Jessie.

"The last time I did that," James countered, "it was such a mess we needed to put in a request for new uniforms because even bleach wouldn't work."

"But you're much better at it than I am sweetheart."

"Jess, we both have the same training... maybe Meowth should have a turn." Throughout the conversation, James was still struggling with the beer bottle.

He succeeded in opening the drink to the accompanying sound of a pop and fizz. The other two exchanged a displeased look. Krieger was just staring at them all, listening to them talk with unfolding horror.

Jessie smiled. "Oh sweetie, you're worried for no reason. So what if last time was messy? It's not like anyone will hear him over the ruckus they're making in the bar. And as I said, you have a natural talent with such basics."

"Yeah," Meowth added a yowl, "You're more sophisticated at this than we, so it falls on you."

"Sophisticated," James scowled with disgust. "There's nothing sophisticated about pain, really. You can inflict it with practically anything."

Jessie's blue eyes narrowed in daring. "Mess or no mess, if you don't, I will."

James sighed. He glanced at their prisoner as if appraisingly, then said simply:

"Bring me a towel and ice cubes. Oh, and a hammer."

"Wait," Krieger jumped fearfully, "Please...have mercy! Yes, I was approached to help overthrow Giovanni. There are many of us among Team Rocket's rank-and-file; no one else in your squadron, but there are over thirty of us across Kanto and Johto. We receive our orders through encrypted radio."

"Orders from whom?" James asked placidly.

"A rival syndicate based out of Orre. They call themselves Cipher."

"Who's in charge?" said James.

A moment of gleeful superiority flickered in Krieger's eyes. "That's what everyone wants to know."

"Lucky for us, we have you to put us up to speed."

When he did not reply, James turned casually back to Jessie— "Jessie can you get those things I needed...?" —prompting a return of terrified prescience to their captive. "Look, the head of Cipher is Mr. Rose, all right?"

This drew their attention fast. "Mr. Linford Rose? The former owner of Macro Cosmos?"

"Yes."

"And I guess he told your little group of renegades to steal the Charizard from headquarters?" Jessie leapt in, following the trail to its logical conclusion.

"We were given orders to get the Charizard if we could," he relented, "but the orders weren't given directly by Rose."

James and Jessie both exchanged a glance. They had heard nothing about a rival organization, and the last they knew about Mr. Rose was that he'd fled to Orre, coerced by Giovanni to sell his company holdings for safe passage there – but nothing since.

Krieger was still insisting, "Rose is the leader of Cipher, but he's not who I get my orders from....I swear I don't know who gives the orders! I've told you everything, so please...don't do it!"

"Don't do what?" James asked.

"Whatever it was you were going to do with those things."

James blinked, as if mystified. "I just wanted to crush ice for my drink."

Jessie's smile was turning into a grin, and Meowth was purring loudly and coiling his tail. It took a moment for Krieger to realize the whole thing had been an elaborately preconceived trick.

"Oh shit," Krieger muttered, and sank deeper into the chair.

Jessie kissed her companion's lips lightly. "I tell you James, you've got a way."

"How long have we been here?" James asked himself, and the three of them crowded around his transceiver for the time.

"It's only been...thirty minutes. What the fuck." Jessie turned to the others casually. "Anyway are we all satisfied here?"

"I think we're good," said James, giving a little shrug.

Meowth yawned. "Yeah, I wanna get home already."

In less than a blink of an eye Jessie snatched up the revolver from the table. Mercy had the speed of a gunshot – if it had been a minute, it was a second; if it was a second, it was merely a heartbeat.

Ash heard the shot, echoing clear against the alley's brick walls, however he was not sure at first what it was he had heard.

Saffron City was still inaccessible thanks to the unofficial toll, so Ash's intended detour to Lavender Town would ideally provide access to Saffron through an alternate road – that of route 8.

It was the principle of the thing. If he hoped to get eight badges to challenge the Elite Four, he needed to traverse these gatehouses, yet the idea of paying the notorious mafia syndicate a fee for use of the public road was so distasteful to him that he would rather seek out an unorthodox way through even if it put him back a couple of days.

The road from Vermillion to Lavender, and consequently to Saffron, was an ostensibly straight path. Still, it was one of the longest treks he had yet taken, two day's travel that stretched across grassy trails and down several boardwalks overlooking a seaside vista.

At least the weather was good and they spied several varieties of wild Pokémon. There were so many that Ash briefly entertained the idea of eschewing his planned solo-run of the Elite Four to catch some, but he was in quite a hurry to get to his destination and so, for that matter, was Pikachu. They therefore tried to skirt any battles along the way, which was probably inadvisable considering any gained experience would be helpful for the gym matches.

Ash eventually reached Lavender Town and got a room at the Pokémon Center's lodge to spend the night. It was there that he overheard two trainers discussing a wild Marowak they brought to the Pokémon Center after finding it had been injured from a gunshot.

"It was shot?" Ash had exclaimed. Considering Marowak were such rare Pokémon as it was, the idea was outrageous. "Who would do such a thing?"

The other trainers hadn't wanted to say at first, but he coaxed the information from them eventually. "I saw them fleeing. They were wearing a Team Rocket uniform."

Of course, thought Ash, it had to be Team Rocket. And when he retired to sleep he was still fuming about the organization and their callous disregard towards Pokémon wellbeing.

The unpleasant thought of that cruelty, however, kept Ash awake. He lay in bed mulling over Team Rocket, and it was about five past midnight when Pikachu gave a small squeak from where it was curled up beside him.

"You can't get to sleep either, huh Pikachu?"

"Pika," replied the little animal. Ash petted it on the head.

"Yeah," Ash agreed, "I keep thinking about that hurt Marowak too."

Pikachu gave a squeaky growl and stretched.

Ash reflected on it. "Maybe a nighttime stroll would help us both," he decided.

That was how Ash was compelled out into the night. Pikachu scampered along at his heels and followed Ash all the way to the side street with the tavern.

It was not the safest part of town, let alone walking down that dark alley like if it were Lavender's main street, but Pikachu was sufficient protection. What he did not expect was noise like a firecracker, or for a narrow portion of the tavern's back wall to give way readily as he leant against one of the bricks.

Against his better judgement, Ash examined the short passageway he had uncovered, walking into the warehouse room in time to see James tossing a rose to a slumped figure, Jessie remarking something about how tedious their night's work had been, and Meowth lifting his ears at Ash's presence and give an alerting mew to the two humans.

When Ash realized what the scene before him was, he froze. When their attention shot towards him, his breath caught short.

Instead of the civilian clothes he had first seen them in, now they wore their full uniforms, brazen white with accented black patent-leather. It was oddly impressive; the same halting kind of awe at seeing a dangerous jungle beast at arm's length, poised to pounce. Somehow too Ash had never imagined they were high-rank.

James shot an accusatory look towards Meowth. "I thought you said there was no other entrance!"

Meowth flattened his ears. "Hey what're you looking at me for? How was I supposed to know there was a secret passage?"

Ash blinked in surprise. "Did...did your Meowth just talk?"

Jessie frowned at him. "Listen twerp, this is Team Rocket business; stay out of it."

To this, Ash was taken by ill-advised indignation. "Like trying to kill that Marowak still recovering at the Pokémon Center? Stealing its cub? Now you've moved to people; you're making progress."

The instant he blurted this out, he realized he shouldn't have. Even Pikachu gave him a disapproving look.

"I think you've seen a little too much here," Jessie added calmly, taking a step forward as Ash took a step back. "You'd better prepare for trouble."

"Make that double," James chimed in, right beside her.

"That's right!" hissed Meowth, taking a huge leap towards Ash's eyes.

Ash ducked, and the cat succeeded only in knocking his cap off his head; Pikachu instantly leapt to defend his trainer, tackling Meowth backwards, and they ended up in a ball of screeching, flying fur.

"Get him, Arbok!" ordered Jessie, throwing a Poké Ball.

"Go, Weezing!" added James.

The three animals instantly surrounded Ash, with defiant little Pikachu trapped in the center. Jessie and James both laughed loudly at the sight of this seemingly evident futility.

"You really think you can take us on with one Pokémon?" mocked Jessie.

Whether Ash thought he could, or could not, was soon irrelevant. Pikachu bounded straight up, and in one sudden electrical shock threw them all against the wall, even farther back than the day they first met at the Cerulean Pokémon Center. Wood crates crashed to the floor accompanied by the piercing sound of shattered glass, and beer poured out.

Arbok and Weezing had been knocked out in a single blast of electricity. Only Meowth remained, standing unsteadily with a sliver of strength. "Me...owww..."

"That Pikachu is no ordinary Pikachu," marvelled James.

They were still angry, but at the same time they now appeared curious. It was strangely more unnerving to Ash than if they had been completely filled with rage.

"Maybe we've been hasty," Jessie set forth. "Would you like to join Team Rocket?"

Ash just stared at them, astounded. "...I'll think about it," he replied, too incredulous to utter anything else.

"Well then, get outta here before we change our minds," said James.

He wasn't about to argue the point. Ash picked up his cap from the floor and ran out of there as fast as his legs could carry him, with Pikachu at his heels.

"Wonder how that Pikachu got so strong?" asked Jessie.

James shrugged his shoulders, "Let's us hurry back to the boss, Jess, before we attract any more unwanted attention."

The trio exited the building and was soon lost in the shadows.

Delia was in her dining room setting the table when her son Ash called her on the phone.

"Hey Mom!" he greeted her enthusiastically.

"Hello my boy!" his mother said as she balanced the phone to one ear and simultaneously placed a plate of food at the table, "How have you been?"

"Okay," he said simply, "but I've had some tense moments...I crossed paths with the Rocket people a couple of times."

"You've had run-ins with Team Rocket?" There was sudden pallor on her face.

"You don't know the half of it," Ash said, though he did not sound very concerned at all, "I walked into a storage area and I found them with someone who was badly injured...maybe dead. Anyway, they told me to get out of there so I did."

"Ash, I'd prefer it if you stayed clear of them." Delia spoke with urgency bordering upon desperation. "There's something you don't know."

"Like what?" he asked.

Briefly, she hesitated, as if weighing an admission or lack thereof. At last she just said, "Never mind."

"Don't worry about me Mom," Ash assured. "Anyway, Pikachu and I have got to get going if we want to reach Saffron by nightfall. We've already got two badges already...just six more left to go. I'll talk to you soon, bye!"

He hung up and Delia sat down at the table to her dinner, but she felt as if her appetite was waning.

She sighed and whispered to herself, "I need to tell him."

Chapter 7 - Voyage to the Isles

Having received word from Team Rocket headquarters about the supposedly 'most powerful Pokémon of all' being sighted somewhere about the Sevii Islands, an archipelago located in the oceans between Johto and Kanto, Archer set out immediately with the troop of cadets. This was a top priority and, at least as the minions saw it, an all-expenses-paid trip to the Johtonian seashore.

The latter view annoyed Archer. To his businesslike sensibilities, which still felt aggrieved at any damage their image had suffered at Azalea, they had no time for frivolity. If they had, it would be after they had caught the Legendary Pokémon – not before.

"This isn't a vacation," he snapped, seeing how they all jostled to buy trinkets when they came to an open-air flea market. "It's a business trip. We catch the Pokémon, bring it to Giovanni, and then maybe we can return home to the Kanto region." He was feeling nostalgic – nostalgia, was that the right word? – for Celadon City. Johto, for all its prettiness and admirable qualities, did not hold the same personal connection to him as the cities of Kanto.

In the middle of his lecturing Archer was approached by someone familiar.

Archer sighed. "Hi Kris. You're in Olivine too, I see?"

Kris was straightforward. "I need to get to Cianwood so I can challenge the Olivine gym."

"You mean get to Cianwood to challenge the Cianwood gym," Archer corrected.

"Do they have a gym in Cianwood too?" she asked blankly.

Against his better judgment, Archer ventured, "Why would you need to go to Cianwood to challenge Olivine's gym?"

"To catch a Shuckle," Kris replied, as cheery as ever.

Archer was trying to figure this out when Kris relented and explained:

"When I came to Olivine this morning, I headed straight for the gym. The receptionist told me Jasmine – she's the gym leader – is on temporary leave and had gone to the lighthouse."

"Okay," Archer said, following her story.

"I went to the lighthouse and found Jasmine at the top with a sick Ampharos. Ampharos is the lighthouse Pokémon."

"I guess that's important here?"

"For hundreds of years Olivine City has always had an electric type Pokémon living at the lighthouse. Anyway she says Ampharos fell sick like a week ago. No one knows why but the Pokémon Center nurse said it could be a sensitivity to some kind of radio wave."

"I should mention this to Dr. Colress. Maybe it'd be useful."

"Apparently they think something in milk can cure the Ampharos, so Jasmine asked me if I could run to the dairy farm outside Olivine to get some, and she'll cut her leave short and get back to her post at the gym."

"Why not go to the Mart?"

"The Mart was out," Kris said. "When I got to the dairy farm the farmer told me he also has sick Pokémon, so they haven't been able to produce milk for a week and he's desperate for his own business. It looks like the same ailment."

"Even more important to mention to Colress."

"Of course Miltank are different from Ampharos; the only thing that can heal the Miltank is a special kind of fermented berry juice. The farmer said he'd give me milk for free if I could get some juice for his cows."

"So go back to the Mart."

"Except the Mart is all out of juice too. They tell me however that it's very easy to make it yourself if you have a Shuckle. It's a kind of Pokémon only found on Cianwood Island." Kris beamed. "So now I'm off to Cianwood."

"Forgive my practicality, but why not just walk one route back to Ecruteak and see if they have milk in the grocery stores there?"

"I'm sure they do."

"Then...?"

"I wanna see what a Shuckle looks like."

Archer opened his mouth to say something, then stopped to consider whether it was even worth it before deciding, "Actually, no, I have nothing to say to this. Go to Cianwood."

"That's kind of why I was mentioning it. I only have an Eevee..."

"So?"
