"I have no way to get across the ocean to Cianwood Island."

"Evolve your Eevee into a Vaporeon."

"No water stone. Besides, poor Eevee."

"I don't see how I can help you with your travelling woes."

"I overheard some of your people saying you're heading towards the Sevii Islands."

"Who, pray tell, so I can punish them for talking too much?"

Kris didn't answer. "I hoped I could hitch a ride on your boat."

"Not happening," replied Archer.

"Eevee and I wouldn't interfere," she said, "We could even help out."

"We already have enough hands on deck," Archer said pointedly. "Look, talk to some of the fishermen down at the wharf. One of them might give you a fishing rod so you can catch a water type and use that to swim across."

Archer figured he'd shooed Kris off till a couple of hours later, when their ship was getting ready to set sail and she appeared on the dock with her Eevee.

"I talked to the fishermen."

"Did you, now?"

"One of them said since the grocery store is low on supplies, he was willing to trade me an old rod for a half-gallon of milk, and..."

"Never mind. Just get on the fucking boat," scowled Archer.

The Team Rocket ship set off uneventfully from the port. Everyone accepted Kris as practically already one of Team Rocket, which would not have bothered Archer too much were it not for the fact he kept admonishing the minions to not talk so loosely about Team Rocket business, and here they were accepting this outsider so carelessly. Yet he already had the idea he would invite her to join, if that is what she wanted; he merely wished to feel out her motives.

Archer joined Kris on deck where she was watching the Tentacool drift around carried aimlessly by the waves. The sun glinted on the seawater and Eevee, sitting atop a barrel, seemed to be enjoying the salty freshness of the surf.

"Kris?"

"Yeah?"

"Why do you even want to join Team Rocket? Do you even know what you'd be doing, really?"

"I guess I'd do the same things you do."

"I do a lot, Kris."

There it was again, that nagging impression of his that she had a patent naïveté to the world, and a carelessness unsuited to crude realities. "Have you heard stories at all about the kind of business Team Rocket engages in?"

"I know Team Rocket relocates Pokémon."

"Relocates. Yes." Good euphemism for theft, but I still think she's not cut out to be Team Rocket material, Archer thought, adding tentatively, "There's more than that."

"Yes, more than that, but every organization sometimes has to liquidate liabilities."

Scratch that. She's perfect for Team Rocket.

It was nightfall by the time they reached Cianwood. Archer was restless; however, continuing a voyage across rough waves such as the whirlpool-laden waters surrounding Cianwood was inadvisable at night, so it behooved them to make port and be patient till the sun came up and made sailing easier. Patience of course, was one of the virtues that eluded him.

The other was perhaps humility, not for himself so much as his organization. Capturing a Legendary Pokémon would only affirm the magnificence of Team Rocket in Archer's view. For tonight at least, his imagination of such grand accomplishments made all the stupidities and failings of their agents-in-training capable of being overlooked.

The nighttime lights of the small island village sparkled like starlight across its sandy paths, and traditional residences spread out at walking distance from the seashore. It was a quaint town that had as its main source of income the fishing trade, as well as rare medicines that were an exclusivity from the isle's natural flora and fauna.

Unable to sleep, Archer's inquietude led him out to the beach where he strolled along with Houndoom keeping him company. Attired in the white syndicate uniform, people kept away – the few people who were out at this moonlit hour anyway. Everything was peaceful, and a nocturnal Pokémon like Houndoom always enjoyed talking a walk at night, as did Archer himself admittedly.

He had not expected to go very far from their ship, but when he saw what looked like a gleam of crystal light racing in the distance, he changed his plans.

Archer ended up at a rocky alcove erosion had carved into the island's cliffs, before which he found none other than Kris, and the wild Suicune – and another trainer, whom Archer did not know.

Even at night the creature's fur shimmered ethereally. It was watching the two humans quarrel.

"That Suicune is mine," the man snapped.

"No it isn't. Suicune is wild," Kris countered.

"In that case, we'll battle to show it who's more worthy as a trainer, you or me."

Her opponent unlocked a Poké Ball, a knowing smirk on his face. From where he stood, Archer frowned; with the assured way he carried himself, this trainer looked experienced enough to out-level Kris' lone Eevee and probably carried a full team of six Pokémon.

"I don't even know who you are," said Kris honestly.

"Gary Oak from Pallet Town. And there's no way I'm losing!"

Suicune was glancing between Gary and Kris as the latter protested.

"But don't you see fighting is pointless?" Kris replied, "Suicune can pick whomever it wants for a trainer. Or maybe it just wants to be free."

The Suicune, with a mischievous little cry, sprang forward to poke one of Kris' empty Poké Balls with its nose. Before anyone could react it opened the capsule and was drawn in with a flash of light.

Everyone froze in shock as the Poké Ball's red indicator light flickered a few times, the sphere not shaking at all, before registering as caught. Then it was Gary who gave the first utterance; it was less coherent and more a frustrated exclamation of outrage.

"I guess that solves that," figured Kris.

"No it doesn't! How can a Pokémon choose its master? It's unheard of."

"Actually in Unova, the legendary dragon Pokémon selected their own—"

"We're in Johto, not Unova! And Suicune is not a dragon." Gary was furious. "I can't believe it! Without even a challenge? The Legendary Beasts belong with a future Champion, not some rookie trainer with a pet Eevee."

"It's in my Poké Ball now," she replied with a shrug.

Gary eyed the capsule. "You know, Poké Ball registration numbers can be forged."

She stared at him wide-eyed. "You saw it walk up to me!"

"Actually, the only people who saw that are you – and me."

What was he considering? He never got so far. Archer stepped into the open.

"Ready to go, Kris?" Archer prompted.

She sprinted over to his side as Gary stared at them, his face blanching. "You're part of Team Rocket?"

"Yes, as a matter of fact, we both are," Archer replied smoothly, and the look of appreciation Kris shot him did not go unnoticed, "Is that something your Pokémon would like to take up with us?"

Houndoom was growling in anticipation of the fight. Gary took a disarming step back, but there was a spark of sheer resentment in his eyes.

"Whatever… Suicune is yours," Gary relented.

They walked away together, back down the beach. Kris turned to Archer and asked, "Am I really part of Team Rocket now?"

"Well, perhaps we should make it official. Would you like to join Team Rocket?" asked Archer.

"Would I ever!" she exclaimed.

"Then I'll see to it you're brought in. After all, it's better for us to recruit the trainer than steal the Pokémon," he quipped, with a motion towards Suicune's Poké Ball.

The next day was bright and sunny. They set sail as soon as the sun was up, with their newest crewmate practically bouncing with excitement. All the cadets were happy to have her officially part of the team – because she still apparently had like three boxes of cookies left – and Archer was happy to be able to report to Giovanni that they now had a trainer with a Suicune on their side. Things were going great for Team Rocket in Johto.

Kris was fitted with one of the black Team Rocket uniforms, and once she had dressed was told to report to Archer.

Archer filled her in on their present mission. "The Tanoby Ruins are abandoned, ancient temples within the Sevii Islands archipelago," he explained as he showed her a map. "A contact of ours sighted a Legendary Pokémon in the area, one that Giovanni has been after. It's our job to trap it and bring it back to the boss."

"What kind of Pokémon?" asked Kris.

"Mew."

Kris glanced at her Pokédex and searched for the species name. An artist's rendering of a small catlike Pokémon displayed onscreen as well as the following information:

Mew
Type: Psychic
This Pokémon is said to be extinct. Because it was able to use every known move, many scientists believe Mew was the prehistoric ancestor of all Pokémon.

"It says Mew is extinct," she remarked.

"That's what everyone thinks," smiled Archer. "We've got evidence that there's at least one left. Ancient carvings within the Tanoby Ruins depict Mew, so if there's any place to start a hunt, it would be there. That's where you'll be a help...Mew is said to be the most powerful Pokémon in the world. If we end up in a battle with it, another legendary like your Suicune might be the only thing strong enough to fight it."

"Then how did you ever expect to catch it before we had Suicune?"

"The way we still expect to catch it," replied Archer, "through cleverness. However, any confrontation should be easier now."

They arrived at their destination within a couple of hours and disembarked. Eevee strutted ahead, leading the way for its trainer.

The Sevii Islands each had a small village settlement, but for the most part were rather untamed. Wild Pokémon flourished here, of unique and rare varieties, and Archer could absolutely imagine a supposedly extinct Pokémon having hidden itself away in the inviolability of these forests for years unknownst to man. Being in the ocean some distance southward, the climate on these isles was warmer than the temperate-northern of the Kanto and Johto regions, but not to the oppressive heat of tropical Hoenn.

After trekking through the foliage for some time, they reached the far end of the island and at a signal from Archer, the cadets spread out to search the ruins here. Archer himself made directly for the main temple, which stood as an imposing monument among its smaller brethren. Kris accompanied him.

"What were these temples ever built for?" she wondered as they stepped through its columned portico.

"No one really knows. Most people think they were built by ancient civilizations that worshipped Pokémon," explained Archer.

Eevee gave a cry from ahead, and they walked over to find the Pokémon gazing up at an image carved into the stone. It depicted a feline creature that looked much like the artwork of Mew in Kris' Pokédex.

"Well there's the carving of Mew," said Archer. "Now to find the real thing."

They looked around for some other clue, then something caught their eyes.

Off to the side were a number of small Pokémon called Unown, which floated together in a sociable cluster. Neither Kris nor Archer knew what they were. "Maybe those Pokémon could help us," Kris speculated.

"It's worth a shot," figured Archer.

They were an unusual species, with flat bodies in different letterlike shapes and a single eye in their center, yet despite their otherwise alien appearance they seemed like friendly beings. When they noticed Kris and Archer approaching, they came over to meet them as if equally drawn by curiosity.

"Hi!" greeted Kris.

The Pokémon squeaked happily and shifted about their position. With their figures they spelled the word:

HELLO

"Aren't they cute? And they're so intelligent...they can actually write!"

A young Unown that looked like a letter R had taken an interest in the red R on their shirts. It flitted around as Kris pointed her Pokédex at the nondescript little animal.

Unown
Type: Psychic
Different forms of Unown exist. When alone, nothing happens. However, if there are two or more, an odd power is said to emerge.

Archer frowned skeptically. "That sounds either intriguing or worrying," he said.

"What are a group of you called?" asked Kris.

ALPHABET

"Actually, I should've seen that coming," considered Kris.

The alphabet, as they were, shifted about again to spell:

CHOSEN BY SUICUNE WELCOME TO OUR HOME

"They know about the Legendary Pokémon with us," she remarked with astonishment.

Archer mulled this over. "If they know about one Legendary Pokémon... then perhaps they know about others." He turned to the Unown. "Have you seen a Pokémon called Mew?"

WHY

"Because...I would like to meet a Mew," explained Archer, oddly self-conscious at having to explain himself to wild Pokémon.

The Unown all looked at each other and chattered softly. Archer got the odd feeling they were discussing him in a huddle. Then they arranged themselves:

DOES MEW WANT TO MEET YOU

"Ok, this is stupid," decided Archer. "We're evidently getting nowhere with the epistolary."

The Unown squeaked, and suddenly spread out to encircle the two humans.

There was a flash of blinding light, and suddenly Kris and Archer warped to a forest grotto. Rays of sunlight, at an angle insinuating it was already late afternoon, shone brilliantly through dappled leaves, and within the center was a stone relic. The Unown had seemingly vanished.

Kris turned accusatorily towards Archer. "Why'd you insult them?"

"I didn't insult them! Well, not in so many words," Archer added reluctantly. "Where are we anyway?"

"You're in Agate Town."

They glanced up to see a lady who had entered the grotto through a side cave passageway. She was slender, with long blonde hair and no-nonsense green eyes; Archer felt he should recognize her, but could not place from where. For her part she looked quite surprised, as if she had not expected anyone else to be here. At her heels was a Glaceon, an ice-type Eevee evolution.

Her statement, however, took a moment to sink in. "Orre? We're in the Orre region?" echoed Archer.

"That's almost on the other side of the globe," said Kris, eyes wide. "We're from Johto."

"Did the Pokémon of the forest bring you here?" the woman asked.

"What...Pokémon?"

"Relic Forest is considered sacred. It's said to be a place of purification, the dwelling place of a mystical creature that can heal even mortal wounds or ailments." She was regarding them cautiously and Archer realized she had noticed their uniforms. Team Rocket was known worldwide. Whether they were loved or hated, respected or feared...that was what made the difference.

Kris' Eevee showed no qualms. It scampered happily over to the Glaceon, which recognizing the younger of its kind, gave a happy cry of greeting and touched noses with it. The woman glanced down at it and her guarded expression was tempered with a small smile.

"Well, I can see you raise your Pokémon like a friend – it's so lively. I don't know either of you personally; I know your employer, but I don't think that should matter now. My name's Oleana." She held out a hand to them. "Mrs. Oleana Rose."

Chapter 8 - The Pokémon of Relic Forest

When Mr. Rose discovered Oleana had invited the two Team Rocket agents to their home in Agate Town he was cordial towards them but his skepticism could not be hidden. He welcomed their guests in to sit and have a drink in the parlor and then discreetly took Oleana aside to ask her what she meant by this.

"They say wild Pokémon teleported them to the Relic Forest," explained Oleana.

"I don't buy it. I say they're spies," Rose responded, "probably sent to chart new territory for Giovanni."

"Perhaps," she conceded, "but either way it would behoove us to keep a close eye on them until we know for sure."

"You're right about that, Oleana." Rose pondered for a moment. "I wonder if he found out about our deal with the Silph Company?"

Meanwhile, Archer watched Rose and Oleana from afar. They were out of hearing range at present, and he could only speculate what they were talking about; no doubt it was about them. However, the good thing about that was they couldn't hear what he and Kris discussed right now either.

The Roses residence at Agate Town was unique. It was a three-story house tucked away beneath the roots of what once had been a massive sequoia tree, with a clear view of the mountain creek that wove deftly through the village and down crystalline cascades to the pond. Archer thought the place cozy, both by its exterior appearance and interior comforts. He noticed guards patrolling the outside of the house, all wearing purple bandanas around their necks. The guards didn't faze him; Giovanni had guards everywhere, but the bandanas wear a unique touch, almost like the uniforms Team Rocket wore.

"Do you know these people?" Kris asked Archer, when he glanced at her. "You seemed to recognize Oleana back there in the forest grotto."

Archer nodded affirmingly. "Mr. Rose is the former CEO of Macro Cosmos. Oleana had been his right-hand."

"Macro Cosmos," mused Kris, "doesn't Team Rocket own that company now?"

"It was one of our early acquisitions in the Poké Ball industry," Archer answered. "Both Rose and his wife Oleana are technically wanted in Galar; do you remember hearing what happened over there with some kind of alien Pokémon called Eternatus?"

Kris gave a small nod, and Archer went on:

"Giovanni coerced Rose to sell his company through manipulating that scandal. Orre has no extradition treaties, and Rose and Oleana have had the good sense to stay far away from Team Rocket's business since they moved here. However, because of how our past negotiations with them went, I wouldn't wholeheartedly trust them either."

Mr. Rose and his wife Oleana made their way back into the parlor area followed by a butler who carried a tray with four goblets and a bottle of sparkling apple cider. They sat down as the butler opened the bottle, filled the glasses and walked out of the room. Archer noticed the butler was wearing a purple bandana. It looks just like the ones worn by the guards patrolling the house, he thought.

"My wife Oleana told me that you two had been transported to this region by Unowns," Rose commented.

"Yes," replied Archer, "We were far away, came across them and before we knew it, here we were."

Rose and Oleana glanced at each other and Rose asked, "Where did you say you were from?"

"It was an island with ruins," Archer answered briefly; the question made him a little nervous. How the hell can we get out of here fast? Without appearing rude? he thought.

As if sensing his nervousness, Kris decided to change the conversation. Her eyes caught sight of two very large wolves that were lounging on a rug nearby. They had blue fur and piercing yellow eyes.

"What beautiful animals!" she said in admiration. Are these the famous Legendary Pokémon from Galar?"

"Yes...these are Zacian and Zamazenta," affirmed Oleana.

"How did you ever catch them?" Kris asked.

"I didn't actually catch them. They just selected me as their trainer," she replied modestly.

Archer worried Kris would bring up her Suicune, but she held her tongue, already showing more prudence than the rest of the cadets back at Johto. He began wondering how those recruits were doing. They must have realized his absence by now. Knowing them, they were probably conjuring up extravagant scenarios of death and danger instead of the somewhat embarrassing reality of him getting kidnapped by Unowns.

Archer felt a sudden sense of urgency. Why, he did not know; what he did know was that the entire situation was making him uneasy and he wanted to get out of there as soon as possible.

"Thank you for your hospitality," he said, "But we really need to get going..." he stood up and everyone followed his lead. Mr. Rose extended his hand and Archer shook it.

"Do come back for a visit sometime," Oleana told Kris, "Perhaps for a bit longer; and I will give you a tour of the grounds."

"Thank you, we'll keep it in mind," said Kris good-naturedly.

"My chauffeur can drive you into town, if you need it," Mr. Rose told them as he and Oleana escorted them to the front door.

"That is very kind, yes. Thanks again," Archer said as he put his hand on Kris' back and gently urged her out the door. As far as he was concerned, he couldn't get out of there fast enough.

Rose snapped his fingers at one of the guards standing outside. "Chauffeur, please," he ordered and in less than a minute, the chauffeur stood before him awaiting instructions. "Take them into town, drop them off where ever they like, and then return here."

"Yes sir," the man said, and without speaking to Archer or Kris, he walked quickly to a limousine and opened the door in expectation of passengers. Archer did not disappoint. He took Kris' hand and led her to the car where they both quickly got into.

Oleana waved to them, Rose by her side, as they stood watching them leave. Kris waved back.

"Why were you so stressed?" she whispered to Archer as the chauffeur pulled the limousine away from the house and drove out, "I could sense the anxiety coming off you in waves."

"Because," he whispered back, "It felt just like when we go visit Giovanni in his office... did you notice that he didn't have one or two body guards, but rather a dozen...all wearing purple kerchiefs around their necks." He paused, and then added, "It looked like some kind of uniform."

Kris didn't answer, and the rest of the trip in the car was very quiet. The chauffeur said nothing to them during the entire trip until they arrived where the downtown area began and then asked, "Where to, sir?"

"The Pokémon Center, please," Archer replied.

The limousine arrived at the Pokémon Center five minutes later and the chauffeur pulled up to the entrance. "Sir, we have arrived," the driver simply informed them.

"Thank you," said Archer as he and Kris got out of the car. As soon as they closed the door, the driver drove away.

Archer and Kris went into the Pokémon Center to notify Giovanni. He didn't want to call from Rose's residence, figuring it would be best that their conversation be kept with a modicum of privacy.

While he took the telephone receiver in one hand and set to dialling with the other, he overheard two novice trainers who were seated nearby as they conversed.

"I caught a glimpse of the forest guardian yesterday. It was attracted by the cookies I was eating. I guess it's fond of sweet food."

"You're so lucky! I'd love to see a Mew..."

The moment Archer heard that, he froze. He glanced over and, as charming as possible, inquired:

"Excuse me, you wouldn't happen to be discussing the Legendary Pokémon of Relic Forest, would you?"

They both jumped as if startled by his being there. "Please pretend you never heard us discussing it!" the first entreated.

"It's supposed to be a village secret. Mew protects the forest and Agate Town," the second told him.

"Oh don't worry, I wouldn't dream of telling anyone..." assured Archer with a smile.

...except the boss, he thought slyly as the other trainers departed the Pokémon Center, returning to the immersion of their conversation, and he turned back to dialling the telephone. He could hardly believe his good fortune.

Giovanni had, unsuprisingly, heard from the minions by now about Archer's disappearance, and while glad to know he was not in any danger, the Team Rocket boss had understandable questions.

"Archer. What are you doing in Orre?"

"We got teleported here by some wild Pokémon."

There was a pause; then Giovanni asked, rather with annoyance:

"Why did you offend Unowns?"

"I didn't set out to offend them," justified Archer. "...How did you know they were Unowns?"

"Because only Unowns would do something like that of their own accord," explained Giovanni. "They're as mischievous as Zorua and explorers are warned to never approach a wild Unown unless it's alone. When you see a bunch of Unowns in one place, you're supposed to stay clear of them."

Now we're told this, Archer reflected crossly.

"I'll send a helicopter to pick you up," said Giovanni matter-of-factly.

"Do you think we can delay it enough for us to follow up on something we've heard?" Archer asked, "Mew is apparently here in this town. They've been hiding it like some kind of village protector all this time."

"Interesting."

"Yes sir," concurred Archer emphatically. "All we have to do is flush it out and lure it into a battle."

He could almost envision the fierce delight sparking in Giovanni's eyes. "Then you and Kris will set out to capture the Pokémon. I'll get the helicopter to pass by the Relic Forest at about midnight Orre-time. Get the Mew and be on it."

So saying, Giovanni hung up the telephone.

Archer left the Pokémon Center to find Kris outside with her Pokémon. Eevee was scampering playfully around Suicune, practically underpaw as both Pokémon vied to be fed berries by their trainer. "What's the word from the boss?" asked Kris as she saw Archer approach her.

"Change of plans," he said firmly. "We're getting into the Relic Forest and swiping a Mew."

"Finally, a real mission!" exclaimed Kris. He grimaced at her exuberance.

"Not so loud," he snapped, "or else all the townspeople will know!"

"Oh. Sorry, Archer."

"You know all those Lava Cookies you bought?"

"I've only got a few left," Kris replied.

"...A few?" He gave her a questioning look. "I thought you had three boxes."

"Eevee and I binged them on the boat so that they wouldn't get swiped by pickpockets. You know you have a surprising amount of thieves in the crew."

Archer bit back a retort. "How many cookies do you have left?"

"Half a box."

"Good enough. That's our bait for the Mew," smirked Archer. "We'll need your Suicune's help as well, just like we expected back at the Tanoby Ruins. I'll fill you in."

Archer and Kris stayed at the Pokémon Center till the clock struck midnight. Then they strolled to the Relic Forest.

The forest was at walking distance, connected to the rest of Agate Town via a narrow cavern passageway with rocky features lined by moss and smooth ground. Kris was accompanied by her two Pokémon, Eevee and Suicune, which were contentedly walking outside of their Poké Balls. They all emerged in the woodland grotto.

Moonlight shone ethereally like a spotlight illuminating the ancient stone relic in the center of the forest. As they approached, Archer reviewed the surroundings. The place was peaceful but there were no signs of any Pokémon.

Kris had retrieved a handful of Lava Cookies from her bag. "What are we supposed to do with the cookies? Just leave them here?"

Archer was debating this when movement amidst the trees caught his eye, and just then the Mew appeared.

The Pokémon floated in mid-air through psychic ability. It was a small animal that looked like a kitten, with pastel pink fur and a tail as long as its body; so delicate in form it hardly seemed fit to be considered the world's most powerful Pokémon, but Archer knew to never judge a Liepard by its spots. It gave a friendly mew, alert to the cookies.

"Oh, do you want cookies?" Kris offered it some.

Archer was less patient. "Now, attack with Suicune before it gets away!" he snapped.

Kris glanced at him a bit uncertainly yet she obeyed quickly.

"Suicune, Aurora Beam!" cried Kris.

The leopard arched backwards and unleashed a shimmering ray of ice. Frosty clouds of evaporation bloomed in its wake as the beam struck Mew head-on. The little Pokémon squeaked, tumbling backwards in mid-air.

Before it barely had a chance to right itself, Archer acted fast. He pulled out a metal restraining ring, snapping it open before hurling it at the Mew. It closed around the creature; when Mew tried to struggle loose it squealed as electricity coursed through it, and it slumped limply in its prison.

"I thought we'd just use a Poké Ball," Kris protested.

Archer shook his head. "We don't want it getting away and we don't have any Master Ball with us. Besides, we can heal it once we get it back to headquarters."

Kris looked at the Mew, now lying injured in the trap, without agreement but not about to argue.

Suddenly they heard a clear voice shouting from behind them. "...the Mew!"

It was Oleana and her husband Mr. Rose, with another man they didn't recognize following close behind.

At that moment, wind whipped through the trees as their helicopter came into view, its shadowy form outlined against the night sky. Oleana reacted quickly, tossing a Poké Ball onto the ground and sending Zacian out. "Zacian, Metal Claw!" she ordered.

"Suicune, Gust!" countered Kris. The wolf leapt at Suicune, its gleaming claws colliding with its opponent's side; Suicune, with an almost affronted roar, swung its head to bring forth a whirlwind hurling Zacian sideways. Zacian, itself a Pokémon of comparable power, skidded but held its ground.

The Team Rocket helicopter stopped overhead, dropping a rope ladder long enough for Archer to seize hold of it with one hand and the captive Mew with the other. Kris recalled Suicune to its Poké Ball and grabbed the ladder also as the helicopter began its ascent. Eevee clung tightly to her shoulder.

"Cut that ladder!" snapped Oleana, not about to give up. "Sacred Sword!"

"Eevee, Swift!" Kris called, and the small Pokémon attacked first, shooting bright shards of light at their enemies below. They sparked and flared as they struck the ground, disorienting everyone; in the impossible attempt to evade, Zacian missed its target, stumbling ungracefully over onto its side with a surprised yelp.

As the helicopter flew away, Mayor Cade – the man who had followed Rose and Oleana – asked, "You have a Mew here?"

"We had a Mew here," corrected Rose. "It was supposed to be Agate Town's secret."

"Why didn't you tell me?" Cade demanded.

"Why would we?" replied Rose straightforwardly. "You would have tried to catch it."

"Better in Cipher hands than Team Rocket's," countered Cade.

Rose thought about that and then sighed. "It pains me to say so, but in retrospect perhaps you're right."

"Of course I'm right," answered Cade. "Now Giovanni has a Mew. Do you think he'll be content? The only reason he has a fancy for powerful Pokémon is so he can use them to expand Team Rocket's territory. I wonder how long it'll take him to encroach on Orre, like he did Galar? My bet is...not long, if he's already sending spies."

Cade knew well how to win over Rose. He watched as his associate's indignation strengthened into resolve.

"Get some of our people together," said Rose darkly. "We're going to pay Team Rocket a visit."

As the coastline of Johto came into view, Kris gazed out of the helicopter. Eevee pawed at the window, excited to be returning to their home territory.

Archer was in good spirits after the successful events at Agate Town. He glanced triumphantly from the captured Mew – which, in contrast to Archer, appeared to be in very low spirits – and then towards Kris with a smirk.

"Only your first mission, and we've bagged a Mew," Archer praised, "and thanks to your Eevee's Swift attack we were able to make a quick get-away. For a new recruit you show excellent promise. I can't imagine why I ever doubted bringing you into Team Rocket."

She smiled joyfully. "I'm excited to see what our hideout looks like. I know you've got one in the basement of the Mahogany Town grocery store, but I haven't actually seen it."

"Yes, that's right, you haven't been given a proper tour of our hideout yet," realized Archer. "As soon as we turn over the Mew to Dr. Colress, our chief scientist, I'll show you around."

The helicopter descended to land in the forest area around the Lake of Rage, and they walked back to Mahogany Town and slipped into the grocery store unnoticed by any of the townspeople.

They went straight to the laboratory, where they were met by Colress. "Good afternoon, Archer. Giovanni contacted me a half-hour ago and said you would be bringing a Mew to study." The look of fascination in the scientist's eyes at having such a unique test subject was impossible to conceal.

Archer handed him the captive Mew. "It's injured. You'll have to heal it."

"That will be easy to remedy," said Colress, looking over the Mew. "My, this poor creature looks so downcast. Was there really no other way to catch it?"

"The urgency of time made any alternate method impractical. ...Dr. Colress, meet Kris...she's one of our newest recruits," Archer changed the topic and introduced her. "Could you tell her a bit about what we're working on here?"

Colress readily and cheerily turned to his lecture. Getting him to discuss his scientific research, Archer had learnt relatively early on, was the surest way to redirect a conversation.

"Giovanni wants to learn more about neurological and genetic influences on Pokémon power, and in particular the effect of radio wavelengths on these factors," Colress explained. "Mew, as the genetic ancestor of all Pokémon, is said to be the most powerful creature of all. Perhaps by studying it we can learn more about the traits that increase statistical strength."

"That sounds very interesting," said Kris, with genuine inquisitiveness.

Archer had even more to say. "Giovanni thinks that by extracting and altering genetic samples, we might be able to create a Pokémon even more powerful than Mew itself."

"Alas, I doubt any effort towards bioengineering such a creature would bear fruit," dissuaded Colress, "but it might be worth the experiment just for Science."

At that moment, an alarm began blaring through the hideout. Archer snapped to attention as Kris looked around nervously. "Is that a fire alarm...?" she asked.

"No," replied Archer, his body tense, "it's an intruder alarm. Someone has broken into our hideout."

But it couldn't be an intruder, could it? he wondered as he hurried to the security room with the monitors, and Kris following right behind him, Who would be so brazen? Maybe one of the stupid cadets just tripped the alarm by accident.

When he saw the images on the monitors, he went into shock.

There had to be at least twenty men. They were dressed plainly, with their only distinctive similarity being the violet bandana they wore around their necks, which they pulled up to cover half their face so as to only show their eyes.

Accompanying them were several tough-looking Pokémon, which all looked as if they were at high levels.

On top of that, the men had guns.

Even worse, Archer noticed, the cadets and their Pokémon were faltering in the attempt to repel them. No one had fired a weapon yet, and the confrontation right now was an all-out Pokémon battle, but it would only be a matter of time. Cursing these unknown enemies, Archer raced in the direction of the conflict, seizing Houndoom's Poké Ball in one hand and the handle of his whip in the other. "You stay here," he ordered Kris.

"But I can help...!" Kris protested. "I have gym badges. I know how to fight."

"You might be good at Pokémon battles, but you have no combat training yet. These people don't look like they're going to respect the outcome of a Pokémon battle. They're paramilitary, as we are," he added grimly.

Archer set out to face the intruders, with Kris ignoring his admonition to stand back and following him at a distance.

No sooner did the battle begin, however, did Archer realize he may have grossly underestimated his Pokémon's stamina compared to that of his enemies. With Houndoom knocked out, and out of usable Pokémon, Archer found himself backed into a corner.

He pulled out the whip and held it taut, ready to fight them off himself, when Suicune leapt in between to face his assailants down.

Kris, who had been watching from afar, hurried over. "You okay Archer?"

Of course, he recalled with succeeding elation, we have a Suicune. We actually have a real Legendary Pokémon on Team Rocket's side! Why the hell am I so worried?

Suicune let out a roar as their enemies stepped back. They evidently had not expected to be confronted with such a powerful opponent. It was enough for Eevee to leap from behind, knocking the guns out of their hands with a spray of Swift shards before they could realize what had happened.

"Get 'em, Suicune!" cried Kris.

With another roar, Suicune unleashed its Aurora Beam. The icy ray struck the first of the enemy Pokémon headlong, and before the others could do much more than ready themselves to attack they were swept aside like Magikarp in rough seas. Suicune was too quick for them, and far too high a level. I can see why the Pokédex says Suicune is called the reincarnation of the north winds, considered Archer, watching the swift elegance with which the animal defeated its foes. Thank God it's on our side.

Eevee meanwhile, was easily keeping the trainers away from their scattered weapons. None of these people seemed to know what to do when faced with fighting a Pokémon themselves. That was one area, at least, where Team Rocket training had the upper hand, considered Archer with pride. And with their Pokémon defeated, they ran for it.

"Go after them!" Archer commanded. "We've got to find out who sent them."

A small number of the minions raced after their fleeing enemies dutifully, accompanied by the growling Eevee evidently out for blood.

"You did great, Suicune!" Kris said cheerfully, petting her Pokémon. The Suicune gave a happy cry.

Archer gathered the remaining group of minions for an evaluation of injuries. Everyone was unharmed, but they had suffered losses, though not in the way any of them had ever expected.

"They took our Pokémon," said the cadet.

"What do you mean, they 'took' your Pokémon?" demanded Archer. "We take people's Pokémon, not the other way around."

"They just caught them off the battlefield as if they were wild," insisted the minion, wringing their hands. "I don't understand how their Poké Balls didn't detect our Pokémon as already having a trainer."

Archer narrowed his eyes, but his mind thought quickly to the conversation he had before with Giovanni, about the Silph Company and the modification of Poké Balls. Could it be someone else out there had the same idea? Only they were smart enough to act upon it? He tried to push the increasingly frustrating debate aside as the cadet continued lamenting:

"That was my Furret they took. I raised him from a Sentret."

"You can get another fucking ferret," retorted Archer, all while worrying about how his own Houndoom could have easily been snagged in the same fashion, and conveniently overlooking the hypocrisy of how they sometimes acquired Pokémon themselves. "What it sounds like is, these people got ahold of modified Poké Balls that allow them to catch anything. But we own every single Poké Ball manufacturer...except the Silph Company..."

"They must not have had many of those Poké Balls, if they didn't try it on Suicune," considered Kris.

"Legendary Pokémon are notoriously hard to catch. After all, they don't just walk up to you willingly," Archer added jokingly, "Frankly, unless they had a Master Ball they would have first had to subdue it, and that would have been a feat unto itself."

The idea they had stolen any of their Pokémon at all, however, had left Archer uneasy.

He left the minions to check on Colress' laboratory. He found the scientist amidst what looked like the aftermath of a tornado, his gear-like Pokémon Klinklang floating beside him as he gathered scattered documents and files into neat piles. Besides Klinklang, the flock of Porygon were also present, all of which looked determined – as determined as their blank stares could get, anyway.

"Dr. Colress, is everything all right here?" he asked.

"We're quite well, Archer. My Pokémon and I were able to repel the intruders fairly swiftly," said Colress.

As Colress spoke, Archer looked around the laboratory, now in disarray. One thing stood out, and he froze. The cage where Mew had been was open.

"The Pokémon is gone!" exclaimed Archer, his eyes wide. "They stole our damn Mew!"

"Oh, you needn't worry," Colress remarked, entirely at ease. "I released the Mew."

Archer just stared at him incredulously. "You released it?"

"Yes."

"You released the Mew? Why would you think that's a good idea? That was a ludicrous idea!"

"The alternative was permitting our enemies to appropriate it," explained Colress. "We may not have Mew anymore, but neither do they...and better that it be loose on our territory than on theirs, where it would be harder to recapture it."

Archer thought about this, and saw the logic immediately. "Colress, I take it back. This is why you're considered a genius."

The scientist merely adjusted his eyeglasses with a smile.

"But Giovanni will no doubt be unhappy about what has happened," continued Archer, "I'm in shock that anyone would dare attack us. They must have a death wish." He then turned with accusation to the cadets. "Or they knew we were grossly unprepared!"

"They had really strong Pokémon," justified one meekly.

"At least we were able to fend them off," Archer said with disdain, "thanks to Kris and her Suicune. But if it hadn't been for that who knows what would have happened. Something entirely avoidable most likely, considering we're supposed to be top-notch Pokémon trainers."

"We do have another cause for concern, however," Colress spoke again. "They were able to confiscate several important documents pertaining to my experiments. Unfortunately, such a loss might put the research back several months."

"I had better get this information to Giovanni. See you later Colress."

The scientist waved Archer off and proceeded with the work before him. Archer and Kris walked quickly out the door and within minutes, crossed paths with the group of returning minions that Archer had sent out. They were empty handed, except for Eevee who had flat ears and was carrying a bandana.

"What happened?" he asked them.

"We lost them. Eevee was the only one fast enough to tackle one of them and take his bandana before he ran off with the others."

"That Eevee is a better warrior than the lot of you!" Archer snapped at them.

He bent down to get the bandana from Eevee and took a closer look at it. He recognized it immediately; it was from Orre.

Archer was briefly called back to Team Rocket's headquarters after notifying Giovanni about the strike on their hideout.

He met the don in his office below the casino in Celadon City. The Persian lounged on Giovanni's lap, eying Archer with its usual circumspection as he dipped his head to his godfather.

Archer wasted no time in getting to the point.

"I need like five machine guns, a reasonable amount of ammunition, and a rose."

Giovanni stared at him for what seemed like a whole minute, the Persian on his lap purring with contentedly squinted eyes. Remembering his manners, Archer added by way of an afterthought, "...please."

"Archer, what is this about?"

"Mr. Rose, the former Macro Cosmos CEO. I want to help him have an accident. With your permission, godfather," he added quickly.

"What did he do?" asked Giovanni.

"His men attacked our hideout."

"The reply to that, is to give a warning."

"Then they defeated our cadets."

"Then we beat him up."

"And me."

"...that makes me question why you were underlevelled. Haven't you been training against wild Pokémon?"

Archer narrowed his eyes. He hadn't been training as often as he should have; his own rancour at himself for such a failing was bad enough without his godfather scolding him for it. "They destroyed our radio antenna, not to mention stole documents with information on our research. Dr. Colress says without a way to broadcast, the scientific project has been set back greatly. Not to mention the escaped Mew, which has to be recaptured."

"Yes, we're probably going to have to kill him," conceded Giovanni. "He's a troublemaker."

"So can I have the machine guns?" Archer asked hopefully.

"Archer, we're not common criminals. We don't go tearing through the streets like mob wars twenty years ago. Our business has rules."

Rules. Again with the fucking rules.

"He didn't kill any of our people," Giovanni explained. "We should give him the opportunity first to recompense us for our losses. He owes us for the property damages, the Pokémon, and the aggravation. If he isn't reasonable..." And he gave a mild gesture.

His faith in Giovanni's leadership immediately restored, Archer straightened his posture. "And then?"

"I can send Jessie and James to handle that trifle if your group is still recovering," replied Giovanni.

Archer smiled slightly. "I think we'll recover much faster if we can settle our differences with Rose personally."

Giovanni sighed, "So many things to take into consideration." Persian looked up at him and squinted as he put his hand on the cat's head and smoothed his fur pensively. Now Giovanni was absolutely aware that Mr. Rose was becoming a formidable rival. "The only thing I see that can't be substituted for something of equal value are the research documents and the Mew, but if Mr. Rose is now as bold as he seems to have become, you will likely get your chance to settle his account."

"Godfather," Archer went on, "the Eevee that gave chase came back with this kerchief." He produced the purple neckerchief and added, "When Kris and I were teleported by the Unowns, we met with Mr. Rose and his wife Oleana. They invited us to their house briefly and I saw these bandanas around the necks of some of their guards."

"That concurs with the information Jessie and James got from Krieger," he continued, "He told them Mr. Rose was in control of a group known as Cipher."

Archer found himself thinking a little too hard about James and Jessie, and how lucky they were to be the boss' personal guards. They were always sent on the best missions in his opinion. Thinking about this, however, left a disagreeably sour taste in his mouth.

He really bore no ill will towards the couple; how could he? They had all been raised together, essentially as a family without blood ties, but to say he did not secretly harbor some unspoken envy towards them for being Giovanni's hand-picked bodyguards would have been a hopeless lie. He would have much rather been given that honor instead of dealing with the bunch of inefficient recruits back in Johto.

"...which only makes the situation ever more grievous." A frown crossed Giovanni's face, snapping Archer's attention back to the present. "You said they were able to capture many of our own Pokémon off the battlefield?"

"They had modified Poké Balls," Archer acknowledged. "Unless we have someone altering products from our own factories, those Poké Balls could only have come from the Silph Company."

"Come back tomorrow Archer, I will have a decision by then. ...and send Dr. Colress, I would like to have a word with him."

"Yes sir," said Archer with determination.

Right then and there, he decided he had enough of inefficiency. If he wasn't good enough to be Giovanni's right-hand, it must be due to his own shortcomings, and the easiest way to measure that would be in how well he achieved his present tasks.

Giovanni wanted him to train their recruits, and he had failed. Fine; he could improve. He would see them improve. He was going to forcibly make them into proper Team Rocket agents, and in the process make himself worthy of Giovanni's praise...with a bit of good, old-fashioned discipline.

Shortly after Archer walked out of the office, Colress walked in.

"Buongiorno Colress," said Giovanni as he extended his hand, which the scientist shook in a friendly greeting.

Colress had also been requested to come to Team Rocket headquarters on account of what happened at Mahogany Town. He was always prompt and thorough in his explanations, and Giovanni was eager to hear an update from him as to how their project stood from the scientific standpoint.

"I have spent several hours trying to rewrite some of the research notes that were taken," Colress explained, adjusting his eyeglasses. "Although I commit most of it to memory, I like to rely on notes to ensure that no mistakes are made."

"Yes, of course," replied Giovanni, "I will send some associates to fix whatever is needed. Give the admins a list of what is broken and whatever else you need to make your research easier, and I will review it."

"Mr. Delavita, notwithstanding that, I've completed my preliminary test," the scientist declared.

"And...?"

"Genetic modification has a negligible influence on Pokémon power."

Giovanni frowned, and Colress elaborated:

"It's more tied to their emotional and mental state. My analysis validates my previous, multiple observations on happy Pokémon...any strong emotional reaction, such as love for its trainer, has the potential to increase or decrease their power."

"Thank you for your report, Dr. Colress, though I must say the findings leave much to be desired," Giovanni replied. "How would you propose creating a strong emotional reaction in a Pokémon quickly?"

"A bond of friendship can't be fostered fast," admitted the scientist, "and emotions like rage and sadness are fickle. That said we also observed a paradox; a complete lack of emotion can produce a similar power increase."

"Explain that."

"Mostly we observed that when measuring the statistics of sleeping Pokémon. In the waking state most living creatures will have some trace of emotion, even if slight. Perhaps that is why, again, in my experimental studies I was able to produce a spike in power by placing Pokémon under hypnotic trance, and, other than emotional trauma I doubt there is another way to produce the same effect."

"Thank you, Dr. Colress," Giovanni replied, "Keep me updated with regard to whatever new information you come across."

"Indeed," was the scientist's response.

"One other minor point..." added Giovanni, as an afterthought, "do you think the theft of these documents could provide Mr. Rose with any kind of advantage over us, either from a business or strategic standpoint?"

Colress analyzed the situation. "That quite depends if they have anyone there who understands them," he said finally. "I believe that Mr. Rose's wife, Oleana, once worked as a scientific researcher...?"

Rose and Oleana were upset that their people had not recovered the Mew, but all annoyance dissipated as soon as they received word of having potentially acquired something else of value. They called Cade, requesting he meet them at their Agate Town residence to discuss this important turn of events, and he came by fairly quickly.

"It turns out Team Rocket has been working on secret scientific research," explained Rose, laying the stolen documents out on the coffee table.

"I don't see how that would pertain to us," Cade said practically.

"It might pertain a great deal to us, if we can find out what they were doing and use their discoveries against them."

"Or perhaps what they may have been on the verge of discovering," Oleana interjected, taking the documents from the table. "There's something they seem to have overlooked."

She examined the documents as she explained, her background as a researcher manifest:

"The radio signal they're using follows a pulse similar to the natural dyna-max radiation of the Galar region. Because of that, they're approaching it in the same manner, by haphazardly broadcasting the signal. The result tends to induce evolution in immature Pokémon. However if it were possible to target the central nervous system directly, it might essentially alter the DNA sequences that regulate what we commonly refer to as type..."

"Could you give me the concise version...?" requested Cade, who looked utterly lost.

"Team Rocket found a way to eliminate a Pokémon's natural weaknesses," Oleana said.

Rose looked proud of her revelation. Cade still looked confused.

"But they didn't even realize the extent of what they had in front of them," she added with marvel. "If my hypothesis is correct, this could lead to a scientific breakthrough in Pokémon neurophysiology."

Cade was apologetic but nonetheless relentlessly inquiring. "I don't realize what we have in front of us, with all due respect."

"We could make a water type immune to electric attacks," explained Oleana. "Or a fire type unaffected by water. It would probably increase their power overall too. Maybe even cause them to develop new attacks."

"What would be needed to do that?" asked Rose, who was already seeing the potential of a large army of practically undefeatable Pokémon.

Oleana thought for a long time. "If we irradiate one of the diamonds from the mine," she replied finally, "and then use that gemstone to power a kind of energy ray – not strong enough to cut, but strong enough so that the radiation can pass through bone tissue and reach the brain...it might work."

Rose turned to Cade with certainty.

"We're going to put people to work on this right away. The faster we can get ahead of Giovanni's men, the better. Cade, I know you've got plenty to do back at Phenac City, but do you think you'd have time to manage the project? I don't want to impose, but I need someone trustworthy to handle it."

His cajoling was hardly necessary. As soon as Cade had properly grasped the concept, he decided that he wanted to be involved.

He had his own plans, after all...and the idea of incredibly powerful Pokémon would be a spectacular help.

Chapter 9 - Discoveries

That morning, Giovanni arrived early at his office and kept busy as usual revising business documents and making phone calls. One of them was to Mr. Silph, who still refused to let his company be bought out.

Giovanni spoke bluntly. "I've overlooked several slights already. Your refusal to sell me a Master Ball, for one, even though I'm perfectly willing to pay the two-million price tag."

"Now Giovanni," began Silph, "you know the way they're made is a proprietory secret, and your people would just try to reverse engineer it. Right now Silph is the only Poké Ball manufacturer that can produce something with an infallible catch rate." And Giovanni had to concede the point, it would not do from a business standpoint to have one's only competitor acquire trade secrets, but neither did he let Silph go unscathed.

"You've been transporting contraband to the Orre region. You're letting Poké Balls out of the factory that lack the fail-safes required by law."

There was a noticeable pause. Giovanni could picture Silph squirming nervously, and it was an agreeable mental image till he spoke – sounding far more forceful and arrogant than Giovanni would have thought.

"Don't tell me you're getting up in arms now just because a few Pokémon were snagged from you?" he scoffed.

"And how did you know we had Pokémon stolen from us?" asked Giovanni smoothly.

Once again Silph fell silent, but now it was with the unease of having been caught in a lie. By his own mouth he had laid bare his alliance with Cipher. Seeing as he'd been left at a loss for words, Giovanni went on:

"The Pokémon in question were, as you say, few. I can more than overlook it provided you recompense me for the damages my associates have endured as a result of your...shall we say, defective Poké Balls? Your majority stock in the Silph Company would be more than sufficient barter."

"Don't bother me with your business machinations, Giovanni." Without caring for a reply, Silph hung up the phone.

Such disrespect would not go unpunished.

Sometime around noon Giovanni glanced at his watch and frowned. "Unbelievable it's already midday," he spoke aloud to himself and glanced at his ever faithful Persian laying at his feet under the desk. "Time to take a lunch break," he added.

"Mrreow," responded the cat.

Giovanni pressed a button and almost immediately had an associate arrive at the office.

"I am going out to lunch...take any messages if anyone calls." He produced a Poké Ball out of his pocket and bringing the Persian into it, walked out of the office.

He arrived at the ground floor finding his limo and driver were waiting for him. "Federico's" he told his chauffeur.

They hurried there and he had lunch, alone. Giovanni did this often as it enabled him to be alone in his thoughts and analyze matters. Everyone at the restaurant knew not to disturb him while he was eating, even his personal guards would stay at a distance. Once finished, he motioned to the head waiter who tended to him.

As Giovanni left the establishment, he glanced up and down the street as a habit, and noticed a familiar person. His heart did a little jump as he saw Delia.

He kept looking at her hoping she would feel the silent stare and turn around in his direction; what a surprise he had when she did. Delia turned and looked straight at him...and smiled. He smiled back, which was a rarity to anyone who knew him personally.

She waved, and he did not miss the opportunity of raising his hand in greeting, "Wait a moment," he said to his driver, and walked over to her.

When they were face to face, Giovanni said, "Thank you for stopping for me. It means a lot to me."

"Thank you for helping me with the tax bill, Gio," she said.

He smiled but made no reply to this statement.

"Well, I have to get back home now," she broke the silence.

"Let me drop you off..." he offered.

"It's not very far, really," Delia replied.

"Please. I insist," he responded, "I notice you didn't bring your car, and the buses don't seem to be running on a regular schedule...that reminds me, I need to talk to the Mayor about this issue."

"Oh Gio," she smiled at him, "You haven't changed, much."

"Is that a good thing, or a bad thing?" he smiled back at her.

"A good thing," was her reply.

They were quiet for a moment and then she spoke up again.

"Alright, you may take me home."

"The car awaits us," he said motioning to his limo. The driver saw this and getting into the car, drove to where they were and held the door open for his boss and his companion to board it.

The chat in the car was minimal and the ride home was swift; once they arrived at Delia's house, she hugged him goodbye and exited the car.

When Giovanni returned to his office he asked his receptionist if there had been any calls, there had not, and then informed her that he was going home for the day. "Let's go home, Persian," he said aloud to the Poké Ball he carried.

Delia, meanwhile, was thinking of how her day had gone and a nostalgic smile crossed her lips.

Bird Pokémon twittered happily as sunlight shone warmly across National Park, at walking distance from Goldenrod City. It kept its name from that historical age before the countries united into regions and formed a planetary council, and was the oldest and largest park in Johto.

The primary section of the park had wide pebbled paths and beautiful wood benches, running alongside flowering bushes and large stretches of grass where wild woodland Pokémon could occasionally be spied scampering about. In the very center was a picturesque fountain of white marble, with clean freshwater that caught the light as it poured.

Beyond these areas was a small forest, divided from the main path by a low wrought-iron fence. The forest trail, while technically part of the park, meandered into narrow hideaways and cliffside thickets that made it very out-of-the-way and a haven of solitude.

Archer had swiftly returned to Johto and gathered the cadets in one of these forested clearings. They were directed to kneel facing him in a line, which they did with some perplexity but without question. Only Kris was permitted to stand, towards the back at a small distance.

Archer evaluated the group, in one hand the whip that normally was coiled on his belt; beside him, Houndoom sat expectantly on its haunches. "You've been called here because you've all failed miserably," he began.

Curious glances passed between his audience as he continued speaking.

"Nothing can come between Team Rocket and perfection. We keep our reputation in glory and image because we're beyond a crime syndicate – we're an elite militia. I'm your teacher on Giovanni's personal request, not by my choice. I prefer dealing with experienced soldiers," added Archer. "The difference between experienced soldiers and you is that the former aren't blitheringly stupid. So perhaps all of you need a change in instruction..."

"Can I help?" Kris chimed in from the back.

"Kris, you stay out of this unless you want to join them," he snapped. She ducked her head down obediently.

He turned his attention back to the cadets, a couple of whom were trying to hide a snicker. Adult brats, Archer thought with annoyance. They deserve what they're in for.

"We don't tolerate complacency. And we tolerate setbacks even less."

He pulled back with a vengeance. The whip slashed across their shoulders. The cadets flinched and grimaced; somebody couldn't hold back a strangled yelp. One of them jumped to his feet:

"Wait a sec—"

He could do little more than begin to talk before Archer now cracked the whip pointedly in the air. At the signal, his Houndoom sprang like a wolf, pinning down the rebellious recruit; the snarling dog's bared fangs and the heated breath of fomenting embers inches away from the man's throat.

Archer regarded the cadet with disgust. "They say the pain from a Houndoom's burn never goes away. Do you think that's true?"

Houndoom was growling. Archer could see the man's defiance falter instantly. "Forgive me...! Please...call off your Pokémon."

"I ought to give you five more lashes just for being a whimpering coward," Archer replied disdainfully. "Be thankful it's me punishing you and not Giovanni himself. He's reasonable, but not forgiving."

There was a stunned silence. Archer's audience had just realized he was not kidding. The whipping began anew, and without mercy. Anyone who squealed in pain, and there were a few, got three extra lashes. When it was over, Archer dismissed them and as they limped away, Kris walked to him and asked, "Is all this really necessary?"

"Yes," he simply replied as he coiled the whip and put it on his belt.

Archer and Kris wandered out of the forest to the main area of the park. They strolled along the path in relative silence, listening to the peaceful sound of songbirds and leaves.

The first of them to speak was Kris, when she put her hand in her jacket pocket, suddenly stopped and said, "Oh, no. I think I forgot my identification card back at headquarters."

"What?!" Archer exclaimed. "How in hell could that happen? It's supposed to be kept by your bedside along with the clothing you're wearing the following day!"

Kris had a sheepish look on her face, "Hold on, maybe it's hidden away in one of my other pockets." She fumbled as she searched her pockets and retrieved different objects from them; some Poké Balls, berries, and a wallet, and as she got hold of the wallet it fell out of her hands and several cards and papers that were within scattered on the ground.

"It's a miracle you've gotten this far on your own," Archer scoffed as he helped her gather everything up. He saw a photograph amidst the documents and as he picked it up he froze in shock.

The photo was of a woman sitting under a tree with two children; a boy and a girl. The girl was a very small child, almost an infant, and the boy was approximately nine years old.

Archer looked at Kris steadily without saying anything. Kris noticed it. "Is something wrong Archer?"

"This image..." his voice trailed thoughtfully.

Kris explained, "Oh, that's a picture of me and my mom and brother... before she died. You see I'm an orphan but the people who took me into their home were kind enough to save this picture for me. I carry it everywhere."

"Kris," he asked, "Where is your brother now?"

"I wish I knew. We were separated when my mother died and were split up between two different families. I was taken in by my mother's relatives and he by our father's... I was just a baby and as you can see by the picture he was a small boy so we didn't have much control of anything, really... I never heard of him again." Her face was sad and she took the picture from his hand and stared at it.

"Let me show you something," he said as he pulled out his own wallet from his pocket, and showed her a duplicate copy of the photograph.

Kris opened her eyes wide as she saw the photo, then looked up at him and asked, "Why do you have a copy of my picture?"

Archer's gazed softened as he looked at her face and searched for the right words to say, finally replying, "Because I am the little boy in the picture. That is my mother too...and my baby sister."

Kris' eyes filled with tears, and quietly flowed down her cheeks. He took her by her shoulders and drawing her near, embraced her for a long time. "You are my sister. My sister," he repeated incredulously. "I thought about you often but as a small child my options were limited in getting anyone to help me find you. When I grew up, I didn't know where you had been taken to."

They parted, and she just looked at him in silence, finally speaking she said, "I can't believe it. All this time..." her words cut off at this point from emotion.

Archer spoke up, "Everything is okay now, sis. I'm returning to Celadon City tomorrow morning, and I will tell Giovanni; he is my godfather. I think he will welcome you with open arms... after all, dad was a Team Rocket member and Giovanni likes to keep families together if possible."

From vibrant Goldenrod City, Archer and Kris took the train to Celadon City in Kanto. It was little more than two hour's-long travel from one region to the other via rail, and the scenery was a bonus. As they proceeded swiftly along the tracks, Kris glanced out at the forest landscapes that flitted past; once or twice she saw a Sawsbuck lift its head to watch the passing train with curiosity, its antlers bedecked by leaves as autumnal orange as those of the trees.

"I was so small when I was taken to Johto, I don't even remember Kanto," she admitted, turning from the train window back towards her brother.

"I'll have to show you around when we get time," he said. "Many of its cities are larger and more developed than Johto's. Just wait till you see the Silph Company skyscraper; it's even taller than the Goldenrod radio tower."

"Have you lived there all your life?"

"Yes, though I travel a lot because of my duties in Team Rocket. Give it some time; you'll see plenty of the world too. I'm going to ask Giovanni if I can handle your training myself."

Kris brightened up. "That'd be great!"

"Of course. I just found my little sister. I want to get to know her better. Damn it, we have all these years we have to catch up on." Archer tipped his head slightly. "You never did tell me why you were so desperate to get into the syndicate either."

"I'd heard a rumor that my father had been part of Team Rocket," Kris revealed, "and that my brother had been the ward of someone who still was. I figured joining was the best chance I had to find out what happened to my family. I didn't expect I'd find you so quickly! But I have no idea why we ever ended up being separated."

"From what I understand," Archer elaborated, "Giovanni was chosen as my godfather but mom picked someone else for you. As such, he had no claim to take you in when we were both left orphaned. Back then was when Team Rocket first began. It was when the Delavitas were at war with another family. Our father was consigliere when he was killed in a hit from our enemies, when mom was still pregnant with you. It's easy to forget how vicious the Kanto and Johto regions were back then, given how peaceful they are now...till the civil war in Unova happened, that was considered the most violent time in modern history. Mom wanted to distance herself and us from the violence, but she wasn't able to move out of the region before our enemies attacked her. They didn't respect the idea of 'civilians' who were kept apart from the business...in their eyes, anyone affiliated with the Delavitas was to be taken out. Giovanni always says there are rules, but they sure as hell didn't follow them."

"Who's consigliere now?"

"Giovanni's pet Persian."

Maybe he couldn't keep the splinter of envy from his tone, his private rancour at Giovanni's having granted one of their organization's most coveted positions to an animal, because Kris regarded him pensively before asking point-blank:

"Are you hoping to one day inherit Team Rocket?"

Her remark surprised him. "Oh? Does it seem that way?"

"Not really," replied Kris with honesty. "But it does seem you aspire to more."

He thought about her words, but then briskly shook his head. "All I really want is to be of service to Team Rocket. We can't afford any kind of selfish thinking. Giovanni knows what's best for Team Rocket, and upholding the glory of our syndicate is what matters."

He glanced out the window as the train pulled in to a small town platform in order to let off a few passengers. It was only there for a short period before swiftly setting off on its way anew. "The next stop is where we get off, at Celadon City," Archer said.

Meanwhile James, Jessie, and Meowth were strolling along the Celadon City sidewalk towards the train station, enjoying both the cool fall breeze and each others' company.

As the trio walked along, James embraced Jessie. "I think you get more beautiful with every day that passes."

She remembered distinctly how they had come to be partners. Essentially raised in Team Rocket, they'd always had a rapport beyond that of friendly coworkers and more of soulmates. Giovanni could see for himself how well they worked together.

James had always been the mild-mannered one of the duo. They were effectively dating before their relationship was official, neither admitting what was evident to the whole world. She remembered when he finally confessed his love for her, one perfectly moonlit night on a rooftop.

"You had to muster up the courage," she teased.

"No that wasn't it," James replied with a smile. "I was waiting for the right moment to tell you. It had to be special."

"Sentimental," Jessie smiled back, leaning over and kissing him.

Meowth twitched an ear but did not join the conversation, instead leaping ahead happily to spring upon one of the fallen leaves and trap it under his fore-paws; practised hunting skill in the harmless form of play. When he spied a wild Rattata gnawing on a berry, however, and the rodent sighted him and accordingly darted away into the underbrush, Meowth's eyes widened with excitement and he immediately abandoned the leaf on the hunt for real prey.

Jessie placed her arms akimbo. "Meowth, what the fuck."

"Be right back," the cat purred, and he escaped into the bracken with a swish of his tail.

"He refuses to touch kibble, only eats human food, yet goes after a Rattata like we're in a famine," Jessie said, shaking her head. "Who can understand that cat?"

Suddenly they heard a small, crying sound from the parked cars along the sidewalk. Jessie and James bent down to find the cause peering out from under a truck.

It was a small kittenish creature, with pink fur and large blue eyes. It had a thin tail nearly as long as its body, and dainty little paws like those of an ermine.

"Well, what are you doing under that truck?" asked Jessie sweetly. "Come out."

It stared back with wide eyes, the fright of injured innocence.

"Oh come on, we're not going to hurt you," Jessie assured. "Did someone hurt you? We'll beat them up."

This seemed to coax the kitten out, and Jessie picked it up gingerly. "Look at that – it is hurt."

James rummaged through his pockets. "I know we have an extra potion somewhere..."

Sure enough he produced the flask of medicine, which they sprayed on the kitten's injuries; the wounds, which looked like burns from something, faded away before their eyes.

The little animal now happily, and surprisingly, levitated out of Jessie's arms with a series of squeaky mews.

"Where's Meowth when you need him to translate?" Jessie said, perplexed.

"What kind of animal is that anyway?" James wondered.

"Who knows," answered Jessie, "Must be a flying type if it can float like that."

Circling the couple once, the kitten flew off to the berry bushes beside the path.

Meanwhile, Meowth returned to where James and Jessie were, minus rodent. "I'm back. What've we got?"

"We found that kitten under the truck," James told him. As he spoke the strange Pokémon flew back over, presenting the two humans with a berry it had picked.

Meowth gave a surprised meow. "I've never seen a flying cat before."

"Most people have never seen a talking cat before," countered Jessie.

The kitten gave a few happy mews, which Meowth translated, "It says it wants to thank you for helping it out."

"What's your name?" Jessie asked.

The kitten did not answer. Instead, it blithely produced a large bubble of energy in mid-air and began bouncing playfully on it.

"Well," considered Jessie, "we ought to call it something."

Jessie picked it up and the three of them stared at it.

"Mew," the little animal squeaked.

James spoke first, with decided certainty. "Paulie."

"Paulie?" Jessie echoed.

"He looks like a Paulie," James said.

"He could be a she," pointed out Jessie.

James shrugged this off. "If she's a girl she's Polly, and if he's a Paulie he's Paulie."

"What?" questioned Meowth.

"Polly," Jessie smiled, "would you like to be one of my Pokémon?"

"I named it," James protested, "I should be the one to catch it."

"Hush up. You can't tell if it's a boy or a girl."

The kitten gave a few mews. Meowth translated:

"It says it likes both of you but its species are free spirits and it wants to stay free."

"That's unfortunate," said James.

"Also...it's a she."

"Called it," said Jessie. James snapped his fingers, "Polly, then" he said.

They watched the little Pokémon zip away into the bracken.

As the three of them approached the Celadon City train station and halted here, James remarked, "Jessie, when was the last time we took a vacation?"

"We had that assignment in Hoenn," she replied.

"A real vacation," said James. "We could revisit Hoenn for the sake of it...spend time lounging along the seashore and sunshine..."

Jessie's eyes brightened with enthusiasm at the thought. "Wonderful idea, James! It'd definitely beat Kanto's snowy season. It's autumn now," she considered, "maybe when winter comes we could ask the boss for a brief leave."

Meowth once more chimed in as the voice of reason amidst their frivolity. "You know every time you guys do that, we get double the work piled on us when we come back right?"

"Oh, who cares? I think it's a great plan," declared Jessie, "Don't you feel like taking a few days off?"

"Well, maybe I could use some time to catch up with Meowzie and the kittens," Meowth purred, his mind now captivated by personal thoughts of feline romance and family.

The train pulled into the stop, and Archer and Kris disembarked to be met by James, Jessie, and Meowth.

"Well, look who's here," said Jessie, "the newest brother and sister duo."

"You should give her a mini tour, Archer," James added, "Giovanni's meeting isn't for another two hours."

"I might do that," Archer replied, "but we should get something to eat first."

"Is this the elite pair that work as Giovanni's personal guard?" Kris asked with a wide-eyed look.

"Oh right. You never met them," Archer said, turning to introduce his colleagues. "Kris, meet James, Jessie, and the ever chatty Meowth... Guys, this is my sister...Kris."

"Fate works in a mysterious way, it seems," said Jessie.

"Nice ta meet'cha," Meowth spoke up quickly, "happy ta hear that you two found each other."

Kris' eyes widened. "Wow! I've never seen a Pokémon that talks!"

"You talk to Eevee," dismissed Archer.

"We can communicate all right, but Eevee doesn't speak human language," Kris pointed out.

"I'm special," purred Meowth proudly.

"Archer, we were headed to the mall for lunch..." James addressed him, "why don't we all go."

"Yeah," agreed Jessie, "you can point out some sights along the way."

"Ok, sounds good," Archer replied, "I'll bring out my Houndoom; he could use some exercise by walking."

"...and I'll bring out Eevee," added Kris as she took her Poké Ball from her backpack.

"Houndoom, emerge!" shouted Archer.

"Eevee, out!" Kris joined in.

Houndoom appeared wagging its tail, and gave a contented bark when Archer patted it on the head. Eevee squeaked happily and immediately hopped onto Kris' shoulder.

The group of friends walked up the street together chatting animatedly. Archer and his sister Kris, James and his girlfriend Jessie, Meowth, Eevee, and Houndoom; enjoying the peace that comes with true fraternal unity.

"So what's all that about an attack on Mahogany Town?" James inquired. "Giovanni was irate about it."

"Don't even remind me of it," scowled Archer, "it was a bunch of goons sent by Cipher. They made us lose a rare Pokémon we'd made off with, not to mention some kind of research paperwork. It's a disastrous blow to our syndicate's image."

"Ffftt. That's no cat-astrophe," Meowth chimed in with a yowl and a lash of his tail, "So a Pokémon gets away; you guys can recapture it, no sweat. And paperwork? What can they do with that?"

Little else was said regarding rival syndicates and lost possessions. The sentiments expressed by Meowth were shared by most everyone there; even Archer, who thought that Cipher was an annoyance, yet certainly not one that should ever come to matter in the grand scheme of things.

Chapter 10 - Rocket Game Corner

Rocket Game Corner was objectively far too flamboyant for a secret lair, but considering Team Rocket's natural flamboyance such an in-your-face hideout worked perfectly. It was Giovanni's flagship casino, a glitzy public playground with the undercurrent of subtly sinister charm. It stood only a block away from an elegant office building that was the official business headquarters of Rocket Enterprises, but the center of their illicit activity was without doubt the casino.

Glittering violet neon and rich red carpeting complemented each other in an almost magnetic dalliance. Slot machines were a bright enticement, which drew the onlooker into its shimmering maze-like siren song, and wide tables where games of roulette, craps, and baccarat beckoned further with their temptation of wins and losses. Everywhere people in elegant attire milled about, either testing their fortunes or watching the games, and sparingly in the crowd one could find a Pokémon accompanying its owner as a disinterested sentinel. To the far side of the floor was a long bar with a glass counter, displaying an entire wall of fine liquor behind the bartender, and on the opposite side was a reception area to collect one's winnings; chips could be cashed out for money or rare Pokémon.

All this was the show put on for prying eyes. No one took heed of the back of the casino floor, where a switch, hidden behind a poster on the wall, granted access to the expansive basement level and Team Rocket's headquarters.

Giovanni's office was spacious with furnishings of fine leather and mahogany and, hung on the wall behind his desk, a tapestry bearing a single red R. Jessie, James, and Meowth entered to find Giovanni on the telephone. His Persian sat beside him, angling one ear to them as they stepped in but not giving them much more than a second thought.

"Mr. Silph, I've been very nice till now," Giovanni was saying. "I don't think you want this whole matter to turn impolite."

On the other line, Silph's reply was astoundingly haughty, "Word around is that you're going to retire soon anyway. I don't put too much credence in Team Rocket being the all-powerful empire it was twenty years back."

"What would give you that idea?" asked Giovanni calmly.

"I know people. People you've made enemies of, who are stronger than you. Yes," he added, almost relishing the point, "there's actually someone stronger than the Delavitas nowadays."
