Cade waited till Archer was securely bound by rope between two columns before stepping forwards. The guards retreated to the edges of the room, present in case they would be called on, though Cade doubted he would require their assistance. Without putting away the first Poké Ball, he retrieved a second from his pocket and sent out the Pokémon within.

"Let me introduce you to my Pokémon partner," he introduced it almost jovially, motioned to the creature as he put away its capsule. "This is my Espeon."

Espeon sat in a neat lump with its paws tucked underneath it, shaping its lithe form almost like a bread loaf as it observed Archer. It was an Eevee evolution, diurnal yet catlike, with velvet lavender-white fur and a tapered, forked tail. A red gemstone, not unlike that of Giovanni's Persian, graced its forehead.

Archer glanced from the Pokémon back to Cade, who still held the initial Poké Ball in one hand. Archer knew it wasn't Espeon's, and guessed whatever Pokémon was in there would be the next stage of his torment.

"All Espeon," continued Cade, "as you probably have heard, are able to hone in on thoughts. If you hope to keep secrets, you'll soon find Espeon is my efficient little lie detector."

"What do you want to know?" asked Archer dubiously.

"From you? Nothing," Cade replied. "I want to train you."

Archer sneered back. "I'm not an animal."

"Yet," Cade replied, then said to Espeon, "Zap Cannon."

An orb of golden electricity and fire coalesced in midair, like conjured ball lightning, and with a swing of Espeon's head it spun towards Archer and struck him headlong. Searing pain coursed through his body and he cried out, his skin sizzling audibly as he tried to wrest free. The ropes held fast.

"The first part of the training," Cade remarked nonchalantly, "is for you to acknowledge who owns you."

"You fucking asshole..." His offense cut off as he was shocked yet again. Electricity once more assailed with fiery fury, and Archer could not hold his tongue till the pain subsided, leaving a burnt scent in the air and a sour taste in his mouth.

"My associates within Team Rocket," said Cade, "know enough about you to tell me you're one of the syndicate's most loyal admins, with dreams and goals for your organization. That is precisely why I think you're someone I can reason with. You told me you seek the glory of Team Rocket. Isn't that so?"

"Of course I do," snapped Archer, still gasping from the shock.

"Giovanni is destroying your organization," Cade claimed. "He's planning to disband Team Rocket."

"You're lying. Why would he do that?"

"For his son, a certain Ash Ketchum from Pallet Town."

The name 'Ketchum' sounded familiar to Archer. He recalled his godfather Giovanni having mentioned it once, just once, in the context of Delia Ketchum. Did he have a child with her? It was the first Archer had heard of it, but not unlikely.

"Giovanni's giving up on Team Rocket." Cade was adamant. "Why do you think he wants Silph Co. so badly? Because then he can retire. His plan is either to disband Team Rocket, or turn it over to his son Ash. And his son is absolutely one of those self-righteous idealists who believes crime never pays and will tear down the empire without a second thought. All our ancestors will have died futilely and if you don't help me stop it, you will be complicit."

"What do you mean, our ancestors?"

Cade hesitated. A slip of the tongue had revealed, early, far more than he would have liked. But the possibility of what still could be remained tantalizingly in reach and he laughed it off.

"Why don't I let you think that over? We have plenty of time here." He hinted at a threat.

Archer disregarded it. "Till Giovanni sends people to kill you, that is."

His brave comeback was met with another burning electric shock by Espeon. He slumped against the ropes.

Cade didn't reply at all, instead fiddling with the Poké Ball he held till he saw his prisoner's breath steady. "You don't believe our business has rules, do you Archer?"

"No," Archer choked out.

"Then why are you going to play by them?"

Archer didn't know what Cade was aiming at, but he could fathom it was nothing good. He had to bide his time; he only had to endure long enough for rescue.

In the meantime Archer tried to guess what kind of Pokémon was in Cade's Poké Ball. Without holding it himself, there was no way to estimate by how heavy it seemed to be; then again, even the heaviest Pokémon like a Snorlax could easily be carried about, with only slight difference in weight. The way Cade held the capsule, it seemed light, and for a moment Archer even wondered if it was empty before deciding that would serve no purpose here. The Pokémon within it must be something naturally small.

"You don't even agree with half of Giovanni's decisions," Cade was saying. "Why do you abide by them?"

"Giovanni is the leader of Team Rocket."

"Pathetic, the way you go groveling to Giovanni. Do you think he gives a shit about you? Where is he now? Letting you rot in our little dungeon?"

"Giovanni's forces are already on their way. He'd never abandon any of his people."

"Oh really? Do you know how long you've been here?"

A vicious retort faltered in Archer's throat.

Cade did not let the advantage go. "How long do you think you've been here? Weeks? Months?"

When Archer didn't reply, Espeon shocked him. "I'm not sure," he admitted through gasps.

"You've been here longer than you think," answered Cade tersely. "You don't even know for sure how long you were unconscious. Or how long we kept you unconscious."

The implication he'd been drugged brought further doubt into his mind. Archer caught himself involuntarily wondering, Was I really left for dead?

Cade's venomous insinuations began to take form in Archer's tormented mind. Giovanni as leader, and the glory of Team Rocket; weren't the two things inextricable? He'd made a mistake, picturing a rescue at all. He'd made another mistake in believing Team Rocket could never fall.

The worst mistake of all, however, was when he stopped hearing and started listening. For an instant, Cade's words were no longer anathema but logical in their own way. That was when Archer saw his entire worldview as pitifully ridiculous.

And that was when Cade knew it was possible.

"It's one thing to torture a person until they crack. It's another to keep going until they shatter into a million pieces. Do you comprehend my vision?"

Cade grinned evilly.

"We're throwing the shards of glass into the fire and reforging them into whatever we wish. And when they're pulled from the flames they will never be able to return to what they were. You can't imagine how this will turn out for you," Cade added. "I hold your life in the palm of my hand."

Archer could see his fingers tighten around the Poké Ball. Up to a point he wanted him to throw it already. He wanted to know what he was up against. "But not my will," he pointed out with defiance.

He watched Cade draw in a breath. Then with a sweeping gesture, the ropes tethering Archer loosened and fell away via Espeon's psychic energy.

"Sit."

Archer stared at him rather mystified, as if he didn't believe what he'd heard.

Cade made a quick movement with his hand, palm down. "On your knees, on the floor."

"Fuck you," Archer countered.

The gemstone on Espeon's forehead gleamed, and Archer was both seized with pain as well as pulled to his knees violently by psychic force. He winced as he struck the ground, but he was only held down for a moment, long enough to register his sitting position, before the energy pressure lifted away and he was allowed to rise.

Cade kept condescending patience. "Again. Sit."

He shot his tormentor a spiteful look, but Archer saw little point now in fighting the demand further. With measured, reluctant motions, he sat neatly on the floor facing Cade.

"Well done. Now let's see you react faster, with only a signal."

"I'm not your Pokémon," Archer snapped at him, still sitting.

He only succeeded in getting Cade to seize him roughly by the nape of the neck.

"Let me outline it for you, since you're evidently too dumb to reason it yourself. You are the same as the Shadow Pokémon, and you should be happy you're the same. It means if you're obedient, your miserable life actually has some value. Your only purpose is to be used."

"With one caveat," retorted Archer, and despite his fatigue, a remaining spark shone defiantly in his eyes. "I'm a human being."

Cade regarded him coldly. He released him, took a step back, and finally hurled the Poké Ball...

...at him.

The sphere struck his arm lightly, and Archer could only gaze at it for a single incredulous moment before it snapped open and the world flashed into darkness.

Immediately he was in a small room about five paces in all directions, with curved windowless walls divided horizontally by a single thin line, and to one side what looked like a large metal clasp upon a circular indent; as he stood up, he could see the ceiling and the floor each bore a single glowing circle in their center, flooding the room with red light.

It took Archer a moment to deduce what happened. When he did, dread seized him as he remembered what the red light meant.

It was scanning him. It was sequencing his DNA pattern. And he realized he had only a short amount of time before he'd be irreversibly tied to the capsule like an animal.

"No...no, no, no, no." He had to figure out how to get out. He had to get out, damn it!

He raced from one wall to the other in a frenzy. Finding nothing that looked like an escape, he tried to tackle one side of the enclosure. He stumbled against the curve of the wall. It didn't budge.

The red light dimmed before gradually returning to full strength, apparently pulsing slowly.

Then he took notice again of the clasp, off to the side, inching down at intervals like the seconds-hand of a clock.

It was locking.

He was instantly at the latch, trying to force it back up. It was nearly the same height he was, and he grabbed it with both his hands and tugged – and tugged again. Direly weak from the torture he'd endured, Archer struggled futilely.

He had no strength to force it open.

The red light continued to dim and pulse incrementally as he wrenched rearward as hard as he could, the muscles of his arms and back ablaze with pain. His shoes slid on the curved surface of the wall's edge where it met the floor.

His hands lost their grip and slipped off the metal.

"—shit!" Archer cursed as he fell, nearly hitting his head in the process. The clasp continued moving down.

Grabbing hold of the latch anew, he pulled. Everything was awash in the ominous red glow, making it hard to see what he was doing. Heaving back with the last of his might, groaning from strenuous effort, Archer succeeded in halting the large fixture's descent...the mechanism creaked and pushed stubbornly against his force...he held tight...

He lost his grip again. It lurched forwards relentlessly. In a last desperate attempt, he threw his whole body against the clasp, to no avail; with a click, the latch came down fully and locked. The red light scanning him shut off.

Archer screamed in frustrated anguish.

Cade watched the Poké Ball shake a couple of times before it grew still, and the rapidly flickering red light finally shut off having registered a successful capture. The Cipher guards exchanged a glance, mutely horrified at what they'd witnessed, but they knew better than to say a word as he approached the locked Poké Ball and picked it up.

The bright red-and-white sphere was indistinguishable from any other, save for its highly illegal contents. What he'd done was considered a violation of human rights. But after forced experimentation and torture, so what if he committed one more?

Cade smiled indulgently. "Gotcha."

Chapter 15 - The Possibility II

The natural luminosity of refined tumblestone walls imbued the small chamber with a perpetual twilight, so Archer was not in total darkness. It was the kind of mild and warm light that would have otherwise been calming, had it been the parlor of a cabin or a cozy bedroom; here it was but a condolence. He could not tell whether he was up or down or sideways; for his perception he was upright, but it was the same way one could not properly perceive standing on the planet's round face – that much he knew of the inner workings of Poké Balls.

The Poké Ball was locked. Once a Pokémon was successfully captured, no amount of force from inside could unlock the capsule.

Poké Balls are designed to hold in even a Charizard, Archer reflected, letting himself sink wearily to the ground. There's no way I can hope to get out. I have no choice but to wait until someone unlocks it from outside.

Time stretched out strangely, in a manner reminiscent of when he'd been a child, but more so; as if his prison had some bearing on his grasp of time's passage. Hours dragged on ad infinitum and prolonged isolation preyed upon his nerves. At least he could hear what was outside of the capsule. It sounded muffled and drawn out, but still distinguishable, reminiscent of being underwater.

He sat pressed against one of the curved walls, introspective and downcast. The burns left from Espeon's electric attacks still hurt, but not as much as thinking Giovanni would have abandoned him to his fate. His emotions, it seemed, came at moments; flares of despondency and fear that receded as swiftly as they came, and one of the few things that could bring them to the forefront was the thought he'd been forsaken. Archer was starting to believe there was no other explanation for his captivity. As such, he'd have to think of a way to escape by himself.

His chance would come when he was let out. It was a waiting game. Patience was all he needed.

Unfortunately, his nature was one of impatience.

There was nothing to do here. He was alone, and hungry, and cold. He wished he had a blanket. Or food.

He wondered where Houndoom was, and who they'd given him to. He knew fully well how that went; subdue the trainer, and steal the Pokémon. What was new and enigmatic was their apparent interest in keeping him alive.

Why did Cade say he wanted him alive, anyway? To use him? And what did he mean about their ancestors?

...God, he was hungry.

Feeling more despondent than he'd yet been, Archer lay down and tucked himself into a fetal position, trying to keep warm and welcoming the oblivion of dreamless sleep when it came.

He woke who-knows-how-much-time later to a sharp click. Groggily looking up, he noticed the clasp had returned to its unlocked position.

Archer unsteadily scrambled to his feet in time for the sudden black flash, finding himself outside of the Poké Ball in the laboratory office with the columns and the wooden desk. He spun around to find Cade holding the capsule in his hand, a smugly superior look on his captor's face.

Cipher guards immediately sprang to restrain him but Archer, struggling free, struck one and ran for it.

The world briefly flashed black, and suddenly he had to skid and catch himself before he collided with the wall and the lock. He was back in the Poké Ball.

Before Archer could fully come to grips with what had transpired, there was another flash and he was back outside.

This time he lunged straight for the Poké Ball, intending to snatch it away, just as Cade made a quick motion of his hand; the capsule opened instantly and then Archer was within its confines yet again.

Cade held back a snicker as he addressed his captive inside the sphere. "Archer, are we really going to have to play Poké Ball ping-pong like with a newly trapped Pokémon that hasn't been trained? You know fully well how these work. You can't get away."

Archer leant his forehead against the latch. It was true. He was acting like a wild Pokémon that still hadn't learnt who its master was. A wild Pokémon that hadn't wanted to be caught, but had to accept its new reality.

He snapped back to attention when he heard a new voice outside the Poké Ball; it was at a distance so he could not tell what had been said, but he recognized who it was.

Oleana.

Cade swiftly put the Poké Ball aside on the desk and greeted the newcomers with a broad smile. "Mr. and Mrs. Rose! How unexpected."

Archer pressed against the wall to try to hear their conversation better. Rose was speaking to Cade.

"There's been an attempt on our lives. Someone put a bomb to our vehicle and it was only by the grace of God that no one was in it at the time. Oleana spied James and Jessie, two of Giovanni's most notorious elites, and their Meowth at a distance; we sent people after them but by that time they'd already returned to Team Rocket's territory."

"Look at the bright side. At least they failed their mission," Cade dismissed.

"When they tell Giovanni, he'll send more of his people and try again," Rose pointed out dryly.

"There's more..." Oleana added, "One of our top guards was found murdered in an alley alongside Team Rocket's signature rose. Commander Merardi, who'd been stationed here at the laboratory for a time."

"Oh, yes, I do remember him. What a tragic loss," Cade replied with apparent sincerity, whilst trying to figure out which of the henchmen he'd been.

"We heard the agents responsible for that were tracking the Poké Ball shipment from Silph," Rose went on. "Have you seen anyone around here?"

"Around here? Ah...no," Cade prevaricated.

Archer was listening and felt a surge of hope. So Rose and Oleana have nothing to do with this, if Cade's keeping me a secret from them! Then it was some sort of internal power play by Cade, perhaps to overrule Rose in Cipher's ranks? Whatever it was, Archer immediately saw a chance for rescue.

Cade was assuring Rose, "If our people see anyone here, we'll be sure to deal with the situation accordingly."

"I know you're more than capable of it, but in this case I'd prefer you just inform me," answered Rose. "Giovanni's under the impression we've killed his godson, and I don't know what card's up his sleeve but as far as I'm concerned, never mind getting the Mew back...I want no war with Team Rocket under uncertain conditions. At this point I want them to stay on their territory, and we'll stay on ours."

Inside the Poké Ball, Archer was pounding at the wall.

"Help – I'm trapped here! Let me out!" He'd shouted his voice raw before remembering that even if Pokémon could hear the outer world from within their carriers, the outer world could not hear them.

With a surge of desperation, he put all his effort into tackling the clasp. It was futility at its finest. But at least he could draw attention.

Rose motioned to the Poké Ball atop the table, which was shaking. "Oh, it looks like one of the Pokémon wants to come out."

"They're just getting antsy because it's near feeding time," dismissed Cade easily. "Don't worry about it. I'll feed them after you've gone. ...You know we could use stronger Pokémon here just in case some folks from Team Rocket do show up. Perhaps if you left Zacian and Zamazenta here like guard dogs?" he added, silently envisioning how he could use Silph's modified Poké Balls to capture the Legendary wolves for himself when their trainer was not present.

Oleana, in response, gave a forced and acrid smile. "I don't think they'll take kindly to being ordered by anyone but me. If I'm not nearby it's a coin toss whether they'd think of you as a nuisance...or lunch."

Cade's sly grin faltered only a bit.

"Anyway," interjected Rose, "we came by to let you know to keep on the alert for Team Rocket."

"Oh, no need to worry about that. I'm as watchful as a Sentret," Cade told them, casting a second look at Oleana up and down. She had crossed her arms and was starting to appear irritated.

Never imagining the contents of the shaking Poké Ball on the table, Rose and Oleana bid farewell and departed. From inside the sphere, Archer heard their steps receding, and all at once his frustration boiled over into incoherent despair.

When he was sent out again, despair had turned to ire. No sooner did he emerge from the capsule did the guards fall upon him, and having anticipated as much he fought violently.

It was no use. There were too many. One of the guards punched him in the jaw, while others pulled his arms behind his back and he was struck mercilessly till he no longer struggled. Bruised and beaten, Archer was forced to the columns, where he was once again tied up to face a new round of 'training'. Cade watched with unmistakable amusement.

Groaning, Archer lifted his gaze and briefly met Espeon's. Something occurred to him; if Espeon could read his thoughts, then maybe he could talk with it unbeknownst to Cade. He wouldn't have much chance when the interrogation started, but maybe now... He tried to focus his attention on the Pokémon. Espeon? Please, can't you help me get out of here?

Interest briefly lit in Espeon's eyes, as if it realized he was trying to communicate telepathically with it. It was only when Archer gave up trying to send a message when he received a wave of regret.

I obey, master does not throw me to the shadow ray.

I'll protect you from whatever that is, Archer projected back.

You could not protect yourself. How could you protect me?

The answer was enigmatic to Archer. Espeon looked down at its paws, and there was no further communication save for another surge of regret. He would get no help from it.

Cade was already talking. "I presume your reflection has brought you new awareness of your position, and what your continued existence depends on. Perhaps it would help to delineate some facts. One of which is that you're alone."

He held something, and Archer gazed at it for a moment before some part of the memory returned. It was the family photograph from his wallet.

"Some of my contacts within Team Rocket tell me the infant in this picture is your sister Krystal...and she currently works alongside you in Team Rocket. Other than yourself, she's the last surviving member of your family after the hit by the Cadáins to wipe out the Delavitas – isn't that so?"

At a motion from Cade, Espeon brought forth another orb of fire and electricity, but instead of hurling it allowed it to levitate before its trainer. Its sparking, flickering fire illuminated the room in an eerie half-light, causing shadows to dance on the walls. Cade studied the image he held, and then regarded Archer with defined malice.

"We should have eradicated all of you from the face of the planet."

He dropped the image into the flames.

Involuntarily, Archer tried to leap and stop it, but the ropes held him and he could only watch the photograph crumble into cinders. Cade seemed to find entertainment in stirring up his captive's suppressed emotions into a tumult of anguish.

"You don't have a little sister. Your photograph never existed. She died one month before Giovanni established Team Rocket."

Archer felt sick to his stomach. Something about all Cade was doing crossed a line, far beyond even the cruelties his own syndicate would set forth in; Archer was sure he'd thought that before, but in any case he was thinking it now. In the same manner, something about it remained immensely familiar.

"Who are you?" he forced himself to ask.

"My real name is Evice S. Cadáin."

"That's impossible."

"I figured 'Cade' sounds less ostentatious, and it doesn't carry the same connotations of Kanto mob wars my birth surname does. It's better for publicity."

"The Cadáins are all dead."

"I was the youngest of Mr. Cadáin's sons when he sought to seize territory... After Giovanni slaughtered what remained of my family, I fled to Orre. My grandfather was then mayor of Phenac City, and he brought me into the region's political circles to eventually inherit his position. Giovanni, with his oh-so-noble rules, thought it surrender. He never thought of the possibility it was temporary retreat and I'd harbor vendettas too."

Oh, if I could only get loose, thought Archer. "Our families were at peace back then. Your family hit the Delavitas first. Giovanni's vengeance was justified."

"My family saw opportunity. Isn't it right to seize an opportunity where you can? You yourself tried to take the opportunity to escape."

"Why wouldn't I try to escape? I'm being tortured."

"And the Delavitas were making it difficult for my family's business. It's competition."

Something there aligned incomparably, but Archer was too ill to figure out what it was. His breath was ragged and he wished he could lie down.

"The Delavitas neither took advantage of their influence nor realized the extent of it. They still don't. Giovanni wants to take over the world economy. Me...I just want to take over. And if I had control of his militia I could do far more... Giovanni and Rose already loathe each other. I want to keep them at each other's throats. When the two behemoths eliminate each other, then I get to be king. You, Archer Verdi," Cade emphasized at last, "will help me finish the mafia war Giovanni believed he'd ended twenty years ago. The first step is eliminating Giovanni and his blood heirs."

"I'll never go against my godfather," snapped Archer. "Least of all to help a Skuntank like you."

"You have every reason to assist me," replied Cade. "You've always believed not to let past sacrifices go to waste. The glory of your syndicate hangs in the balance; Giovanni will destroy everything you've worked for. Because of that...you want to rule Team Rocket."

"No I don't."

Espeon unleashed another Zap Cannon. Fire and electricity scorched Archer, yet despite his outcries he remained defiant.

"...I will never go against Giovanni!"

Hours went by. For Archer it was ceaseless.

It wore him down steadily, and where others might have repudiated their tormentor's demands outright, his own doubts began to mingle with them and leant their own peculiar credence.

Some part of him still clung to the idea he'd not been abandoned here. He imagined Team Rocket's soldiers bursting in, killing Cade, and pulling him from this torture chamber. Then after a brief recovery he'd be in Giovanni's office talking with his godfather about everything that happened. He'd be told how proud they were of his efforts to hold firm. How it meant something. How they'd never given up on him...

"You want to rule Team Rocket."

Archer was exhausted. It was all a dream, and dreams were nonsensical hallucinations. He wanted it to end already; he wanted the torture to stop one way or the other. Giovanni wasn't coming to the rescue, no one from Team Rocket was being sent to save him, they'd all left him for dead. With a single, weary sigh Archer at last gave in:

"Yes...I want to rule Team Rocket."

Cade glanced at Espeon, which gave a twitch of its ear – and then motioned again towards Archer.

This time Archer was completely unprepared. Agony burned through his body, tearing him into an excruciating spasm, and his mind raced in attempts to grasp at reason.

As if he'd asked the question aloud, Cade answered calmly. "You don't believe it yet."

Comprehension came over Archer with a pall. He stared dumbstruck at Cade, who looked darkly amused.

"Espeon can read your mind, remember? You'll either have to become very clever at hiding your thoughts or give in of your own volition. And I assure you, pain will eventually rule out the former."

"But how can I believe it?" Archer implored.

He got no answer, save for more pain. Now the true horror of his ordeal began. If compliance was not sufficient, then what was the way out? He couldn't force himself to accept a fallacy.

"What an embarrassment. Giovanni can see you're weak, and weakness is useless in our line of business." Cade smirked. "You don't even have the balls to take charge of the organization when you see your dear godfather failing. No wonder he tosses you aside to play babysitter to their cadets."

Cade saw the small wince in Archer's features. He'd hit a nerve with that one. He'd remember and return to it later.

"Admit that you want to rule Team Rocket," reiterated Cade.

Archer tried to believe it. It seemed shameful at first, but his strangely suppressed emotions were swiftly pacified by self-delusion. There was a sense of surprising freedom in not having to fight against what was demanded.

Cade glanced at Espeon, which twitched its tail, and turned back towards Archer with dissatisfaction. "You're trying, which is an improvement. You still have to want to."

"I swear I want to!"

He'd foolishly gambled the lie, and unsurprisingly was met with the immediate attack of Espeon. Fiery pain slashed through him brutally like a knife. He was broiling alive. Smoke twirled at the edges of his sight; he could no longer tell if it was from lightheadedness, or the electricity, or both. It was mercy when he passed out.

Upon seeing Archer's body go limp, Cade tentatively placed a hand on his neck to check for a pulse. He found one; weak, and extremely rapid, but present.

He scowled and recalled Archer to the Poké Ball with the press of a button. He'd wanted to beat his prisoner up a little longer, but wasn't about to risk killing him yet.

Balancing his mayoral duties with his supposed assistance of Cipher's activities – and the furtherance of his own – proved less taxing than Cade had first thought it'd be.

It was already past six when he sat down to eat dinner. It was a lavish meal, which he always tended towards in the evenings, with meat and wines and a centerpiece bowl of various berries imported from outside Orre. In the midst of this feast came an unanticipated telephone call from Silph.

Cade didn't let him get past more than a greeting. "Mr. Silph, I must commend your company on manufacturing such a flawless product. Your Poké Balls work as they should."

"The ones without the fail-safes?" remarked Silph, "I'm not going to ask what you caught."

Cade skirted the implicit question. "A highly regulated species, one proving quite difficult to tame."

"That reminds me of a chat I had with Lance from the Elite Four," Silph remarked amicably. "He trains dragons; they're supposed to be one of the hardest beasts to handle. He says once the Pokémon realizes you feed it, getting it to respond to you is easy."

"...shit, I think I forgot to feed him."

"Well, there you go. The critter's probably just hungry. Listen, Cade, the reason I called was about Giovanni," Silph changed the topic. "Are you sure your people can prevent him from doing something...er...dramatic?"

"You're still worried about Giovanni? I told you he's inconsequential," Cade dismissed.

"He knows about our business deal."

"Does he know about me?"

"Um...no."

"Well then, how can he know about our business deal?"

"He knows Silph Co. is sending illegally modified Poké Balls to Orre. Cade, that's felony-level contraband; those Poké Balls I'm selling you could even be used to trap human beings."

Cade was glad Silph was on the phone and not face-to-face; he thought his smile at that remark would have been far too revealing. "Mr. Silph, you have nothing to worry about, as I've said. Now, I think I ought to feed my new Pokémon, and you have to get your company's next Poké Ball shipment ready. You can expect the bank transfer as usual." He hung up, cutting off Silph's protest.

Archer woke to find himself back in the warm twilight and peaceful solitude of the Poké Ball. After what he'd been through, he was glad to be in here as opposed to being tortured outside. He didn't know how much more suffering he could take.

His heart beat so strongly that it seemed his body shook in response, and he could still taste a tang of blood on the side of his lip from where the guards had punched him. Hunger and thirst had already reached the point where it made the act of moving an agony in itself. Archer didn't want to move anyway. He wanted to rest quietly and pretend he could will away his nightmarish predicament.

He lay there for a long time. He didn't even bother to stand when he saw the clasp unlock; he only shuddered at the thought of what awaited him. As a result, he emerged lying on the floor.

"Get up," ordered Cade.

Archer forced himself to at least sit, though his body shrieked for him to stay reposed. As usual he was in the dimly-lit office with the columns where they conducted their interrogations; Cade stood facing him, with Espeon unfailingly by his side, and guards, but surprisingly no one sprang to restrain him in any way. "You finally decided to let me out of my captivity?" he mustered a confrontation.

"Well just so you see I'm not completely heartless I thought you might need some food and relief," Cade replied.

He snapped his fingers, and one of his men left the room and returned quickly with a tray that held a piece of bread. It was ceremoniously held out in front of Archer and his hunger was so intense that he grabbed hold of it without any prompting.

More desperate than he admitted to himself, he scarfed down the bread only to flinch at immediate stabbing inside his mouth, bad enough to cause him to halt eating till the pain reduced. Apparently the cut was worse than he'd thought.

"Consider yourself fed," stated Cade, "now you need a drink."

He took a flask that was on the desk and a glass from the drawer; promptly filling it to the brim...with water. He handed it to Archer.

The glass of water was heavy, but he held it like a precious possession that could be snatched away from him; he was genuinely worried someone might. It was one of those crystalline drinking vessels carved with a vintage design, which in surroundings not so dark as these would have captured light like a jewel. If it would only reflect that same brilliance here, Archer thought wistfully. He couldn't tell what the design represented. Vines of flowers? Windswept snowflakes?

Archer drank the water. The freshness cooled his mouth and throat and after he had swallowed some of it, Cade spoke up again.

"You're starting to look a little unkempt too. You'll be allowed to shave under supervision."

Snapping his fingers again, two guards took him by the arms and led him to a restroom sink and mirror that was fully equipped with shaving cream and razors. The guards stood on either side of him, aiming guns at his head. "Proceed with it," one of them ordered.

Archer shaved his face. When he was done, he was escorted back to Cade.

"Do you see how far easier it is for you if you cooperate?" Cade asked.

Archer gave him a sideways wary glance, like a feral Pokémon being fed by a strange human. Cade shrewdly added, "I don't want to harm you. I want to teach you."

"Is that why you put me through those torture sessions?"

"They're not torture sessions," corrected Cade, "they're training sessions."

"It seems torturous," Archer couldn't resist saying. "Not to mention how you're locking me in a Poké Ball."

"Poké Balls aren't inherently inhumane, no more than any kind of animal enclosure would be."

That...was true, thought Archer. Confusion muddled the distinction between being a human versus an animal and the rights accorded each. For a moment the cage seemed innocuous. Cade would attempt to cultivate that.

"If anything you should be happy you have a chance to rest from your injuries," he added.

"I'm injured because you injured me," Archer pointed out.

"You injured yourself, through your own disobedience," Cade reprimanded.

Archer didn't answer. What was the point in disputing it? To be punished yet again?

"You need to accept your training faster instead of self-centering on what resulted from your own stupid mistakes. You fainted. So what?" Cade went on, "You're not badly wounded."

Maybe if he had access to adequate medical treatment, Archer could agree to that latter statement. He didn't think he had any broken bones or similar injuries that could not be healed with a mere Potion spray; however, without access to any here Archer worried about infection, generally a non-issue in the modern era considering their world's advanced medicine. He noticed Espeon glance at Cade, and realized the thought had been inadvertently communicated when his captor added:

"Medical care? That's entirely valid. All I want is for you to learn, and if you make a genuine effort, I'll see that you get medical care after. That's not so difficult, is it?"

"I'll try to learn." Up to a point, Archer meant it.

It was a gradual, insidious process. Small concessions here and there didn't matter in the long run, if it allowed him to survive; right? He wasn't compromising anything if he submitted sometimes to his captor.

"And now, you're going back in the Poké Ball."

Archer didn't argue the point and let himself be recalled.

He did feel a little better. At least the bread had quelled some of his hunger, and he guessed there would be no further interrogations till tomorrow – whenever tomorrow was, because he could not tell time here at all. He didn't think much of Cade's assurance of medical care.

Only a few minutes later a wave of energy washed through the walls, surprising Archer, but when it engulfed him he found it to be tranquilizing. As he watched, the bruises and burns on his body faded away, and even the pain from the cut on his lip vanished.

...Heal Pulse? Archer recognized the effects from having seen Pokémon such as Chansey and Audino use it, but never had he witnessed the energy in such a tidal wave.

When the healing energy receded, a familiar chime rang out, and it was only at that point Archer realized he'd been put through the restoring device commonly used in Pokémon Centers.

Judging from the amount of times he'd been fed, and his frequency of shaving, and even presuming he was not granted these privileges often – he already viewed them as privileges; they were only permitted him depending on how well he responded to Cade's trials after all – Archer estimated he had been captive for over a week.

One of the few entertainments available to him within the Poké Ball remained listening to the outer world and trying to guess what was going on around him. He was able to tell Cade carried the Poké Ball around like any other, except for moments when he placed them aside in what Archer thought sounded like a desk drawer. One day, however, he heard something familiar.

It sounded like Houndoom.

His curiosity suddenly returned sweeping emotion – indisputable dread. His Pokémon sounded in distress. He heard Houndoom yelp, and when its yelp turned into howls Archer sprang to tug urgently at the lock. He knew by now it wouldn't budge, but a sense of fear for his pet's life had now overcome him.

The howls receded ominously to whimpers.

It felt like hours later when Archer was sent out to face Cade again. Espeon sat at his captor's heels as businesslike and attentive as ever, and numerous guards surrounded them.

"What did you do to my Pokémon?" Archer pursued.

"The same thing I did to you," Cade replied, "which I intend to do again."

Archer didn't understand, but he realized he wasn't in the typical interrogation room. Instead he was in a wide chamber, with a control panel overlooking a metal table and a large laser of some sort attached to the ceiling. There was something vaguely familiar about the room; Archer couldn't place it, but it made something within him cower.

Cade went on with no shortage of contempt, "I succeeded with Houndoom far faster than the progress I'm making with you. You're disappointing me tremendously; I've had at this charade long enough already, so maybe you need to be put through the process a second round. If you don't survive this time, there's no sense chasing an impossibility."

It was when Archer saw the sadistic gleam in his eyes, not so different from his own at a time long ago, that he became convinced he was truly going to be killed.

When the guards forced him to the metal table, and restrained him tightly upon it, his mind was awhirl in still-shocked emotionlessness. Fleeting thoughts of former colleagues, and Giovanni, and a young trainer with an Eevee. Reminiscences of happier moments that never occurred. As irrelevantly, his thoughts centered back on the drinking glass...the intricate design etched on it, unique and beautiful and fragile.

The sight of the laser pointed at his forehead brought back the twinge of a subconscious memory, forgotten in the depths of a trauma. And suddenly all his distractions and the last of his hopes withered away in the terror of recollection.

"No... stop—don't!"

The exclamation halted everything, save for his heart throbbing painfully, and the world still whirling around him in unrelenting, nauseating vertigo. He fought to form words, and when he successfully did they came out half-stammered and tremulous.

"I can't take the pain any more. Please, I..." His voice trailed away as he gazed up at his tormentor, who was leering down as he leant over him. Archer's eyes were wide and pleading, blue pools filled with fear.

"I'll do any...anything you want."

Cade hesitated, as if considering the request, and then:

"Will you do what I want to stop the pain, or because you want to obey me?"

Archer's gaze flickered involuntarily to Espeon and back to Cade; the mayor regarded him steadily with an expectant look. He had the distinct feeling that no matter what he replied, it would be met with punishment. Weary, and seeing no solution, he relented.

"To stop the pain," he said feebly.

He fully expected to be shocked yet again, either by Espeon or the dreaded energy ray. To his surprise, Cade recalled Espeon.

"Very good. You're learning to be honest."

All at once his emotions swamped him, as if they had been held back by a wall. Archer was shivering uncontrollably and no longer caring if he looked as piteous as he felt. He did not realize when his restraints were loosened, and only vaguely registered when Cade lay a hand on his shoulder almost soothingly. "Would you like a drink of water? You've earned the privilege."

Archer glanced up at him with gratitude. He was being granted a small kindness, and longing for any sort of compassion had finally made him willing to debase himself for it.

When the crystalline cup with the cold water was brought, Archer reached for it, yet his grasp was weak.

The glass slipped from his fingers and shattered to the floor.

Archer was docile now.

Maybe it was beyond self-preservation after all. If Cade held sway over his life and death and the quality thereof, it was only natural Archer should to try to appease him. He realized he wanted to be in Cade's good graces. He wanted kind treatment in the same way he wanted Team Rocket to return to its stolen greatness, even if it meant he'd have to step up to accomplish that himself.

He took his captivity as inevitable. It had been some time he ceased to feel those rushes of fear at the interrogations, and instead cemented his emotionless calm. He would do what he was told.

And really, why wouldn't he want to do as he was told? All he had to do was genuinely want to please.

He became faster at responding to Cade's hand signals. They were directives of when and where and how to act, in lieu of verbal commands. Disobedience was out of the question. Everything he was told made perfect sense now: Giovanni was unwittingly destroying his own organization, and Archer's abandonment by his former colleagues here had helped him see the state of Team Rocket for what it was. Cade only wanted to help him attain his rightful position, to save Team Rocket and help the syndicate regain its former glory before it was too late. Of course he'd have to accept Cade's guidance; any illogic in that was disregarded.

When the trials were over sometimes he'd be praised, and praise usually came with reward. He was fed more frequently now, with hearty meals substituting the bread he'd been given sparingly. The more compliant he was, the more allowances were extended him.

Frequently the Poké Ball was now left unlocked from the outside, allowing Archer to enter and exit at will, but he knew he was expected to remain when recalled and didn't fight it. Nor did he resent when it was locked. He entertained himself with the idea he was like a genie in a lamp; of course the genie must obey its master. Entirely neutral about his state of affairs, Archer began to accept his own subservience willingly like a pleasant dichotomy.

According to Cade, he'd made a great improvement. Houndoom – having already been "converted" – would be returned to him, and he might even be granted a second Shadow Pokémon considering how well he was doing. Archer would have to give them back to Cade whenever he was recalled, since a Poké Ball could not be nested within another Poké Ball, but he'd otherwise have use of his Pokémon when the time came to make their strike against Giovanni.

The final trial was not even announced as such, and came at the end of one of the routine drills; it was unexpected but taken with nonchalance by Archer, and wholly unplanned for by Cade. Instead of recalling his prisoner, Cade merely held out the Poké Ball. Archer lightly reached out and tapped the button, allowing the red glow of light to wash over him as he vanished into the capsule.

Cade no longer tried to hide his glee as he locked the Poké Ball and deposited it in the pocket of his jacket.

It was not only possible. It had been done. He had done it.

Chapter 16 - Delia's Secret

No sooner did Delia Ketchum hear about the encounter her son Ash had with Team Rocket's boss did she resolve to travel to Celadon City. She left in a great hurry and told no one her intent, not even Professor Oak, and arrived at Celadon that morning.

Delia walked up to the receptionist on the ground floor of Rocket Enterprises.

"May I help you?" the girl asked.

"I need to speak with Mr. Giovanni Delavita please," replied Delia, "Which floor is he on?"

"Well, no one is allowed upstairs without an appointment..."

Delia interrupted her, "Please call him and tell him Delia is here and wants to speak with him."

"Ma'am... what is the nature of your visit."

"It is a personal matter. Please call him and let him know I am here."

"Yes, ma'am," replied the receptionist doubtfully.

She picked up the phone, and pushed a button. Immediately, Team Rocket guards came out of doors that were surrounding the area of the lobby.

"This woman is trying to see the boss," the receptionist told them. "She hasn't stated why."

A very tall guard with a mean face approached Delia and said, "Mr. Delavita cannot be disturbed. I suggest you..."

Delia spoke over him in a loud voice and looked at him straight in the eyes, "Let me give you a bit of advice...He will be very angry if he finds out that I was here and was forbidden to see him! ...I am guessing you have seen him angry?"

"What's going on here?" A voice sounded behind them. It was Jessie, and with her were James and their tagalong Meowth walking into the lobby.

"This woman..." the guard began.

"We heard it," said James.

"Let her pass," ordered Jessie, "or the boss will declare you an enemy."

The guards all looked at each other nervously and backed off.

Delia looked at the receptionist, who was visibly frightened and said, "My name is Delia Ketchum. Don't forget it."

At this point Jessie and James spoke up.

"Miss, we will be happy to escort you to our boss' office," said James.

"It's in the penthouse...top floor," added Jessie.

"Thank you."

They led her to the elevator, up to the top floor, and escorted her to the doorway of Giovanni's office. The door was open, and Giovanni was talking with his large cat, Persian.

"Maybe we ought to let Mr. Rose think over what happened before we try anything else...I don't know. What do you think...?"

Persian replied with a series of meows, and Giovanni listened intently and nodded once or twice. The dialogue Giovanni was having with Persian was two-way; Delia smiled in reminiscence.

"You still understand Persian," she said.

The boss of Team Rocket glanced up suddenly and, the moment her eyes met his, returned her smile.

Jessie and James knew this was their cue to leave. They turned and walked away to the elevator, hand in hand, with Meowth chasing after them.

"Persian acts as my counsellor," Giovanni explained. "Pokémon are more trustworthy than people."

"Yet you like to say Pokémon are just tools for business."

"Except for Persian. Persian is more than that. He's part of the family."

Delia still stood at the doorway, and Giovanni suddenly realized it.

"Perdonami amore mio!" he apologized, "I haven't asked you in! I'm so eager to speak with you."

He stood up and quickly walked over; putting his hand on her back, he guided her over to an armchair gesturing to it for her to sit, which she did.

"Gio, there is something I need you to help me with..." Delia began.

"Anything." There was a ferocious absoluteness to the way Giovanni said it as he sat on the corner of his desk facing her, "What problem do you need to go away?"

"No Gio, it's nothing like that," she hurried to explain.

"I told you once that I'm here for you no matter what you need, and I still say that." Giovanni paused. "You know that I've always loved you."

She blinked with shared emotion. "I've always loved you too. Everything changed, Gio…even when we didn’t want it to."

He got up and taking her by the arms, pulled her gently out of the chair and hugged her close, kissing her cheek tenderly.

"It feels so good to have you in my arms again," murmured Giovanni, as he stroked her hair, "Delia, come back to me. We can start over..."

"Yes, Gio, I think the time is finally right for us...but I must talk to you about something. You might know by now," she said, lifting her eyes to look at him directly, "my son Ash has started on his trainer's journey."

"We've already met," Giovanni replied, "He seems to have made the unfortunate acquaintance of the two who escorted you here as well."

Dread seized her. "You can't let them harm him!"

"Delia..." began Giovanni.

"He's your son!" Delia finally exclaimed.

Giovanni stared at her.

"He's your son," Delia reiterated, feeling weary all of a sudden. "I haven't told him you're his father yet."

"Somehow, I always knew," he replied. "I figured you would address it when the time was right."

They were both silent for a while, and then Giovanni spoke again. "Delia, I would very much like for you to have lunch with me today."

"I'd like that," she answered.

He picked up the phone receiver on his desk and summoned his chauffeur who arrived within a short time. They went downstairs, crossed the lobby, and as they climbed into the limousine, Giovanni took Delia in his arms and kissed her.

Still holding her in his arms, he spoke with the driver. "Drive to Federico's and wait outside till we're finished."

"Yes, sir."

They drove for about fifteen minutes and arrived at the restaurant. As they went in, Giovanni was greeted happily by the head waiter. "Mr. Delavita, sir... So nice of you to come see us today."

"Hello, Tony... My usual table please."

The man led the way to a permanently reserved table at the back, where Giovanni pulled the chair out for Delia himself, as the waiter did for him.

It was a very elegant establishment with waiters wearing black and white uniforms and white silk gloves to serve the food. The tables were set with real silver utensils and the plates were all crystal. Flower bouquets adorned the tables, which the waiter retrieved when they were seated.

"This is a really nice place, Gio," Delia commented.

"Glad you like it, my dear. You deserve the best, and I intend to see you get it," he replied. At this point the waiter came and took their order.

"Bring a bottle of the best champagne you have, and two goblets," Giovanni ordered.

"Yes sir," answered the waiter, and left.

There was a moment of silence. Giovanni then took Delia's hands in his and they looked into each other's eyes. Delia's heart skipped a beat, and Giovanni squeezed her hands a bit and said:

"Delia... I have never loved any woman as much as I love you. I ask you now what I planned to ask years ago... Delia, would you marry me?"

Her eyes filled with tears of joy, and she smiled. When she found her voice her reply was brief. "Yes, Giovanni... I will marry you."

He kissed her hands, "We shall go together to buy the engagement and wedding rings...you shall have whichever you want."

At this point, the waiter arrived with the champagne and glasses; he opened the cork, filled the two cups, and left anew.

Giovanni lifted his glass in a toast, "To our happiness."

"To our happiness," repeated Delia, clinking her glass to his.

Soon, their lunch was served and as they ate they talked about how to break the news to Ash.

"Imagine, Gio!" Delia exclaimed, "I first tell him you are his father, and then tell him that we're getting married."

Giovanni shrugged his shoulders, "L'amore e dolce, cara mia. He's not a child anymore. He'll understand."

"I suppose you're right."

"Why don't you both come to the mansion tomorrow for dinner," Giovanni said.

"All right. Then that's when I'll tell him about us."

They finished their meal, returned to the limousine and Giovanni dropped Delia off at her home, with a kiss and a promise to call her that evening. Delia went into the house and watched from her window as the car drove off.

Her world was finally becoming truly joyful.

Ash returned to Lavender Town with the Cubone, which he took to the Pokemon Center. There it was reunited with its mother the Marowak. Content that he at least had helped these Pokémon, he and Pikachu headed on their way.

They were now en route to their next gym battle. That happened to be in Fuchsia City, which was a long way from here. Still, after the easy way in which Ash won against the Celadon gym, his spirits were bolstered and the loss against the Vermillion gym – which he still had to return to challenge – was put out of his mind. Even the annoyance of not being able to access Saffron City was momentarily pushed aside – he'd get to it eventually but it was a future problem.

From Celadon, the quickest way was a long street heading towards Fuchsia with an adjoining bicycle path sloping downwards. It was known as Cycling Road. However, Ash did not have a bicycle. He had an idea to buy one back at Cerulean City, but the prices were exorbitant and he airily declared to Pikachu that before spending half a fortune on a bike he'd sooner walk the whole way. That was being put to practice now. With no way onto the shortcut of Cycling Road, he was forced to take the longer pedestrian path of route 17 called Pokémon Road, and that promised to be no shorter than a full two-week's trek through forest trails and meadowland. Signs at the beginning of the route warned hikers to pack accordingly.

Ash made the best of it, however. The route had beautiful foliage especially now in autumn, and berry trees grew in abundance alongside the road. He also knew this was one of the few areas in the Kanto region where wild horses known as Ponyta and Rapidash could be found, and after three days of walking with no town in sight he made up his mind that if he should happen across one he would make a concerted effort to catch it and ride the rest of the way to Fuchsia.

That afternoon they made camp in a thicket clearing not far from the main trail. While Ash chopped wood for the campfire, Pikachu had found an acorn and began batting it around playfully; when Ash finally settled down to cook, Pikachu scampered over and sat beside him.

He had stocked up before leaving Celadon. He was roasting some sausages for himself, and had kibble for Pikachu. That said out here it was easy to live off the land. Pikachu in particular loved the wildness of the route; occasionally it would dart into the bracken and emerge with berries to share.

Rustling bushes made Ash glance up, distracting him briefly from the food, and as he watched a Pokémon lifted its head from the bracken.

It was an Eevee.

Wild Eevee were exceptionally rare in these parts. Ash observed it without making any sudden movements. Sniffing the air, the animal padded towards the campfire and the meat roasting over it.

The Eevee snatched a sausage.

"You're hungry, I see," Ash said.

The Eevee squeaked as a reply, and was tame enough that it allowed him to pet it. "You can't be a wild Pokémon, can you?" Ash surmised.

His question was answered immediately by a female voice calling through the trees:

"Eevee...! Where are you?"

She looked about his age, with teal hair picked up into two ponytails and bright blue eyes. The moment she saw them, she deduced what had happened.

"Oh, I'm sorry! Did Eevee steal some of your food?" she asked apologetically.

"No, we're happy to share," smiled Ash. Pikachu, sitting beside him, gave an equally friendly chirp.

"My name's Ash."

"My name's Kris," she responded gathering Eevee into her arms.

"Are you also challenging the Pokémon League?"

"Well, sort of. I'd actually been gathering badges from the Johto region. But I got sidetracked."

She looked sad about an unspoken memory, but then shook it off when Ash asked, "Would you like to join us? We've got plenty of food here, enough to share."

"Well..." Kris started to say, hesitant, but Eevee gave a cheery cry and gave a little hop out of her grasp to join Pikachu beside the campfire. She smiled. "I guess it won't do any harm."

Over the meal, Ash and Kris chatted about their respective voyages. "I figured I'd travel around Kanto for a while and take in the sights," Kris told him. "Autumn is such a pretty season, don't you think? So I decided to take the long way to Fuchsia City to see the zoo."

"Oh yeah that's right, Fuchsia City has the Safari Zone. I've never been there," Ash remarked. "We're heading to challenge the gym. I know they specialize in poison types, so I probably should stop by the mart before going there and stock up on Antidotes."

"You could also get a bunch of Pecha berries," Kris said. "I saw a grove of them down the trail. Pecha berries are a natural antidote against attacks from most poison type Pokémon."

Pikachu gave a chirp, and Eevee replied with its own cry. Both Ash and Kris laughed, and then glanced at each other in fair surprise.

"You understand your Pokémon too?"

Yes!" Kris exclaimed, "I guess when we treat our Pokémon like family we end up so bonded that we understand their language."

"That's true," Ash nodded his head.

They were quiet for a while, mulling their thoughts, and then Ash spoke up, "Since we're both heading in the direction of Fuschia City, maybe we could walk along together?"

It was phrased as a question but Kris detected wishful thinking on Ash's part, almost a hidden shyness.

"Sure," she smiled, "Thats a great idea!"

After that the two of them journeyed the rest of the way. They found in each other ideal travelling companions, and Pikachu and Eevee enjoyed playing and occasionally sparring with each other too.

They had made camp for the night when Eevee nudged Kris awake.

"...hmm? Eevee? What's wrong?" Kris asked drowsily.

Ash and Pikachu were fast asleep, and the forest was resolutely peaceful. The faint hooting of a Noctowl competed with the nighttime ballad of Kricketune.

Eevee was staring intently at the bracken. As Kris watched, she saw the sudden gleam of a Pokémon's eyes behind the leaves and – before she could do anything – the swish of a Meowth's tail.

Suddenly realizing who was there, and being cautious not to wake Ash, Kris stepped lightly over to the bracken and behind a large tree.

She found who she expected to find: Jessie, James, and Meowth.

"Hi Kris," purred Meowth nonchalantly.

"What are you doing here? Did Giovanni send you to keep an eye on me and make sure I don't do something reckless?" Kris asked with a tinge of affront.

"Shh! Keep your voice down!" Jessie said.

"The boss doesn't even know we're here," James told her honestly.

Kris blinked. "Then...?"

"Quick question, does the twerp still have his Pikachu out of its Poké Ball?" asked Jessie, her eyes darting towards the campsite.

"Ash?" Kris echoed, perplexed. "Yeah, I don't think he ever puts Pikachu in its Poké Ball."

Jessie grinned. "Perfect."

"What's going on?" asked Kris.

"Can't tell you. It's top secret."

"And our secret tops them all," James chimed in.

"Top cats only," purred Meowth.

"Whatever. Look as long as I'm not in trouble with the boss or anything."

Meowth gave a yowl. "You travelling with the twerp now?"

"I figured, why not? At least until I reach Fuchsia City," she added, "It takes my mind off things."

"Well, stay out of the way when we get involved," Jessie replied. "Trust me, you'll know when."

Kris hesitated. "You're planning a hit?"

"More like a heist."

"We want his Pikachu," James admitted.

Jessie elbowed him sharply. "Way to spill our secret, James."

"His Pikachu? What's so special about his Pikachu? You know they're a dime a dozen out in Viridian Forest."

"It's the principle of the thing. We don't want any Pikachu; we want the twerp's Pikachu. You're still a rookie recruit, Kris. You have time to learn."

"Just keep quiet around that twerp and pretend we never let it slip about our Pikachu pilfering," James added.

Meowth was far less oblique, bearing his fangs in a hiss. "If you tell him you're a snitch and a traitor."

"I'm no snitch or traitor," Kris answered. "Team Rocket has my loyalty, you know that."

Satisfied with her response, they disappeared into the bracken. Kris shot them a dubious look as she returned to where Ash and the Pokémon were.

Chapter 17 - Pitfall Trap

The trees were already aflame in autumn's maturity, their blazing shades of red and gold intermingling with the fickle light-green of summer's fading youth. It was one of those bright fall afternoons when the sun's warmth and brilliance played amidst cold breezes and infrequently brought leaves down in a cascade, where the day's insistence of dragging on compensated through outward beauty, and neither the splendour of the foliage nor the peace of routine failed to belie the many schemes about to be set in motion.

Waylaying their enemies was Team Rocket's favorite attack strategy, or at least the favored strategy of Jessie and James. It gave them the chance to scout out a battle site as well as plan the best type of ambuscade. They decided to keep to something tried and true for Ash, which would allow them to see his aghast reaction when they pounced – just out of gleeful revenge.

Meowth had gone off who-knew-where again and returned as they were finishing their insidious set-up.

"Another pitfall trap?" hissed Meowth, clearly unimpressed as he flattened his ears at it. "Don't you two knuckleheads remember what happened last time we did that?"

"Didn't we succeed at our mission?" asked James airily, as they dragged branches to cover the ditch.

Meowth refreshed their memory with a growl. "You fell into your own trap. Both of you."

"This time is different," James purported.

"Yeah Meowth – who says we don't learn from our mistakes?" insisted Jessie. "Don't you think we're smarter than that?"

The cat did not answer this and merely stared at them with his ears still flat.

"Someone's coming! Let's hide," said Jessie, and they all leapt into the bushes.

Strolling down the forest path were none other than their targets – the "twerp" with the Pikachu prize. With him was none other than Kris.

Ash and Kris were animately discussing something as they walked by, and James and Jessie instinctively crouched lower behind the cloak of bracken.

Ash was complaining. "We're running late damn it. We should be farther along than we are!"

"It'll work out...stop worrying so much!" responded Kris.

Meanwhile, the Team Rocket trio was assessing the situation.

"They're standing right on top of the hole; why the fuck don't they fall in?" hissed Meowth.

"James, you reinforced it too much," remarked Jessie with a tinge of accusation.

"I reinforced it too much?" James countered.

"Quit your yakking before they hear us!" screeched Meowth.

Ash, Kris, and even Pikachu however were oblivious to the trio and continued talking. The Pikachu chimed in with a squeak.

"See that?!" Kris said, "even Pikachu says you are a worrier."

"Since when do you understand Pikachu?" Ash countered.

"Didn't I translate it right?" Kris demanded.

Ash scowled at her, but reluctantly grumbled, "You translated it right."

Back behind the bushes, the trio persisted with their analysis of the work at hand.

"We don't have a problem," James assured, "At least we planted those firecrackers around the edge of the pit."

"When did we do that?" Jessie asked.

"When you were touching up your lipstick Jessie," he teased.

"Well...beauty comes first," she said in a similarly coquettish way.

"All we've got to do is press this button," James added, revealing a small remote control. "This sets off the fireworks..."

Meowth's eyes lit up. "...and down goes the prey!" the cat meowed excitedly. "Push it!"

"...later," said James. Meowth flattened his ears again.

"Let's just relax, and enjoy it all," Kris said.

Ash sighed, "I guess you're right Kris."

Hidden behind the bushes, Jessie and James were watching with riveted frustration.

Meowth bared fangs. "Press the damn button!"

"Not yet," James objected.

"We need to wait for the right moment." Jessie remarked.

"Gimme that button," hissed Meowth, outstretching a paw.

"No, Meowth," James said indifferently, lifting the remote away from the cat."

" They're over the fucking pit. Push the button already!"

"Oh, Meowth," dismissed Jessie, "if they step away we'll just follow and hit them over the head the old fashioned way."

"Can't believe you two, watching this stupid conversation like a damn soap opera."

Meanwhile, Ash and Kris had sat down to rest and had quieted down.

"I think we should get going," Ash remarked, "I want to get to town before evening sets in."

"You're right" Kris agreed, "I'm ready," she added getting up.

Meanwhile, the Team Rocket trio had had enough.

"So, are we all in agreement the time is now?" said Jessie.

"Let's go!" affirmed James.

"Yeah. Please push the button," replied Meowth emphatically.

In a swift motion, they did.

Suddenly firecrackers exploded in a circle about the ground, and with a unified cry of shock Kris leapt narrowly back while Ash and Pikachu fell into the trap.

With an exclamation of gleeful triumph, Jessie and James sprang to the edge of the pit. They could see Ash scrambling amidst the branches at the bottom of the ditch, and he could not regain his footing before Pikachu was swept up into a net.

"Give back Pikachu, you thieves!" exclaimed Ash.

"Nice doing business with you, twerp," sneered Jessie as she walked away with the captive Pikachu.

"Yeah, you oughta consider yourself lucky!" Meowth purred, padding after her.

"Lucky?" Ash could barely believe the assertion.

"We're letting you live," explained James snidely, tossing the rose into the ditch towards them. Ash caught it by the stem, narrowly missing the thorns, as James strolled after his companions.

"You're not getting away with this, Team Rocket!" Ash shouted after them.

Above, Kris now peered over the edge of the pit uncertainly at him, and Ash practically sprang with hope. "Kris, stop them!"

She looked rather embarrassed. "Ash, this might come as a shock to you..."

"They're getting away with Pikachu," he insisted desperately.

"I'm part of Team Rocket," confessed Kris.

Ash was left wordless for a long moment before finally uttering:

"You mean the whole thing was some kind of a sick setup?"

"I didn't know they were going to ambush you, honest!" exclaimed Kris.

He only stared at her, looking utterly betrayed. Kris sighed somewhat regretfully.

"Sorry, Ash," she said, and slipped out of sight.

Jessie, James, and Meowth strolled down the path to a clearing bend in the road by a cliff, feeling utterly pleased with themselves. Pikachu, to the contrary, was utterly annoyed. It let out sparks in a futile attempt to break free.

Jessie addressed the captive little creature. "Don't be so upset. You'll be much happier with the boss than that twerp. ...or at least we'll be much happier with our bonus," she acknowledged with a sly smile.

"I know we left the hot-air balloon parked around here somewhere," said James, searching the area.

Suddenly there was a gust of wind, and they stopped as a large black helicopter landed lightly at a distance. As a group of lower-rank Team Rocket agents streamed out of the helicopter, their superior hopped down to meet the trio.

"Archer?" James remarked with surprise. "You're alive?"

"The boss sent me on a special assignment," said Archer.

"But he told everyone you were dead," added an astonished Jessie. "He even told us to hit Cipher back for it."

"Forewarned, forearmed," came Archer's easy reply, "It was necessary to keep things secret. I didn't expect you here at all." There was a tinge of something bitter in his tone, perhaps envy.

"Did he send you after this Pokémon?" Jessie asked, a little downcast at how their plan for a surprise gift was being upended.

"You can just give my subordinates the Pikachu. Where's its trainer?" Archer asked impatiently.

"We got him stuck in a ditch back there," responded James, pointing down the path as Jessie dutifully handed over their prize.

"That will make it easy. Good work...you won't be required anymore."

At a sharp signal his soldiers and their animals turned, weapons and fangs bared respectively, to encircle James, Jessie, and Meowth. The shock took a moment to sink in for them.

"The three of you have always been too soft – and too loyal to Giovanni. All that's left is to eliminate the don and his heir," Archer grinned, "and I will rule Team Rocket!"

"You two-timing traitor!" Jessie seethed.

Archer did not hesitate. "Shadow Wave – blast them off!" he called to Houndoom with a wave of his arm.

With a howl, a wave of energy shook outward from Houndoom in a concentrated tremor. Before Jessie or James or Meowth could react a jagged line splintered across the ground, pulling the earth upwards in a sudden explosive force, and suddenly the three of them were hurled into the sky.

They were barely able to register when their flight reversed into a plummeting descent over the precipice. Everything twirled about inconceivably in midair; the sky and the trees, the impaling rocks below, the buffeting rush of wind. Instantly James struck out with the whip to seize hold of one of the rocky outcrops, halting his fall just as he caught Jessie by the hand, and she managed to grab Meowth by the tail.

They held on tightly and crept carefully back to the cliff top, still trying to catch their breath. No one noticed them as they watched the scene unfold from behind a boulder: Archer's group forcing Ash into the helicopter at gunpoint before flying off.

James was first to speak, his mind still spinning. "What just happened?"

"I don't know but I'm sure if we ever have to do that again it'll be the death of us," Jessie replied wearily.

"You guys speaking for yourselves? I'm the one who got my tail yanked," Meowth hissed.

"Oh don't throw a hissy fit," countered Jessie, "you've got nine lives and you'd be one short if we'd all crash-landed."

To which Meowth gave an ornery ffftt.

"I can't believe it," Jessie was saying, "Archer is a turncoat?"

"Giovanni's own godson," James thought it over briefly. "Jessie...what could he have meant by the don's heir? Giovanni doesn't have children as far as I know."

"I don't know, but Archer's got to pay for making us look like fools." Jessie clenched a fist.

Meowth chimed in with a caterwaul. "And we've gotta stop him before he gets Giovanni!"

"But first things first," James began, and Jessie finished his sentence adamantly, "...we're getting back our Pikachu!"

In the midst of this, Kris came running over to where they were. "I hid behind a tree back there," she said, halting before them, "I can't believe it; my brother's alive, but... Are you all okay?"

"We're fine, but Archer won't be for long if he's really planning to overthrow the boss," James said.

"Archer's not a traitor," Kris insisted, "I don't believe it."

Jessie squinted at her. "Well if he's not, then a ghost Pokémon possessed him. He's talking treason."

Meowth scratched behind an ear with a hind paw and gave his comments. "You two are jumping to conclusions. If those Cipher folks in Orre are able to produce Shadow Pokémon, maybe what we've got is a Shadow Human."

Jessie thought about this. "That's impossible."

"Is it, really?" considered James. "Jessie, supposed he's been brainwashed."

"Then he's a victim, not a traitor," reasoned Jessie. "Damn it, why can't things ever be straightforward?"

"We'll find out what's happened when we go after them. The people with Archer dropped this when they were pulling Ash out of the pitfall trap," Kris chimed in, showing them a crumpled handwritten note.

James took the note from her and the trio read it silently. "Kris," said Jessie, "we'll handle this. Go tell Giovanni what's going on."

Kris looked a little disappointed to not come along for the fight but she nodded briskly and, sending out Suicune, mounted the Pokémon's back and raced away. Jessie turned back to the note.

"So they're heading to the Kanto power plant."

Chapter 18 - Trial by Fire

Secluded in the farthest reaches of Route 10, along the narrow canyon river that snaked past Rock Tunnel and opened out into the ocean beyond Lavender Town, was the regional power plant that supplied electrical energy to the entirety of Kanto. It was hydro-powered, with a massive turbine run by a waterfall downriver. The untamed fields outside were a haven for electric Pokémon, and trainers would come by sporadically to hunt them. Other than this, the power plant was only frequented by those who worked there. At this hour, the employees at the main building had already gone home and not even a single security guard would be on duty that night.

Ash had never been to the area. It was such an out-of-the-way place, a veritable side quest; with his hurry to collect all gym badges in time for the League opening this year, Ash had figured it to be unnecessary for the furtherance of his career, though he did plan to make a trip there at some point when he felt less urgency. Never had he imagined he would be brought there, the hostage of a man whose aspirations he would soon come to learn.

Archer had collected a few favors of his own from certain regional officials and had gained access to a semi-abandoned annex separate from the main area of the power plant, so isolated not even Team Rocket were aware of its existence. It was of the days when the power plant had generated its energy from coal, mined from the depths of the Rock Tunnel, and had been the boiler-house for the furnaces.

Faceless concrete and the drab grey of cinder-blocks enclosed a wide, windowless factory. Imposing cylinders within towered two-stories high, the mills that had once pulverised coal powder to be fed to an even more ominous contrivance: a behemoth, rectangular pillar of metal that stood threateningly to conceal its purpose. Overhead metal walkways stretched through crisscrossed iron, old pipes, and concrete columns of ceiling supports. Even the ghost type Pokémon and Ratatta had forsaken dwelling here; this was how abandoned and lifeless the boiler-house was.

Ash did not dare speak at all. He was encircled by armed guards, his wrists bound by rope as he was pushed roughly down the path; meanwhile Pikachu was carried along still helplessly trapped in the net. Archer led the way through the concrete maze till they were brought before the giant metal pillar.

"Do you know what this is?" Archer asked mildly.

"No," answered Ash.

He proceeded to explain, maintaining the equable demeanour of instruction:

"This was the coal boiler. Boiler is a misnomer – it's a giant oven, which once heated water pipes running inside it to create steam to run the generator turbine. Nowadays it serves no purpose for the power plant, and the region intends to dismantle all this eventually."

He opened a latched metal viewing door on the side, and revealed not only the coal powder still blanketing the interior but also the switch beside the view-port. When he snapped it on, a ripple of whitish energy covered the opening like a screen, and dissipated as he switched it back off.

"This is similar to the technology used in Poké Balls," said Archer. "The barrier kept the heat from escaping, but allowed workers to visually ensure the blaze was at a proper level."

Ash was wondering where this was going, and starting to worry it might not be so irrelevant to his plight.

"The strength of the fire could be regulated by this dial," Archer went on, "and was ignited by a gas burner. Much like a conventional oven, but on a far larger scale. The burner doesn't work anymore."

He finished his explanation tersely, and looked expectantly at his Houndoom. As if following an unstated command, Houndoom shot a stream of fire into the open view-port, igniting the powdered coal bed into a carpet of flame.

Ash watched the fire shimmer, first to a snarling bonfire and then, at a mere twist of the dial, down to fine embers flickering and flitting like faeries within the coal sand.

"Technology is incredible, isn't it?" Archer commented genially, drawing Ash's attention back to him. He gave an approving nod to his subordinates. "I can handle this from here. You may leave."

The guards dipped their heads and exited dutifully, leaving the restrained Ash and Pikachu alone with Archer.

"Shadow Hold," Archer addressed Houndoom sharply, and with a violet glint of the dog's eyes, a shining energy washed over Ash. He flinched, but it settled quickly and dissipated from view, leaving his body weak.

Archer offered a brief explanation. "Shadow Hold is like the attack called Mean Look. In case you haven't fought many dark and ghost types, Mean Look prevents its target from escaping – more precisely, from moving more than a few paces. You're staying put."

Considering his hands were already tied behind his back, the need for added restraint perplexed Ash. He glanced from the flames to Houndoom; the fire's glow highlighted something strange about the Pokémon's features, which Ash realized all the Pokémon accompanying his captors shared. The creatures reacted with a dull obedience that toggled rapidly to sharp aggression, so different from most Pokémon Ash knew. Pikachu, still hopelessly ensnared, seemed unnerved by them.

Even Archer himself, Ash noticed, shared that expression of impassivity bordering on disdain, as if tainted by the remnants of some unknown trauma.

At that moment, another man joined them and stood observantly at a distance. When Archer glanced towards him, the newcomer gave a small nod.

"My name is Archer Verdi," said Archer, turning back towards Ash, "My overseer is Mayor Evice S. Cade."

'Overseer' is kind of an odd choice of word, thought Ash. By now steadily growing concerns brought him courage to speak. "What does Team Rocket want with us?"

"Team Rocket?" Archer echoed. "They want whatever Giovanni wants. You are not a prisoner of Team Rocket."

"That's hard to believe," Ash replied, fidgeting against the ropes.

"As I said," Archer clarified coldly, "you are not a prisoner of Team Rocket. You are a prisoner of mine."

Ash looked at him in mute surprise.

"Those two clowns who set the trap for you...Jessie Scordato and James Marchesi...they were representatives of Team Rocket. I represent what Team Rocket will be," said Archer. "My goal is to take over the syndicate as its new don. And you, Ash Ketchum of Pallet Town, stand in my way."

"Look, I don't know what you mean. I've got no stake in this. Let me and Pikachu go."
