"You have a very large stake in it. I don't appreciate being less than the majority shareholder of an enterprise."

"If you want to be leader of Team Rocket, go ahead. We don't have anything to do with it," said Ash. "If Pikachu and I..."

"You care a lot about Pikachu, don't you?" Archer interjected with observation.

Ash hesitated, and then the force of his apprehension wavered. No, he was imagining this; his mind was painting dark figments of fancy, probably having watched too many sensationalised gangster films or heard too many exaggerated tales of Team Rocket's misdeeds. There was no one so evil, so cruelly cold-hearted. So he answered with honesty:

"Pikachu's my childhood friend. I probably care about him more than I do myself."

Archer considered this thoughtfully but did not respond.

"Please let us go," Ash ventured again. "We haven't done anything to you."

Archer glanced from Ash to Pikachu. From where it was trapped in the net, the little animal gave an inoffensive squeak. "Pikaaa..."

"And someone so entirely worthless as a trainer," continued Archer, ignoring Ash's statement as he faced Pikachu, "with a Pokémon little more than a house-pet, appears from obscurity and cuts in line for the throne. Don't tell me you're crossing paths with Team Rocket by coincidence. There's no such thing. Destiny is already set, Ash Ketchum, and I am the one who will take over from Giovanni."

His eyes lifted briefly towards Cade; when Ash followed the motion he saw Cade give a hand signal, the gesture slight and swift and missable. Archer's eyes fixed again on Pikachu.

"You think you're strong enough to weave a different destiny?" added Archer calmly.

In a sudden motion Archer threw Pikachu into the furnace. In the same motion he hit the switch to bring up the energy barrier – preventing Pikachu's escape.

What followed were more screams than squeals. The little animal writhed as flames sprang to consume it; Ash shouted but, kept immobile from Houndoom's attack, could only bear horrified witness as his pet struggled and cried in the depths of a fire far more concentrated than any brief ember on a battlefield. Archer, in turn, watched him. And Cade watched all three of them, the subtle malice of a smile playing at his lips.

"Do you know it's actually possible for a living thing to incinerate while alive?" added Archer, still lecturing with that terrible mildness. "Not just alive, but in full conscious faculty..."

"Stop, please!" Ash pleaded, distraught.

"You know the coal covering its fur is only going to make it worse," observed Archer. "It'll be roasted like a brisket of Tauros."

"Make it stop!"

Archer twisted the dial into a small inferno.

"What do you want from us?" implored Ash.

"I want you to realize the futility of your efforts. I want you to realize destiny is mine and you should have stayed out of it."

The simple statement whirled violently in Ash's mind, torment without solution set against the backdrop of racked cries and that terrible image: a gleam of gold fur in a cast of unrelenting fire. There was a sickeningly burnt smell. He wrenched his gaze away in distraught anguish.

Archer forced Ash to look back, pulling him forward so hard that the nerves affected by Houndoom's energy stabbed in a strained, numb protest to this motion being imposed.

"No. Watch," Archer snarled, "Watch as your piteous electric rat gets barbecued to death. And know if you had any influence at all, you could have saved it."

"No..." answered Ash, and in a strange moment, he lifted his gaze to look directly at Archer and his voice acquired unusual calm, "...you could have saved yourself."

Ash's eyes had acquired a profound cold look; reminding Archer of someone else. Giovanni.

The remark and its delivery stunned Archer by how unexpected it was. It was enough for him to release his hold on Ash, and his captive once more turned away from the sight before him but continued to speak.

"You're already deep in debt. But the day you kill any of my friends..." Ash turned to face Cade, his voice suddenly bitter, "I'll personally make you pay."

Cade stared at him for a moment, something akin to a brief hesitance of doubt; then amusement soared in his eyes instead and he laughed long and loud.

"How funny...!" sneered Cade, at last speaking. "Junior thinks he can be scary like his dad."

Ash stared at him, fury unabated despite being mystified at Cade's words.

"Don't claim you don't know. Don't pretend to be naïve." Cade walked over and leant closer to him with incisive menace. "Someone of your distinguished heritage can't pull that off even if they tried... son of Giovanni Delavita."

The words were met with stunned disbelief within which came nothing to say. Finally Ash spoke again, his voice mired with concentrated hatred.

"Take Pikachu out of there."

Neither moved; Cade and Ash faced each other steadily, Pikachu's squeals growing fainter. Archer watched Cade expectantly and, at last, Cade gave him the awaited signal in a flourish, and Archer switched off the fire.

Ash shuddered and leant his body against the metal casing of the boiler. It was astonishingly cold; so cold it was nigh impossible to believe such furious fire could be kindled within. He looked from Pikachu lying limp in the coal dust to Archer, and then to Cade.

It was Cade directing all this, then. He was pondering this fact as Cade spoke. "You're very observant, aren't you, little Delavita?"

"I'm not Delavita," said Ash.

"No, you're not," agreed Cade. "You're Ash Ketchum, known in his small town as Red, and if you were half as skilled a trainer as your father Giovanni you'd probably never have been caught. None of which will make a difference when they find your dead body."

"I don't understand why you'd do this."

"You're not meant to understand. Why must I have the misfortune of explaining to simple-minded people?" lamented Cade patronisingly.

He meant it rhetorically. He scarcely expected a response – first a woman's voice, then a man's.

"If you're asking for sympathies..." said Jessie.

"...we'll be here to deliver them," added James.

They poised atop one of the metal platforms, two svelte spectres of vengeance. The moment Cade saw them, a shiver coursed through his body.

"They survived," Cade realized, "How the hell did they know I was here?! You damned fool!" he turned to face Archer, infuriated. "You led them here."

"Forgive me, sir," Archer replied, dipping his head.

"You'll be grateful if I do." He directed Archer's attention brusquely back to the platform where Jessie and James stood. An inscrutable glance and smile passed between the two Team Rocket admins as Archer took a step forward.

"My former colleagues," Archer addressed them, "don't tell me Giovanni already sent you to collect my payment? Or perhaps you've come to beg to join us?"

James smirked. "Don't flatter yourself."

"The only thing we want is that Pikachu," answered Jessie.

"I think it's a little overdone," Archer countered indifferently. "Where's your mangy cat?"

Meowth leapt from the rafters overhead. Houndoom gave a pained yelp and spun, jaws snapping audibly, as Meowth's claws and fangs sank into its hide in a savagely shredding grasp. Houndoom fainted before either Cade or Archer could do more than turn and Ash, immediately freed from Shadow Hold's effects, tackled the boiler switch to snap the energy barrier off.

"Smokescreen," ordered James, opening a Poké Ball; in instant obedience Weezing emerged and engulfed the entire place in smoke.

In the ensuing smog, Cade raced for the exit and was gone before anyone could catch him. Meanwhile Archer began coughing, trying to search the haze for the deadly couple from Team Rocket.

"Where are they, damn it!?" Archer cursed under his breath. He pulled out a pistol, which he gripped tightly.

There was a flash of another Poké Ball being open; his eyes snapped towards it and the vague distinguishing of both Jessie and Arbok's silhouette.

Before he could shoot, Weezing tackled him and knocked the gun out of his hand, upon which Arbok sprang to wrap itself around him. The snake narrowly missed as Archer leapt aside only for him to end up grappling with James.

"Why didn't you three die when I hurled you into the stratosphere," snapped Archer.

"Archer why the hell are you listening to that guy?" James pursued, "You've always been the most loyal to Giovanni. He's your godfather damn it!"

"Giovanni's not the leader he once was. He's trying to disband Team Rocket," Archer countered.

"What...?"

Archer wrested free and snatched up the pistol from the ground, only to fire it multiple times at the ceiling. Concrete shards began to shower down from the old supporting columns of the building, and it began to fall to pieces.

Jessie tensed. "We'll all be crushed when the building collapses."

"You will, anyway," said Archer, tossing a Poké Ball lightly. When it struck the ground, a Pokémon was sent out: none other than one of the Legendary Beasts, the tiger Raikou.

"Raikou?" exclaimed James, "He's got a Raikou!"

Archer ignored his statement, instead he bounded nimbly onto Raikou's back. "Off," he ordered, and with a booming roar the creature bolted up to the roof through the now gaping hole and escaped.

"You're only postponing the inevitable...!" Jessie called after him.

"Forget him. Let's get the Pikachu and scram!" caterwauled Meowth.

Swiftly Jessie ran to the furnace.

Ash had successfully untied himself and he was scrambling to retrieve Pikachu. The little creature, too injured to react, lay limp in his arms.

No sooner had Ash gathered the badly burned Pikachu – Jessie wrenched it away from him.

"Those assholes, doing this to our rightfully stolen property," she hissed.

"You give him back!" exclaimed Ash, trying to grab Pikachu from her.

"We want it, not you!" In practised motion Jessie pushed Ash aside, and he fell with a gasp onto the floor.

Ash regained his footing quickly and sprang at her again. She reacted equally fast with the whip, and using the lash kept Ash at bay.

A creaking sound of metal brought Jessie's attention up all of a sudden, in time to see the pipes holding the furnace pillar loosen and the whole tower come crashing down towards her.

From behind James yanked Jessie out of the way. They ended up in each other's arms, clinging together with Pikachu in the middle and watching the ceiling overhead where the pipes had been anchored now crack into kaleidoscopic patterns.

"We should get out of here," said Jessie.

"On the double," James concurred.

"Rrrrr," agreed Meowth.

They were about to run for it when a shout made them instinctively glance back.

The debris that had nearly landed on Jessie had trapped Ash. He was trying to pull out from the rubble only to cry out when more rockfall nearly pinned him down; he fell back swift enough to save himself from being crushed but ended up being irrevocably separated from the exit, effectively sealed in a tomb.

Jessie and James turned pointedly away, but took only one step further before something stirred again, more adamantly; humanity they resolutely tried to push away but could never reject completely.

"Oh, fuck it!" cursed Jessie, and she and James ran back to save him.

Upon reaching the stone rubble, they sent out their Pokémon again. It was a race against the clock – a senseless one, thought Jessie and James, lamenting what they felt was meaningless morality.

"Arbok try to push these boulders aside," ordered Jessie.

"Weezing, smash the rocks," James directed.

Meowth leapt onto the stones and even he tried to move them, though the cat was too small to assist much.

There was utter confusion in Ash's eyes, but he would not refuse the help. Between the joint efforts of the trio and of the trapped trainer himself, Ash managed to get loose from the debris. The moment he was freed, he snatched Pikachu out of Jessie's arms.

"Weezing, use Protect!" James ordered his Pokémon.

In a cloak of unseen energy, Weezing enveloped the little group in a barrier. The raining boulders were blocked from hitting them, and James, Jessie, Ash and the animals were shielded long enough for them to get outside. They were in time to bear witness, from a safe distance, as the last of the building crumbled into dust.

They gazed at the now-decimated structure as Pidgey roosting in nearby trees scattered from the last of the noise. It was already dawn; the glow of newborn morning still in its faint and dewy stage.

Ash cradled the unconscious Pikachu carefully, not reacting even when the others looked over at him.

"It's hopeless," said Ash bitterly. "We're too far from help..."

His voice halted somewhat and faded away.

The Team Rocket trio considered the sorry sight briefly, and exchanged ambivalent glances; in resignation, James turned towards Ash:

"There's a Pokémon Center not far from here. We'll get you there."

Pikachu looked tinier than ever on that gurney; a frail little creature far from the vivacious animal the trio had set out to steal.

Jessie, James, and Meowth had gone as far as to help Ash to the Pokémon Center they knew to be in this area. It was right outside the Rock Tunnel caves, a rest stop out in no-man's-land. They made certain Pikachu was being tended to, and then discreetly retreated outside.

The whole thing was awkward to them. They wanted to keep to themselves, partly because they feared someone there would try to be a 'good citizen' and call the authorities, and the last thing they wanted was interference in issues that were their syndicate's – and their syndicate's alone – to contend with.

Ash did call someone, but it was his mother Delia.

"They say they had to amplify Chansey's Heal Pulse abilities to do any good. If it wasn't for modern medicine and the fact we got here quickly, Pikachu would be dead," he recounted to her bluntly.

Delia was very silent as he told the story, and Ash noticed it.

"Mom? are you there?"

"Yes, Ash. I'm listening, and thinking."

There was silence between them, and Ash decided to just break it with a question.

"I overheard something Mom, and I want to know if it's true or not... Is Giovanni Delavita my biological father?"

"It's true. Giovanni is your father."

"Why...?" Ash asked simply, "Why did you keep that from me?"

"I never wanted you involved in your father's work," Delia insisted. "He inherited a dark profession and built it into an empire that measures success by who lives and who dies. I love him, I've always loved him, and he loves me...but his business is...dangerous."

"Danger?" Ash echoed. "After everything that's happened? I've already been thrust into danger I never even sought out."

"Oh, Ash...don't be upset."

"No I'm not. I couldn't be. It's just..." His voice trailed away. "I'm just worried about Pikachu."

"Ash, your Pikachu is strong. I think he'll be all right."

With all said, they both hung up their phones.

Everyone on the streets below rushed about immersed in their own hectic lives, few noticing the three figures atop the Pokémon Center.

Jessie and James sat lounging together on the roof's edge, trying to make sense of their tumultuous day and, if nothing else, take in what solitary peace remained of that faded starlit night. Meowth groomed his paws and face beside them, nonchalant as ever.

"Maybe we really are too soft," James was saying. "We lose track of Archer and that corrupt mayor, and – of our own accord – end up saving the twerp and returning Pikachu... leaving us right back where we started with nothing to show for it."

Jessie sighed. "I can't believe we fucked up so badly."

"I wouldn't say it's so much as badly," Meowth purred, continuing to groom his face, "it's just you two define Murphy's Law."

James and Jessie exchanged a glance and finding the confusion mutual, turned back to the cat. "What's that supposed to mean?" James asked.

"You're the best at being the worst," Meowth replied matter-of-factly.

"It's either the world's most polite insult or the most offensive compliment," Jessie observed dryly.

The cat squinted at them and purred.

"Team Rocket?"

The introduction of a new speaker made the trio turn attentively around. To their surprise, they discovered Ash had joined them on the rooftop.

Ash briefly weighed his words but spoke honestly. "I never got to thank you for helping rescue us."

There was an awkward moment, and James finally answered him. "Well...don't mention it. Don't. It'd make us look like goody-goodies."

Ash nodded, but something else seemed to be on his mind. "Do you know anything about what Cade said?"

Jessie gave a disdainful scoff. "He said a lot of things."

"He said Giovanni Delavita is my father."

To this came a distinctly astonished unease; they all remained silent.

"Is that why you rescued me?" asked Ash.

"We went to get Pikachu. You just happened to be there," Jessie admitted bluntly. "We don't know anything else."

"You don't know or you can't say?" Ash pursued.

Her eyes narrowed. "You ask too many questions, twerp."

"I think I have a right to ask," he maintained.

Neither James, Jessie, nor Meowth responded to this. In truth, how could they respond? The trio knew very well of Giovanni's feelings towards Delia Ketchum, but discovering a possible lovechild of this union was unexpected even to them. Even if they had been sure, they were reluctant to say so for fear of incurring the boss' wrath should he wish it kept secret.

Ash evidently saw their hesitance, and with reasoned tact appeared to change the topic. "You once asked me if I would like to join Team Rocket."

James gave a pursed smile. "Only because, you know, having you join willingly is a lot easier than having to steal your Pokémon just to get them on our side. Forget about it."

"Except maybe I do want to join," ventured Ash.

The trio regarded him with surprise.

"I'd like to discuss it with Giovanni," Ash said cautiously. "Please take me to see him."

Chapter 19 - La Famiglia

Somehow the outside of the mansion, for as lovely as it was, appeared humble the moment one stepped inside. The interior was like a palace; ebony furnishings stood alongside champagne flooring of the finest Botticino marble, the décor pure lavish elegance, and overhead a chandelier shimmered as if it were made of diamonds. A staircase sloped gently up to the second level, where the Persian sat gracefully observant of the goings-on below.

From the unreadable look on Ash's face, James wondered if he was awed at the splendour of this place, the fact it existed in such forested seclusion near the large city, or merely surprised the Viridian City gym leader actually lived in Celadon's outlying suburbia. Of course, Giovanni's legal residence was a more modest Viridian house that was one of many properties he owned, and not this elegant Celadon mansion where he really dwelt, but the residency requirement for politicians and gym leaders to have local homes had many loopholes.

Pikachu clung to Ash's cap as usual, but it growled if anyone tried to pet it. The instantaneous healing of modern medicine had removed all traces of its burns; the only remaining sign of the little creature's ordeal was the guardedness with which it now regarded humans other than Ash.

If deep down James and Jessie felt partly responsible for having abducted Pikachu to begin with, they would never have admitted it, and quickly succeeded in sweeping aside this bothersome sentiment upon convincing themselves they only felt bad because it turned out to be the pet of the boss' son... plus, they had told their boss the newly found information about how Archer was now in possession of a Raikou; something that surprised him and somewhat distracted the conversation. At least Giovanni had not been angry with them regarding the mix-up regarding Ash.

On the contrary, he had been glad to hear they'd saved him. They did not entertain the thought as to what would have happened if they hadn't. He not only confirmed Ash was his son, but that Ash's mother was none other than Delia – who was now his fianceé. For Jessie and James it placed them in the very awkward situation of realizing the 'twerp', for all intents and purposes, was Giovanni's heir if Ash would accept inheriting his rightful place when the time came.

"I've never seen a place so luxurious," Ash remarked, confirming what had been on his mind.

Meowth gave a chirpy meow. "The boss likes to live large, twerp. His place here is fancier than the League offices up at the Indigo Plateau."

"I can imagine," Ash said.

"Ash." His mother's voice made him spin around. Delia was standing there with Giovanni by her side. The large cat Pokemon leapt down from the staircase and joined his master.

"We finally have our family together. It's a good day...isn't that so, Persian?" Giovanni said to his cat.

The feline consigliere wrapped itself around its master's legs in a hug.

They were ushered to the dining room and seated. Jessie, James, and Meowth lingered at a distance at different ends of the room as silent guards. The servants served their dinner and after a while of eating, Ash broke the silence with a point-blank question:

"Mom, why did you and father break up?"

Delia and Giovanni looked at each other and Delia explained, "Ash, the truth is those were very violent years in our region's history. When I found out I was pregnant with you, it was around the time that your father was given control of his family business and well...I didn't want you to grow up in it."

Giovanni jumped into the conversation. "We never stopped loving each other, Ash...but I understood her opinion and I also thought it was a way of protecting her from all the feuds that were ongoing."

"At some point," added Delia, "as years started rolling by, I thought maybe he had forgotten me and I felt awkward of approaching him so..."

"So we loved each other from afar," Giovanni finished. "The day your mother came to me in the office to tell me you were my son was simply a confirmation of what my heart had always known."

It was all very pretty and very romantic, and Ash was truly happy for his parents, but his mind still reeled over the whole revelation of being related to the boss of Team Rocket – the infamous Team Rocket. The idea of his father managing that sinister enterprise of stolen Pokémon and contract killings gave this otherwise joyful reunion a slightly sour taste, though Ash tried to swallow it down with his usual mild diplomacy.

Pikachu was far less moralistic and had already warmed up to them, evidently having decided that anyone against the people who hurt it were hereby its friends. It had no qualms whatsoever about its new friends being gangsters. If anything, Pikachu seemed to like the idea of being the pet of someone in a position of power, much more than Ash would have liked it to. It sat happily alongside Giovanni's Persian, each with their bowl of food.

Ash wasn't sure when the conversation flitted from wedding plans and happy fantasies to the family business, but he wished it hadn't. He could sense James and Jessie watching inobstrusively from the sidelines, interested in everything being said even though they were well-mannered enough not to interfere. Delia distanced herself from the discussion as Giovanni explained a bit to Ash about the many investments of Rocket Enterprises, or as everyone knew it better, Team Rocket.

"A sign of a well-run business is dependability and efficiency. That's what I've got and that's what I aim to keep," he said finally.

"But father..." Ash was briefly unsure how or even if he ought to say it, and ended up being boldly direct, "...what about the people you kill?"

Giovanni lifted a hand momentarily. "Unreliable business associates are eliminated, for the good of the organization," he corrected. "I take no pleasure in hurting people pointlessly."

Ash looked like he would have protested, but again he was not so tactless to express these sentiments now at the dinner, especially when he had only recently come to learn the truths of his parentage. Yet perhaps Giovanni could tell of Ash's displeasure at the matter, for he went on clarifyingly.

"I'm someone with power," explained Giovanni. "There is no such thing as good or evil when it comes to power. There is only power...and those who are willing to use it. You'll come to see that soon enough."

"Maybe," Ash replied, "but I'd never be an executioner. I could never kill anyone, least of all in cold blood."

He turned to his pet, who was munching happily on Pokémon kibble. "Pikachu agrees with me. Don't you buddy?"

"Piii." It...wanted a small shirt with an R. The request was met by a side-eyed glance by Ash and no reply.

Persian gave a couple of meows, which Ash could tell were clearly a translation when Giovanni stifled a chuckle.

Ash sighed, and muttered to himself, "How can death be treated so frivolously?"

"Vendettas are never to be taken frivolously," replied Giovanni. "I think your Pokémon understands that."

Ash restrained a scowl. Pikachu went on eating without a care.

"The organization that held you hostage is called Cipher," Giovanni said. "It's a rival syndicate, headed by a disgruntled business associate of ours."

"Why is he disgruntled?" Ash asked.

"We currently own his company."

Maybe I shouldn't have asked, thought Ash.

"The leader's name is Mr. Rose," recounted Giovanni, "You might recognize the name since his activities in the Galar region were highly publicized a few years back...he now lives in Orre. Mr. Cade, who you unfortunately met at the power plant, is the mayor of a city in Orre and has been working with him."

Giovanni hesitated, his gaze briefly faltering as he added quietly:

"The other man you met at the power plant was Archer, my godson. He'd gone missing a couple of weeks back."

"Archer didn't look like he was acting of his own accord," Ash told him. "Honestly he looked like his mind was affected somehow. Cade was ordering everything. There was something strange about all the Pokémon they had with them too."

"From what we've been able to learn, those were Shadow Pokémon. They're more powerful than regular Pokémon."

"They look traumatized."

"They get that way," Giovanni explained, "after being subjected to a special laser affecting their nervous system. Cipher then backs it up with abusive re-training sessions until even the stolen Pokémon are compliant. They become practically invincible in battle. If we can get in that racket by producing Shadow Pokémon for ourselves..."

"You just said they've been put through abuse!" Ash interjected with repulsion. "I saw what those poor Pokémon are like firsthand. Team Rocket can't possibly do the same," he said, and added emphatically, "We need to live alongside Pokémon. They're worth more than profit for a business enterprise; they're our friends."

"When your enemies think otherwise you have no choice but to be as ruthless as they," countered Giovanni.

"There has to be a way to reason with them," Ash replied, "everybody has some good in them."

"A childish fantasy," Giovanni smiled, in a gesture that was affectionate yet could easily have been patronising. "And I doubt someone as young as you would ever understand what I hope to achieve."

Ash flinched, but the words weren't delivered harshly. The syndicate don went on graciously:

"In any case I was told you might be interested in joining Team Rocket."

"I just want to stop Cade." Ash faced Giovanni with directness. "The longer he spends out there, the more Pokémon will suffer from this cruelty. If Cipher is behind it, then we'll stop them too...besides I want my revenge for what was done to Pikachu."

"That's a start," responded Giovanni approvingly.

That decided, the topic of conversation shifted to Ash's journey. It was a less-contentious matter he much preferred discussing.

"How many badges do you have left to go?" Giovanni sounded like he already knew the answer.

"I have three badges," Ash told him.

"So you're almost half-way there," noted Giovanni.

Ash decided to test the waters. "Saffron City was cordoned off. If it wasn't for that I could've tried for a fourth badge."

"Oh yes, Saffron," the Team Rocket boss smiled subtly.

"Well, there was a Snorlax blocking the entrance via route 8, and through route 5 an...unexpected toll booth." Ash found such indirect ways of speaking difficult.

Giovanni encouraged his attempt. "I'll see the toll is waived."

How easy things were becoming, like all the roadblocks had been lifted all at once. Ash merely stared at his father. "Does no one get ahead in Kanto without having some affiliation to Team Rocket?" he asked point-blank.

"We try not to let it happen," Giovanni responded demurely. "Still, it wouldn't suit an Elite Four challenger to be unversed in proper battle technique."

"I'm not—" Ash began saying.

"Out of the three badges you won, the Pewter gym was due to being lucky and getting a critical hit, the Cerulean gym was due to your Pokémon's type advantage, and the Celadon gym was due to the gym leader feeling indisposed and eager to get home early so she threw the match."

Such straightfoward knowledge of his progress unsettled Ash, but even more discouraging was the new information. He didn't know Erika of Celadon had gifted him the victory. The fact he hadn't even detected it meant he did have much to learn when it came to Pokémon.

Giovanni was not disparaging at all. "If you'd like I'll see that you're trained in the finer points of Pokémon battling."

Forcing away disquietude, Ash considered it openly. "Well, I'd never turn down an opportunity to get better at what I do. Who would be the instructors? The Viridian gym apprentices?"

"They're low rank," replied Giovanni, and only then did Ash realize that the entire staff of the Viridian gym must be Team Rocket members. "If you're going to learn it should be from the best. I'm assigning only the strongest and most skilled fighters of Team Rocket."

Ash couldn't disagree with that.

Overlooking their points of difference was central when both parties sought peace. Ash tried to be easygoing enough to get along with, and Giovanni also made the effort; all things considered, the meeting went far better than it could have. They found despite their drastic worldviews, they really had much in common. Giovanni had raised Persian from a kitten, and shared the same strong bond with it that Ash did with Pikachu. It stood out that both Ash and Giovanni had learnt the language of their starter Pokémon, a rare talent that, it seemed, was hereditary; even Giovanni's great-grandfather had apparently been able to communicate with his most trusted Pokémon.

"I suspect we're distantly related to the Harmonias," admitted Giovanni, referencing the famous Unovan councilman who could understand all animal language, "but I haven't had time to do a proper genealogical search."

After dinner they all spent a couple of hours engaged in family conversation and so when the pendulum clock at the entryway of the house rang nine times, they were all surprised at how fast time had passed by.

"My goodness!" exclaimed Delia, "I can't believe it's this late."

Giovanni looked at her and said, "I think it would be safer if you and Ash would spend the night... With Cipher's people still on our territory, the roads are not as safe as they used to be."

Delia looked into his eyes and saw the same tender look that he would always have in their past youth.

"Yes, Gio," she replied softly, "I like that idea."

Ash looked back and forth from one parent to another and saw the passion reflected in their eyes. He had no memory of ever seeing his mother this happy.

"Okay. Sure," Ash said, "Where's my room?"

Giovanni clapped his hands and two butlers entered the dining room.

"Show my son to his quarters," he told one of them, "See that he is comfortable and lacks for nothing."

Pikachu, who had been seated at one of the chairs at the table next to Ash, hopped onto his shoulders and squeaked. "Pika pi!"

"Let's go, Pikachu," Ash told him, as the butler led the way.

Giovanni faced the other butler and said, "Make sure there is a bottle of champagne on ice and two goblets in my sleeping quarters."

"Yes sir," the butler replied and left to his chore.

This left Giovanni and Delia alone.

He gathered her in his arms and whispered in her ear, "At last...My darling, there wasn't a day that went by when I didn't think about you...all these years. I love you."

"Oh Gio," she whispered back, "I never stopped loving you."

They kissed, with the same passion they had in their younger years, and when they finished he took her by the hand, led her up the staircase to his bedroom where the champagne was waiting, and closed the door behind them.

The next morning Giovanni and Delia came down to breakfast arm in arm.

The table was set with a lace tablecloth, porcelain plates and silver cutlery. Different kinds of breakfast foods, including bowls of fruit, were spread out on a buffet table nearby.

"What a feast!" Delia said in surprise.

"If you don't see what you want my dear, just ask the butler to prepare it," Giovanni said.

After filling their plates, they sat down and he added, "Sweetheart, have you thought about what we discussed, about your moving in? This is your home now."

"Yes Gio," she answered, "I will get some of my things and move in... Little by little... I plan on putting the house in Ash's name and he can stay living there."

At that moment, Ash came briskly walking into the dining area. "Good morning!" he said cheerfully.

"Did you have a restful night?" Giovanni asked him.

"Yes I did. It had been a long time that Pikachu and I managed to sleep through the night."

The little Pokémon concurred via a chirpy squeak.

"Ash," his mother said, "I am moving here with your father... You can use our old place as your own...I will be putting it in your name soon."

"Okay," Ash answered simply and proceeded to choose his breakfast from the buffet.

He sat down and they all ate their breakfast in silence.

When breakfast was done, Giovanni got up, put his hand on her back and bent down as she turned her face to him. He kissed her tenderly and said, "I have business to tend to my dear. I expect to be home for dinner this evening."

"Gio, I will go to my house to start the move, but I will try to be here before you arrive."

He kissed her again, and waved to Ash as he walked off.

Chapter 20 - To Be The Very Best

Ash wandered out of Celadon to route 7, where the instructors Giovanni was sending were supposed to meet him. The forest path was always peaceful, but at this early hour especially so. Cold breezes sifted through the boughs of the trees, unleashing leaves in a plentiful cascade. Dew still shimmered like fragile frost across the grass, yet the dawn had already turned bright and the Pidgey were singing praises of the morning sunlight.

He reached a leaf-strewn clearing off the main road, and was about to turn back when Jessie and James showed up. Meowth was nowhere to be seen.

"You two?" Ash did not know why he was surprised. They had never shown themselves to be anything but astute and ferocious, and certainly had that air of danger, but perhaps it was the modesty with which they carried themselves in all other respects; they certainly looked tame in civilian clothes.

Jessie seemed to read his mind and smiled smugly, but it was James who responded. "Surprised?" he asked. "We want people to see us as inept at least half the time. It makes it easier to work."

"I never thought you were inept," Ash said.

"But you didn't expect us to be Giovanni's top people either," James discerned.

"Well... no," Ash conceded.

"Good. Then we haven't lost our talent for hiding in plain sight," Jessie remarked cheerfully to James.

In the midst of this Meowth scampered up from the bracken to join them.

"Meowth," greeted Jessie. "What took you so long?"

"I had cat things to wrap up," explained Meowth.

"You and your cat things," scoffed James.

"Which're more important than human things," hissed the cat.

"How did you ever teach your Meowth to talk?" Ash could not help but satisfy his curiosity.

"He taught himself," Jessie replied, which really did not answer the question.

"And you got this the wrong way around," added Meowth, "I'm not their Meowth; they're my humans."

"Says who?" James queried, turning towards the cat.

"I've trained you to feed me, not the other way round," justified Meowth. "Or at the very least you put up the cash so I can order takeout."

"He's got a point, James," said Jessie with a little smile.

Ash fidgeted as they turned back to him. "The boss sent us out here to train you. That's what he told you, isn't it?" asked James.

"Yeah," Ash affirmed.

"All right," said Jessie. "What's your goal? We'll go from there."

Ash straightened up. "My goal is to become a Pokémon Master."

"In what way?" asked Jessie.

This question utterly perplexed him. She elaborated:

"To some people it would mean becoming League champion. To others it would mean catching one of each Pokémon. Or it would mean winning with a pedigreed show animal in Pokémon Contests. There is no one-size-fits-all for being a Pokémon Master."

Ash thought this over. To his frustration it still stymied him.

Jessie broke in again. "We can start with perfecting your battle technique. You'll no doubt figure out the rest as we make progress."

Arbok and Weezing reared back as Ash boldly made the first move.

"Pikachu, Quick Attack!" he ordered.

Pikachu darted forward to tackle. The moment it struck, however, Weezing retaliated with a close-range Sludge Bomb. Ink sprayed across Pikachu's eyes and, now completely disoriented, it was easy for Arbok to spring swiftly at a signal from Jessie and wrap itself around the electric type Pokémon - immobilizing it.

James gave a slightly amused shake of his head.

"Avoid taking risks rashly. Think through how your enemy could respond."

As he thought about this, Ash's eyes drifted off to Meowth. The cat was grooming himself indifferently.

"They sell thunder stones at the Celadon department store," said Jessie.

"No," said Ash, adamant, "I'm not evolving Pikachu. Pikachu told me he likes his current form. I'll only evolve him when and if he decides to become a Raichu."

"Most Team Rocket agents aren't so understanding with their Pokémon," Jessie posed.

Ash stiffened anticipatively. It had barely been one week into their training, and he was expecting a quarrel. He did not expect agreeing smiles from James and Jessie.

"I'll confide you this – we've never understood those agents," she said.

"A Pokémon fights more enthusiastically if it has a trainer that cares about its feelings," admitted James. "That said there's only one other way to win against a strong opponent with an unevolved Pokémon. You'll need to use status moves to reduce your opponent's accuracy and charge your own electric power."

"You mean moves like Double Team?" Ash asked quizzically. "I've always taught Pikachu other attacks instead. If a move doesn't do any actual damage, what's the point?"

"Stat changes make the difference between victory or defeat when a low level Pokémon goes up against a high level one. I once saw a Pidgey take down a Rhydon that way," James mentioned. Ash wondered if it was in the Viridian gym; he knew Giovanni owned a Rhydon. The idea of a small bird like a Pidgey defeating such a massive creature seemed so incredible to Ash's mind that he wished he could've seen the fight.

"More importantly, it lowers the opponent's guard," Jessie added, "and that's central to all combat."

"Is it?"

"Don't let your enemy know the extent of your abilities."

Ash considered this. He glanced curiously at Meowth, who had angled an ear towards their conversation briefly but decided it was uninteresting and turned instead to pawing at a falling leaf.

Electricity arced from Pikachu, a jagged intermittent flash that stabbed at its opponents. For every electric attack Pikachu gave forth however, Arbok and Weezing both managed to strike first.

"Your Pikachu is very strong, but our Pokémon are faster," Jessie noted.

Ash allowed himself to get a bit haughty. "We don't need to be speedy to beat you."

"Maybe so, or maybe not," evaluated James, and then his eyes glinted.

"If that Pikachu was strong and fast though, you'd be nearly unbeatable."

Meowth was sitting, paws tucked underneath himself in a loaf, watching everything with appraisal.

Pikachu raced so swiftly as to practically dance around Arbok and Weezing, its nimble bounds and dodges so distinct from a month prior.

This was thrilling to Ash, who could see how far they had come. Experience was always something desired, but to see it present and put to practice was exciting. Pikachu followed his orders instantly, darting in tandem with them in an electrified glow from one end of the field to the other and striking before its opponents could react.

Ash was so enthralled with how he was winning the battle that he barely noticed Meowth had crouched in pouncing posture, his tail lashing and eyes fixed on Pikachu's motions, nor how Jessie and James exchanged a glance and a subtle smile.

In an instant Meowth leapt into the fray, assailing Pikachu viciously with his claws and spinning the combat unexpectedly into a triple-battle. Ash had scarcely oriented himself to this new development when the flight of James' rose thrown towards him drew his attention off the battlefield, and without warning he was suddenly entangled in Jessie's whip.

Direct attack on his person was something he had not imagined. The lash held fast, despite Ash's struggles; Pikachu was faltering in the outnumbered battle, and for a moment worry flickered as to whether the fight was about to turn deadly after all.

He quickly realized the intent remained demonstration. Of all the lessons till now, Jessie had never spoken quite so seriously as this:

"Never assume your opponent battles with the same honor you do."

Ash had reached the second stage of his training. The only way to be ready for foul play, explained the Team Rocket trio, was to have a ready knowledge of self defense. And if they were going to spend time teaching him self defense, well, they may as well teach him full military strategy and weapons usage; why not? Ash went along with it to see how far they would really go, and Pikachu sat on the sidelines with Meowth to watch the spectacle.

The whip was standard issue for all Team Rocket recruits, and skill with the dagger was mandatory – or so they explained. Jessie would instruct him in the use of the former, with James to teach the latter.

"You see Jessie's better with the whip. I'm better with the knife," James mentioned.

Ash opened his mouth to ask something, then thought more lucidly of it. "I'm better not asking."

"You're learning, kid!" purred Meowth approvingly.

"The trick to whip combat is distance," explained Jessie, "Long-range with the lash, mid-range with strangulation, short-range striking with the handle. Learn all you can because you're going to need it for your next trial."

This aforementioned 'next trial' awaiting him was kept with unusual secrecy till Ash had gotten the hang of using the whip. Finally, Jessie told him what they had planned.

"You're going to battle a Pokémon."

"Again?" Ash remarked, "Pikachu can beat any Pokémon you send out."

"That's not what we said," smiled Jessie slyly.

It was only when she tossed him the whip that realization fell on him.

"Your opponent is Meowth," announced Jessie, jerking her head towards the feline.

Ash turned in disbelief towards the cat, which had outstretched a hind leg and was grooming indifferently.

"Are you serious?" Ash exclaimed.

"Don't you know how Pokémon battles were conducted in the days before Poké Balls?" prompted James. "What do you expect to do if you're ever separated from your Pokémon and attacked directly? Sometimes shit happens."

The truth was Ash was starting to wish he had paid more attention in history class back in the day, but the fact remained it seemed too barbaric for his liking and he remained firm. "I'm not whipping Meowth."

"Good," purred Meowth, "this'll be easy!"

The cat launched himself at Ash with a screech, claws bared, and the result was a haphazard race around the clearing as Ash tried futilely to flee or block Meowth's Fury Swipes.

It ended with Ash flat on his back, Meowth pinning him down.

"At that low level, you'd be lucky to beat a Pidgey!" purred Meowth.

"Get off me, cat," Ash grumbled, pushing the squinting, contented Meowth off.

Jessie seemed to be evaluating him. "Your technique is lacking, but your defense was OK. The biggest problem you have is a conscience. We need to work on getting rid of that."

Ash stood up, dusting himself off as he tossed the whip back to her. "This is pointless. If people can fight just as well as Pokémon, it's almost defeating the purpose of being a trainer."

"You don't get it, do you," James observed.

When Ash looked at them quizzically, Jessie added, "The point isn't that you fight instead of your Pokémon. The point is that you fight with your Pokémon."

She smiled genuinely.

"That's why it's called teamwork."

The rest of their training turned into a blur for Ash. He had been tasked with everything from running a veritable gauntlet – "It's properly known as parkour," James had said, as if that made it better – to trying to best them both in hand-to-hand combat.

Exhaustion was the overarching sentiment in that time in Ash's mind, and it was hard to keep himself awake when they arbitrarily insisted on holding late-night training sessions one week – "I'm up; I'm up...damn it!" cursed Ash, upon getting bitten awake by Meowth – but the one thing he felt grateful for was they never asked him to participate in any of their seedier operations, such as thievery, poaching, or worse. Nonetheless worry plagued his mind between sleep deprivation and overwork, and he wondered what he would do if it came to that, but his worry never manifested as an ultimatum.

The reality was Jessie and James knew Ash did not have either heart or stomach for their work. He might have agreed to join them, but he had feelings of sympathy he could not hide, and they did not see the need to place him in a situation where this would be overtly challenged, at least not without their boss' explicit orders. Sympathy was not foreign to them either; Jessie and James had merely learnt to restrain it for the sake of cold-blooded logic, and they had every conviction Ash would one day find himself the same eventually – "It's something that happens," said Jessie, "whether you like it or not, as a natural course of events, because life can be fucked up like that."

For the majority of that long month they trained tirelessly in this vein. For one week after they gave Ash a break, and the first day of this vacation he spent sprawled in bed till noon.

By now camaraderie had bloomed within their thorny animosity; the sort of friendship where they spoke bluntly, bickered sharply, and then instantly dropped the quarrel by realizing it was lunchtime and going out to eat together.

James and Jessie would always change into civilian clothes first. Only once did they decide to go attired in full uniform, on the pretext they were too starving to give a damn, but it had secretly been to show Ash what would happen.

They had not done anything more than walk in and quietly announce themselves as a party of three from Rocket Enterprises, yet it resulted in people scrambling in fright to give them the best table and service. Ash almost felt guilty for being there. In contrast, Pikachu took advantage of it to swipe a whole ketchup bottle all for itself.

"Flamboyancy is fun, but it needs to have a purpose," explained James, as they ate. "Otherwise it'll lose its impact."

Ash was still trying to align their duality in his mind. They were what they were; he remembered the bloody scene he had stumbled across in Lavender Town, and despite all this they were always genuinely gracious with everyone, the least likely people in his mind to be paid killers. Finally he just decided to ask:

"How did you ever end up in Team Rocket?"

Jessie answered him in a simplistic way. "We found you have to make your own happiness where you can. The only kindness ever extended to us was from Team Rocket and each other. To us, that's worth our loyalty."

It was vague enough to Ash yet not so cryptic as to be incomprehensible. Whatever their individual backstories were, it evidently pained them too much to go into detail; for this realization alone, he felt oddly sympathetic.

"By the way," James switched subjects, "I wonder where Cade and Archer have gone. We haven't seen a whisker of them since that situation at the power plant."

"Probably they've left the region," replied Jessie. "After all, Cade knows what Giovanni will have done to him if he and his goons stick around."

"Frankly I don't want to know," Ash said. The memory of them hurting Pikachu still aggravated him.

"Whether you like it or not, soon you'll have to know," Jessie pointed out gently. "This is Team Rocket business after all and you're part of it."

"I guess," conceded Ash, who at this point was watching Pikachu attack the ketchup bottle. "I want the people who did that punished, but somehow I'm still not accustomed to how our syndicate does things. Somehow I doubt I ever will be."

"It's a business matter, that's all," replied James. "There's not much depth to it. Kind of a peculiarity of our corporate culture."

"That reminds me," Jessie turned to her companion in a sudden happiness, "James...it's time he learned our motto."

"You're right, Jessie," he agreed with enthusiasm.

"We have a motto?" Ash echoed, turning back to them.

They recited it with natural flair, even though they were merely sitting around the table; somehow Ash could picture them up on a theatre stage for how they delivered the lines, each in turn, with flawless dramatism.

"Prepare for trouble!" Jessie began.

"...and make it double!" James followed after.

"To protect the world from devastation!"

"To unite all people within our nation!"

"To denounce the evils of truth and love!"

"To extend our reach to the stars above!"

"Jessie!"

"James!"

"Team Rocket, blast off at the speed of light!"

"Surrender now or prepare to fight!"

"...and then Meowth jumps in to say 'That's right!' " added Jessie, rather annoyed, "if he were here, which he isn't, because he's taken to prowling in the daytime too and we have no clue where the fuck he's going."

"When do you say this again?" Ash questioned dubiously.

"Mostly to rally our minions," Jessie replied.

"We wanted to say it every time we show up to raise hell somewhere, but Giovanni put his foot down," James admitted wryly.

Ash could not tell if they were being serious or not. He merely watched as the waiter brought the bill and James paid it, the suddenly wide eyes and profuse thanks of the man receiving a handsome gratuity, and the little group walked out of the restaurant as uneventfully as they had come.

"What does that even mean?" asked Ash as they strolled down the sidewalk together. "Uniting people and protecting the world? It makes it sound like we're some kind of governmental organization instead of a criminal syndicate."

"We're basically the private enterprise version of government," James provided a correlation, albeit a questionable one in Ash's view. "Think about it...what we do, we're merely safeguarding our interests and those of our allies, and collecting fees for our valuable service to the community."

"Look, no offence intended..." began Ash.

"No offence taken," interjected James. "How are you going to learn without saying some stupidity first?"

So Ash spoke, more emboldened. "It just seems you're...umm...we're... basically well-dressed thieves and assassins."

"Exactly," grinned James.

"If we weren't doing this, someone else would take our place. That's the thing with people," continued Jessie, "there's always going to be someone who's power-hungry or money-hungry or just plain vengeful who will step in to take advantage. It's human nature. So we may as well exploit it."

"...but 'the evils of truth and love'?" Ash queried, "There's no such thing. How can virtues be evil?"

"Not in and of themselves," James clarified. "Sometimes truth and love can result in evil."

"I don't see it," said Ash.

"Think it over, twerp," smiled Jessie, "One day you might figure out what we mean."

Ash did think about it for the rest of the day, and when he met Giovanni again later he brought it up.

"Oh yes, the motto." He sounded a bit annoyed.

Ash pursued, "Was it written to be some kind of way of messing with the enemy or..."

"That was not my doing," Giovanni emphasized. "That's actually the fault of a Team Plasma general called Zinzolin, who indirectly gave my two otherwise-bright associates James and Jessie the foolhardy idea we needed some kind of rallying cry like the old Plasma war cheer."

"I don't really get it," Ash admitted.

"No one gets it except the minions. That shows you're meant to be a don."

"So I guess you wouldn't be able to tell me what they meant by 'the evils of truth and love.' "

Giovanni's reply was indirect. "Good and evil are two sides of the same coin. A good intention taken too far will inevitably become evil," he explained, "and one day you may find yourself standing opposite of where you started."

"I remember the story you told me about how Team Rocket came into being. Kind of like that?"

To this Giovanni was pensive. Perhaps the memory bore scars. Briefly Ash wondered if he had phrased it indelicately, or if his father would answer at all, but he leant back and replied:

"Exactly like that."

Ash still did not fully comprehend the syndicate's ideological intricacies, but he was sure of one thing: he had to learn as much as he could to get stronger, because getting stronger was the only way to both revenge what was done to Pikachu and stop Cipher from inflicting even more torture to create Shadow Pokémon.

He stood up to leave and Giovanni said, "Ash...you are my son. I am here for you, don't forget that."

"Yes, father."

Chapter 21 - The Silph Company

Silph's logo was a stylised S in the shape of two halves of a Poké Ball. It graced the glass doors of the skyscraper, which was located in the heart of lively Saffron City and housed the company headquarters.

Two black vans and a limousine pulled up at the entrance. Giovanni Delavita and his two bodyguards, along with the cats Persian and Meowth, got out of the limousine. Persian gave a trill.

Giovanni placed a hand on his head affectionately. "Yes, my friend. Business before mealtime."

Out of the other cars emerged more Team Rocket members, all wearing their distinctive black uniforms. Giovanni turned to his bodyguards and ordered, "James, Jessie...as usual I expect the job be done neatly." To the others he simply said, "Let no one in or out of the premises. You have your orders."

Giovanni and his entourage followed by Meowth and the Persian went inside the building, where a very surprised reception desk manned by a secretary and two security guards tried protesting the intrusion. They were met swiftly with snarling Pokémon, which looked as eager to pounce as their Team Rocket trainers were to give them the go-ahead. Giovanni held them all back with a signal motion.

"Where is Mr. Silph? I believe he and I have pending negotiations he forgot to list on his itinerary," said the Team Rocket boss.

"Holding a meeting with the company executives," responded the secretary nervously. "He's on the eleventh floor."

"Well then...we'll have to vacate his schedule for him."

He gave a snap of his fingers and Meowth, with a meow, leapt up and snatched a card key from one of the security guards. No one dared protest.

Giovanni, followed by Jessie, James and the two cats went into the elevator, and swiped the card key for the eleventh floor. They could see the three Silph employees watching with uneasy knowledge as the elevator closed and whisked the Team Rocket don and admins away.

Meanwhile, Ash was strolling down the Saffron sidewalk, on his way to the gym at last.

As he neared the Silph Company, he saw Giovanni's limousine parked there and two of the black-attired Team Rocket minions guarding the office building's elegant glass entrance. One of the minions was Kris; still upset about Archer's alliance with Cipher, which she knew had to have been achieved through coercion, she had thrown herself into her work for Team Rocket and succeeded in at least keeping up a cheery attitude in conversation. She smiled when Ash approached.

"Hi Kris. Where's my father?" Ash asked.

"Inside," she answered promptly. "I think he went to see the Silph Company CEO."

Ash glanced up at the towering skyscraper, and then peered inside the lobby where he could see more Team Rocket guards with their Pokémon. "Did...Team Rocket take over the company?"

"Yep," Kris affirmed. "Well, not officially; we didn't buy it yet as far as I know...but we still invaded. I get to stand guard with Bob."

"Hey," acknowledged Bob, the other Team Rocket agent, with a casual wave.

Ash mulled over the situation, and arbitrarily decided to detour from the Saffron gym. "I think I'm gonna go see what my father's up to. Catch you later Kris...and nice meeting you, Bob."

The meeting-room was lavish, with oil paintings depicting mountain landscapes and an imported rug of a deeply burgundy hue, upon which was set a long mahogany table. Seated at the head of the conference table surrounded by six other people was Mr. Silph, who looked up in astonishment as Giovanni and his top guards strode into the corporate boardroom.

"What's the meaning of this? How did you get up here?" Silph demanded.

Jessie and James gave a cryptic smile; Giovanni's answer was darkly succinct.

"I'm here to collect a debt."

Silph swallowed hard, and turning to the others said, "We shall resume this meeting later. Thank you for coming."

The people exited the room quickly, heads down as if they knew there would be trouble. Once they had gone, Silph's attention shot back to Giovanni.

"You can't be serious. The mere fact you barged in here," snapped Silph. "Don't you think everybody saw you? Don't you think people downstairs saw you?"

"Right now your company is in the midst of a very literal takeover," Giovanni mentioned.

This casual remark carried a degree of offhand indifference that Silph, lacking in judicious foresight, could not begin to gauge fully.

"A takeover? What do you mean – a takeover?"

"I mean that if you would have been more attentive to corporate affairs instead of personal ones you would have noticed as of the market close I hold the majority of Silph Company stock." Giovanni did not mince words at all. "And I have agents stationed at every floor and exit preventing anyone from leaving, but that's just for my amusement."

He walked closer to where Silph was still seated; when he saw the man's astonishment flicker briefly into concern, Giovanni added with blunt coldness:

"I'm not a fool, Mr. Silph. I don't play a hand unless I know it's a winning one. And I never renege on a promise."

"Well, what is it you want?" asked Silph, suppressing the first tremble of unease.

"Payment," replied Giovanni easily. As he spoke, he retrieved the rose from the lapel pocket of his suit and tossed it to James.

"I intend for you to sign over the last remaining shares in the company. The Silph Company and Rocket Enterprises...no, that's woefully inaccurate." Giovanni leant forward. "By nightfall, the Silph Company will be merged with Team Rocket."

"Impossible. I won't do it," Silph declared.

He must have thought himself impressive, defying the don of the Team Rocket syndicate to his face. In Giovanni's sight, however, it inspired little more than petty rancour.

"You have a debt with me. I gave you a favor and the time has come for you to repay," Giovanni practically snarled.

He appeared to forcibly regain his composure, and when he spoke again his voice was eerily calm.

"Look, Mr. Silph...you're a smart man. I'm sure you can imagine what will happen if you say no to me now."

Mr. Silph stared at Giovanni, the magnitude of his words settling slowly. His eyes drifted once more to the two lithe figures who now stood on either side of him – Jessie drawing the whip taut, James holding the rose with almost kindly patience, and suddenly Mr. Silph's stately poise crumbled away into pleading terror.

"Mr. Delavita, please...!" he implored, "we can find a solution."

Before Giovanni could respond to him, or give a final order, Ash walked in.

"What's going on?" asked Ash in his sprightly way. Pikachu, clinging to his cap, gave a corresponding squeak.

"The president of the Silph Company and I are discussing a vital business proposition," Giovanni said with brevity.

Mr. Silph did not dare open his mouth. He sat stiffly, in visible fear, with perspiration dripping down his forehead. Meanwhile Jessie and James side-eyed the intrusion with displeasure. Ash evaluated the situation in one quick review of the boardroom and his shoulders seemed to slacken.

"Is this really necessary, father?" Ash posed.

Giovanni thought about the situation and then turned back to Silph.

"It seems you're having a very fortunate day." His words became terse. "Enjoy it."

With a single motion indicating for his two employees to follow, Giovanni whirled around and left.

Ash showed up the next morning to his father's office at Team Rocket headquarters. He appeared a bit uncertain about something as he met the Persian in the hallway and was led by it to Giovanni.

"Ash," Giovanni greeted him pleasantly, "Buongiorno... I've been told you triumphed over the Saffron gym yesterday. I don't believe I got to congratulate you."

Ash began tentatively. "I just heard they found Mr. Silph at the Celadon Hotel."

"Yes, apparently he was there meeting his mistress," said Giovanni, with the veneer of good-natured gossip.

"...in an elevator," Ash continued flatly, "stabbed to death, with a single red rose beside him."

To this, the boss of Team Rocket gave an innocuous shrug.

"La vita è così, figlio mio," Giovanni smiled slightly.

Ash looked at him with skepticism.

"On a more pleasant topic," commented Giovanni, "I've heard Mr. Silph's grandson is a reasonable man and plans to sign over ownership of the entire Silph Company to Rocket Enterprises tomorrow."

"After what was done to his kin?" Ash was astounded.

"People have an innate, instinctual desire to live," said Giovanni simply. "And most are not as committed as we to the ideal, if you will, of vendettas."

Ash listened accordingly, but he seemed a bit ill despite himself. His gentle nature was difficult to overcome. The only thing he answered was:

"I need a drink."

"Why don't you join me for a glass of amaretto?" Giovanni replied amiably. "Or if you're going out, take Jessie and James with you. After this, the Cipher syndicate might want to hit us back."

He handed Ash his drink and poured one for himself. "Saluté," he said, and they drank.

Ash sat down at an armchair and asked:

"Why would Cipher care about that?"

"Because they were the ones who told Silph to not sell in the first place."

Ash looked mystified, and – he was forced to admit to himself later – impressed. Giovanni leant back and stroked Persian, which was purring loudly.

"As I said once," Giovanni added naturally, "I run a very efficient organization."

Chapter 22 - A Light in the Shadows

Mr. Rose paced up and down the living room, deep in thought and increasingly tense. Oleana and her Garbodor, a poison type Pokémon that looked almost like a trash bag, sat watching him walk to and fro. "Darling, you really shouldn't get so stressed," Oleana said, "It will be easier to think things through if you try to allay your worries."

"It's incomprehensible, Oleana," lamented Rose, "Giovanni seems intent on all-out war. I don't get it."

"Surely it would help if we opened a line of communication with Team Rocket," she considered.

"There's no way to reason with him." Rose shook his head as he kept pacing. "First his baseless accusations we somehow hurt his godson, followed up by an attempt to kill us both. Only two weeks later I receive word Giovanni now thinks we tried to harm his biological son. I didn't even know he had a son till that point. Now Mr. Silph is dead...and with him goes our last independent supplier of Poké Balls."

Oleana had to admit the setback that posed. "It was always unfortunate we had to outsource production of a product we once manufactured ourselves."

"...and we know," added Rose, "that trying to open our own business to rival Giovanni's new monopoly will be faced with all manner of retaliation. What bothers me is how he won't just admit he doesn't want competition...he has to shroud it in all these lies, acting as if we're going after his kinfolk to justify his actions as a vendetta."

He sat down wearily on the loveseat beside her as Garbodor hopped onto the floor to give them room. "At this point, I don't know what to do," he admitted.

Oleana narrowed her eyes pensively at the same time as Mayor E. S. Cade walked in. His normally formal attire looked dishevelled and tarnished with soot, and it caused Rose to have a double-take.

"Cade, what happened? You look awful," Rose remarked.

"You know the laboratory where we had the equipment to produce Shadow Pokémon?"

"Yes..."

"It burnt to the ground."

"What do you mean, the laboratory burnt to the ground?"

"Team Rocket did it."

"My God, that place took a small fortune to build, not to mention the scientific equipment, and now it's literally up in smoke."

"...as well as all our remaining crates of Poké Balls!" Oleana added.

Cade looked red in the face. "Your building was technically on regional land, allocated towards the Phenac City revitalization. How do you think it makes me look?"

"Inept," snapped Rose.

"No, corrupt," Cade countered.

"Which you are," Rose answered with a scowl, "It's not like you ever tried to hide that."

Cade forced down his ire with a slow breath, and manufactured his usual charm. "Look, Mr. Rose, bickering will get us nowhere. It's those hoodlums from Team Rocket that have to pay – both for your property damage and my public pride."

"What are you proposing?" asked Rose dubiously.

"Hit them back, hard," Cade emphasized, "None of the niceties from when we tried to recover the Mew; it got us nowhere. If they want a war with Cipher, let's go all out."

"It'd be a massacre!"

"That's evidently what they want, and for no reason at all... It's clear Team Rocket won't stay on their territory even if you try to stand down."

Oleana spoke with frosty skepticism. "You're overly eager to go to war with Giovanni...as usual."

"With all he's been doing, I believe it's merited," Cade replied, and turned to Rose. "We've still got the Shadow Pokémon we produced; we can use them in battle. With their type resistance, even Team Rocket's high-level Pokémon won't stand a chance."

"That reminds me, someone told me Giovanni thinks we're collecting Legendary Pokémon or something to that regard," Rose commented. "He knows Oleana owns Zacian and Zamazenta, but he seems to think we've captured a Raikou, and right from his territory."

"Oh...I wouldn't know anything about that," Cade responded. "More of his lies no doubt."

"No doubt," smirked Rose. "I'll think over what we do. Starting with our batch of Shadow Pokémon; they may be astonishingly powerful, but the procedure obviously left them in distress, so we'll have to find a way to alleviate what the energy beam did to them." The displeased look on Cade's face to hear this did not go unnoticed by Rose, but it did go politely unaddressed. "You'd better get yourself cleaned up too," he added when he saw Garbodor waddle over to Cade's side, attracted as only a poison type could be by his dingy suit.

When the Phenac City mayor had left, Rose turned aside to speak with Oleana again. "If there was any doubt about your suspicions, my dear Oleana, I think Cade himself is dispelling them. Heaven knows we'd have ample reason to want war with Team Rocket, considering Giovanni's theft of our former company, but Cade seems to want it more than we do. Perhaps enough to stir the pot in secret. Now...why?"

Destroying Cipher's laboratory would merely be the beginning. Now that Silph was out of the way and Team Rocket owned a monopoly on Poké Ball manufacturing, Giovanni could focus all his attention on Cipher. If Rose wanted war, and really – interfering in Team Rocket's capture of Mew, the mystery behind Archer's defection, and trying to kill Ash; and Rose brazenly denying all of it – there could be no other explanation, save that he wanted a war.

First thing was first, though. They needed to get Archer back.

So after James, Jessie, and Meowth contacted Giovanni, telling him how they'd succeeded in his orders and the Cipher laboratory was in flames, he sent them posthaste to the Under. If there was a chance to track down Archer, it would no doubt come to the forefront there.

The Team Rocket trio walked till they found a flickering neon sign above a doorway that read: The Under Grand Hotel. They went in and saw a door to the side that had a symbol that appeared to be a bottle drawn on it.

Opening the door, they found a staircase leading to a cellar, and they followed it downstairs. It led them to an entrance of a liquor vendor. James was eyeing the place suspiciously.

"This is a seedy place," he decided.

Meowth let out a hiss. "What do you care? We’ve been to seedy places before."

Jessie concurred, "Yeah, but this is seedy even by our standards."

Meowth added, "Let’s go in and wait for our contact to arrive."

They wandered in virtually unnoticed, since most of the people there were keeping themselves low key as well, and sat at a corner table. A bartender walked over.

"What can I get you?"

"Nothing," answered James, "We’re waiting for someone, and don’t expect to be here for very long."

"Makes no difference to me," the man answered gruffly, "Everyone here is either waiting for someone, something, or already 'doing business' …either way, you order or you get out."

"Nice attitude," hissed Meowth.

"Bring us a beer," replied Jessie.

"Just one?"

"Yeah, just one!" screamed Jessie, "You said to order, you didn’t say it had to be more than one, or if we had to actually consume your stinking drinks!"

This outburst momentarily made people look their way, but everyone knew better than to get involved in what was not their business. The bartender left quickly and returned just as fast with one beer, which he set before them.

Jessie promptly took the beer glass, poured the beer on the floor and putting the glass back on the table looked the man straight in the eyes and said, "Now leave us alone, before I let my Team Rocket boss know that you are most uncooperative."

Meowth added a hiss.

The bartender left without another word, and the trio was left waiting for the business partner to show up. They sat there for about a half hour and then they saw their contact, a man called Miror B.

He was quite unmistakable in a crowd. He was dressed in a showy gold suit, with his red-and-white hair styled in an afro, and wearing large sunglasses for looks – the Under was certainly dark as it was, to merit them. As soon as he sat down, Miror B. wasted no time in speaking.

"I have to get back to the club; I'm on stage in an hour."

Jessie tossed a couple of cash bills onto the table, which Miror B. wasted no time in snatching up. "...but I might be able to stop the music long enough to have a conversation with such a charming couple and their kitty-cat."

"We're flattered," Jessie replied, bored.

"Look, short and sweet. We're trying to find someone," said James, who produced an up-to-date photograph of Archer. Miror B. scrutinized it before affirming:

"Short teal hair, blue eyes, always with a strict kind of formality? Yeah, I've seen him. He hangs around with E. S. Cade as muscle. I don't know where he goes off-duty, though. He could be living under a false name."

"Could you find out?"

"I doubt it."

Jessie tossed another bill of cash onto the table, but this time Miror B. shook his head.

"I know better than to accept advance payment from Team Rocket when I can't provide the goods," he said. "If there was a way to find out without putting my hide on the line, I'd have info already from my contacts in Cipher...but many people, in particular those who'd know, because they worked at the Cipher lab alongside Cade, are too afraid to talk. They say Cade's got a Pokémon that isn't a Pokémon."

"What the hell is that supposed to mean?" asked James. Miror B. shrugged.

"Whatever it is, it's scared everyone who knows into silence. And I'm not particularly keen to find out what they mean either."

When Miror B. left, Jessie, James, and Meowth lingered in a huddle.

Jessie spoke first. "Okay guys. Riddle me this...what kind of Pokémon, isn't a Pokémon?"

"A Bidoof," declared Meowth.

Jessie practically rolled her eyes. "Serious answers only, Meowth, not your own prejudice."

"But those damn woodchucks are evil," the cat hissed.

James ignored Meowth. "Suppose Cade caught something obscenely powerful. We know Cipher already owns a Raikou, and no one's seen Entei roaming the Johto region anymore so it's safe to say they've got Entei too... What if now they've got something even more fearsome; something so strong it's beyond what people normally think of with regard to Pokémon?"

"Maybe he's caught the missing Mew?" considered Jessie.

"Maybe he turned it into a 'Shadow' Mew," James replied.

"Cat-astrophe," growled Meowth.

"We don't even know what a damn Mew looks like. Archer knew," Jessie lamented, then realized, "Wait...didn't Kris help him catch it?"

"We oughta ask her," Meowth alerted his ears. "At least we'll have an idea what kind of critter we're even talking about."

"It could only help," agreed James. "Let's get back to the Pyrite Motel...Kris is probably getting restless there anyway waiting for us."

It was dawn, and the sun was steadily creeping higher in the sky. Kris poised cautiously on the roof of the Mart and adjusted her binoculars, her post affording her a clear view of Phenac City Hall across the street.

She should have been back at the motel in Pyrite Town. She'd come along with the trio of Jessie, James, and Meowth to train some more and be a backup fighter with Suicune, not to go off on a solo search-and-rescue mission.

But her own desperation to find her brother finally got the better of her.

Beside her, Eevee looked up at her and squeaked.

"They won't be too pissed," Kris answered her Pokémon's question, "not if we come back with a lead on Archer's whereabouts."

Eevee's long ears lay flat. It didn't seem to share her certainty, but it would stand by its trainer regardless.

City Hall was relatively quiet. At this early hour, with the sun still an increasing glow in the sky, the offices were closed and no one had arrived to work yet. She was going over a plan in her mind as she studied the building and the possible ways in.

"Okay Eevee," she announced at last, lowering the binoculars, "we're going to sneak into City Hall and find the mayor's office. The last time anyone saw Archer was with Cade, right? And Cade was apparently the same person in charge of those Cipher guards back at the laboratory."

Eevee tipped its head to one side attentively.

"We're going to get into the mayor's office and see if there's anything he's got there that could tell us something we don't know."

It was a long-shot; Kris knew that, but she figured it was the best chance they had. She knew Jessie, James, and Meowth thought a contact of theirs in the Under would know something, and perhaps he did, but in her mind it seemed a far more effective plan of action to go investigate who she presumed was the heart of the issue – and that was Cade himself.

Kris hurriedly brought the binoculars back up to her eyes when she saw a black car arrive, and the driver get out and head for City Hall.

It was none other than Mayor E. S. Cade.

She hadn't expected him so early. Nevertheless, that wouldn't be a problem for her; if anything it was a bonus.

"Change of plans..." decided Kris, "we're sneaking in and confronting Cade."

He generally came to the office much later, but Cade had an urgency to get something he kept there. If Mr. Rose would still not be spurred into action, then perhaps he'd have to help the war along a bit.

It didn't matter if Rose or Giovanni was the first to go down. Granted, he'd hoped it would be Giovanni, because he had his own personal dislike for the Delavitas, but his aim would be fulfilled regardless. It was nonetheless preferable they wear each other down; he would have an easier time taking over the surviving group if it was weakened from fighting, and seeing Rose's Cipher was hesitant in getting involved at all, he'd have to restructure his plans and wear Team Rocket out another way.

Within his office he had one of the radio systems with which he could contact those loyal to him in Team Rocket. It was through that system he had gathered them together to assist in kidnapping Ash. He would contact his infiltrates and have them strike at Team Rocket – from the inside.

Cade smirked at the thought. It was a perfect ploy! Team Rocket knew they had enemy agents embedded in their ranks, but they'd been unable to weed them out. What they didn't know was how many of them were assigned to the Viridian gym.

It would be the first time in Kanto's history that a League gym would be ransacked and its gym leader assassinated on-site. First time for everything, Cade thought with malicious contentment.

His good mood vanished upon stepping into his office.

He was confronted by a woman in the black uniform of a Team Rocket recruit. Her Eevee poised in a battle stance with fur fluffed out, growling and ready to shoot its attacks directly at him.

"Shut the door," she ordered simply.

He slowly did. The silence was devastating. "My, my..." began Cade, "I must be honest...I never imagined anyone would go so far. A Team Rocket agent, entering my own office!"

"You can quit the sanctimony," snapped Kris, "I know you're involved with Cipher."

Cade did not dispute it. She went on, "I'm here to find out where my brother is."

"...who?" he feigned ignorance.

"Archer Verdi!" Kris countered. "You must know where he is. You were with him at the power plant."

"You're evidently mistaken," said Cade tentatively.

She narrowed her eyes as she pulled out a Poké Ball. "If you don't tell me where Archer is the nice way, my Suicune will get it out of you the nasty way."

"Oh, you have a Suicune?" Cade asked with visible interest.

Kris hesitated, suddenly aware she might have spoken a bit too much. Cade was as demure as ever. "I don't think you want to battle me."

"I don't think you want to face my Suicune."

"Perhaps it's the principle of the matter." He gave a slight shrug. "Trainers' eyes locked; that sort of sentiment? I know Johto's customs too from when I lived there years ago. It's a point of honor." Retrieving a Poké Ball from his pocket and unlocking it, Cade added:

"Who am I to turn down a challenge?"

He opened the Poké Ball with the press of a button.

Archer emerged from the capsule in a flash of white light, standing attentively. And Kris, taken completely by shock, could only blink and stare in stunned horror.

"Get that Poké Ball!" ordered Cade.

Archer sprang at her, wresting Suicune's Poké Ball away and pushing her aside. Cade meanwhile had opened another Poké Ball, and Houndoom was sent out.
