With a set of hand signals, too swift for Kris to properly detect, Houndoom directed its attention to Eevee and with a pounce sank its fangs into the small creature's pelt. Eevee squealed as it was hurled sideways against the wall, knocked out.

Archer handed the stolen Poké Ball to Cade without a trace of emotion. Cade snickered as he regarded the still-locked sphere containing Suicune.

"The last of the three Legendary Beasts. I must thank you for such a generous donation to my campaign," Cade taunted. "...of conquest, that is."

Kris managed to recall the hurt Eevee to its Poké Ball, feeling sick to her stomach. This had been a disaster. She should have stayed in the motel. She had never planned for this turn of events...and she never would have imagined what she'd just witnessed either, her brother being commanded from a Poké Ball like an animal. She was now left without useable Pokémon, facing down both Archer and Houndoom, neither of whom showed any form of recognition. Archer spoke before she did.

"Don't try to fight. It won't do you any good."

"You can't listen to him!" Kris exclaimed, "What he's doing will bring down our syndicate."

"Not bring down – lift into glory!" Archer replied with conviction, "We're weakening Team Rocket's power only enough to refashion it. I plan to create an even stronger Team Rocket, to regain our former glory under the leadership of a new don."

"Yourself," she echoed, with comprehension. "Archer you've been lied to. Don't you recognize me?"

Cade broke in, addressing Archer. "Don't pay her any mind. This pretty young lady is one of your misguided former coworkers, sent here to prevent us from achieving our mission."

"Archer..." she emphasized, "I'm your sister."

Archer wavered a bit; Kris noticed it. Cade frowned. "Enough! Don't embarrass yourself, Archer!" He made the swiftest motion with his hand, a signal.

To which Archer's voice became terse as he addressed Kris. "I won't allow you to interfere with our plans."

His eyes were cold, and almost empty of everything save a fixed darkness. Her body felt a chill, and she took two steps backward. Instinctively, she knew she was in trouble. The look in his face was one she had seen before...before he was about to kill.

With a single signal, Houndoom leapt at Kris with its fangs bared. She tried to fend off Houndoom with her whip, but the dog succeeded at last in snapping its jaws on the lash and snatching it away from her. Out of the corner of her eye, Kris could see Archer watching this play out inscrutably.

Disarmed, Kris fled, sprinting up a spiral metal stairwell as fast as she could with the drum of Archer's steps close behind her. She emerged onto the roof, where she found escape barred on all sides by a steep drop. The desert's rugged wilderness stretched towards the faraway peaks of Mt. Battle and their jagged etchings upon the horizon, and daylight – brilliant morning sunshine, which bestowed jarringly scenic beauty upon her stage of violent peril.

She turned to see Archer standing at a distance, at the rooftop exit she had come from. He now advanced; she backed away, taking one step too far.

Height begot a naturally wild wind and as her heel reached the edge of the building, Kris lost her balance in a gust and fell; by a miracle, she managed to grasp hold of a flagpole, saving herself narrowly from the earth miles down.

It seemed like centuries in a full minute. She clinging desperately to the flagpole, he gazing down with conflicted impatience, and suddenly, as if remorse had softened his heart, he reached for her.

"Give me your hand."

Even now, Kris hesitated.

"Quickly!" Archer exhorted her, "give me your hand."

Kris reached gingerly for him, at the same time Archer seized her hand with his, and she abandoned the flagpole for her brother.

Yet in that same instant his eyes betrayed a darker motive, a sinister reality of purpose.

Realization dawned upon her as she said, "You really don't remember."

He smiled back subtly. "You really thought I cared."

And he let her go.

Chapter 23 - Reminiscence

Cade recalled Houndoom and deposited all the Poké Balls in his desk drawer, including the one containing Suicune, but sent out his Espeon. The lithe Eevee evolution appeared with a cry.

"Just in case," Cade told it.

Espeon twitched an ear but responded nothing.

He headed briskly up to the rooftop, followed by his Pokémon, and arrived in time to see Archer drop Kris from the building.

Cade walked over to the edge of the roof and peered down. Below, he could see the city banner fluttering fitfully where it had been partially torn from the flagpole, and Kris lying motionless on the ground.

"It's only one story down. She might've survived," said Cade, handing Archer a pistol. "Go make sure she didn't."

Archer took the weapon.

Kris was passed out, but she was indeed still breathing as he approached. Archer unflinchingly aimed the gun point-blank for the coup de grâce...and then took notice of something.

Beside her, some of her possessions had spilled out onto the ground; Eevee's locked Poké Ball, a small medicinal Potion, and...a photograph. The moment Archer laid eyes on the image, he froze. Slowly, he bent down to pick it up.

It was a familiar image; he didn't know why, at first. There was a woman, with an infant and a boy of nearly five in age. With it came the shiver of a recollection...two people at National Park – yes, that was the name, the park in Johto – and they had found something they'd both lost...and one was he, and the other was...

Archer's throat went dry.

Cade fidgeted restlessly as he stared down at his slave. "What are you waiting for, damn it? Shoot!"

Archer only regarded the image with a kind of dumbstruck horror, and when he glanced with the same horror at the unconscious Kris, and took a shaky step backwards, only then did Cade begin to comprehend what had happened. The Shadow process was not infallible. If brainwashing successfully closed the door to his heart, or that of any of the Pokémon, memories could reopen it.

He reached into his pocket only to be hit with dismay upon finding it empty. He'd left Archer's Poké Ball in his desk, meaning he had no way to reach it fast enough to recall his prisoner.

At that instant, Cade realized the game was up.

All Archer's distraught understanding evolved, in a flash, into a spirit of revenge, and he spun around to shoot Cade. Cade commanded Espeon faster with a thought:

Zap Cannon.

Espeon hurled its fiery electric attack directly at Archer, the ball of lightning striking squarely. The gun fell from his grip as Archer, crying out in pain, collapsed. When he tried to pull himself up and reach for where it had fallen, Espeon attacked yet again, and this time Archer fainted.

Cade's expression contorted into a smirk. Now he only had to ensure they were dead...

He descended from the rooftop and hurried to where they lay unconscious, Espeon trailing after him.

"Hyper Beam," Cade ordered.

Espeon pulled back obediently, and as Cade watched it charging the lethal attack, he heard two familar people shout:

"Copperajah, Protect!"

"Garbodor, Acid Spray!"

He glanced up in time to see two Pokémon spring. Espeon leapt back as the trash bag Pokémon Garbodor lifted its arms and unleashed an aimed dart of poison liquid; acid seared narrowly past and Espeon yelped as it cut across its fur, its Hyper Beam faltering into harmless sparks. Meanwhile, the steel type elephant Copperajah barred their way to defend the injured siblings, sending forth an energy barrier as a shield.

Hurrying right behind the Pokémon were their trainers, Oleana and Rose. Alongside them in turn were a small group of five or six guards with violet neckerchiefs. Seeing the guards open Poké Balls of their own to send their creatures on the attack, Cade dashed back into City Hall to his office.

He scarcely imagined he could run as fast as he did then. Espeon followed at his heels as he practically leapt to the desk, yanking open the drawer and snatching up all the Poké Balls, able to hear his former allies racing to seize him.

Rose and Oleana burst in at that moment to see Cade standing next to Espeon. The Pokémon faced the intruders and growled.

"Teleport," ordered Cade.

Espeon gave a cry, and with a whisk of its forked tail both it and its trainer were warped away.

"Of all the inexcusable...!" exclaimed Oleana, "How did he even teach his Espeon the move Teleport?"

Rose shook his head. "It doesn't matter. We've got a bigger issue at hand."

They returned outside, where the guards and their Pokémon were protecting the seemingly lifeless Kris and Archer. One of the men addressed Rose.

"They're alive sir, but both are out cold and badly hurt."

"It's still early enough that no one else is here to be a witness, but that won't last," contemplated Oleana.

"Two injured," Rose added thoughtfully, "one a uniformed Team Rocket agent... The authorities will ask questions." He and Oleana exchanged a glance, and with wordless agreement Rose turned back to his guards.

"Take them to our property here in Phenac City."

Kris woke up groggily, finding herself lying in a bed. Her muscles ached tremendously.

Recollections of what had happened at City Hall took a moment to return, and as Kris was going over them in her mind and trying to collect her bearings she glanced over to see a Chansey, which gave a cheerful cry to see her awake.

Having alerted its trainer, Chansey was soon joined by a lady wearing the familiar nurse's uniform from the Pokémon Center. Kris knew she wasn't in the Pokémon Center's lodge, however; this place looked more like the guest bedroom of a large house. "...Where am I?" she asked.

"You're at Mr. and Mrs. Rose's place here in Phenac City," came the prompt answer.

Kris let this sink in; she initially thought this meant she was a prisoner of Cipher, till the nurse elaborated in a friendly way:

"They saved you and your brother from Cade. You were both badly injured, but you'll be fine now...Your brother is in the next room."

"Aren't you one of the nurses from the Pokémon Center?"

"The Roses are acquaintances of mine," she explained, "They needed to get someone here with medical knowledge and a healer Pokémon on short notice...someone who wouldn't run to the authorities when they saw the patients."

"I'd like to see my brother," said Kris; as she tried to sit up, she felt a momentary dizziness and had to lie down again. "Ohhhh...that's bad," she groaned.

The nurse checked her blood pressure and said, "You can get up but slowly." She helped Kris get up from bed. "He's right next door. You can go now if you feel better; I'll be in there in a few minutes," added the nurse as she left the room.

Kris stumbled her way to the door and walked out to an elegant hallway. She saw the room next to her had the door ajar and a light on so she knocked. No answer. She walked in and saw her brother Archer lying in bed, either asleep or unconscious.

She sat down at a seat next to him and let her mind wander. So many thoughts passed through her head; she felt sad that she couldn't do more to help. Suddenly, Archer stirred.

"Archer! Archer!" she called him in a loud voice, "It's me, Kris... Archer!"

Archer opened his eyes and Kris felt such joy as she hadn't felt in a long time. "Thank God! You're awake!" she exclaimed, "We were rescued by Mr. and Mrs. Rose."

Archer groaned. "I feel like shit."

"Yeah, I know," agreed Kris. "...my body hurts all over."

"Kris, I'm so sorry...I never wanted you to get hurt."

"It's not your fault."

They were quiet for a while and Kris broke the silence, "I find it amazing that it was the Roses who came to our rescue... seems we were wrong all along about their involvement in your abduction."

Archer sighed, "I realized it at some point when they came to see Cade. I was inside that damn Poké Ball and they couldn't hear me yelling out but I could hear everything they were discussing."

At that point, the nurse walked in followed by Mr. Rose and his wife Oleana. "Good to see you're awake," Mr. Rose said.

"The nurse said your prognosis is good," added Oleana, "You will be well enough to travel soon."

"Thank you...both." Archer said, "Has Giovanni been notified of what has happened?"

"Yes," answered Mr. Rose, "I've called and spoken to him...he will arrive as soon as possible."

"He's eager to see you and Kris," said Oleana, smiling at them both.

Giovanni would be getting there by dusk, and Jessie, James, and Meowth would be meeting him at the airport; giving some time for Kris and Archer to spend recuperating. The more active of the two was decidedly Kris, who didn't leave the premises but made it a point to get up and walk about.

Archer, in contrast, remained in the bedroom all day. He didn't feel well enough to get up, but he was mostly just pensive and wanted to reflect on everything that had transpired. Some part of him held a secret fear that his rescue was a dream, or that these amenities would be taken from him. He'd forgotten the softness and warmth of blankets and pillows; resting in a bed had become a luxury, a priceless one he barely recollected. Yet he still had a sort of inexplicable emotional numbness, which did not cease to be unusual to him.

He glanced up to see Kris appear at the entryway with a tray in her hands. "I brought you food."

Archer gazed at her for a moment and sighed. "Kris, you don't have to coddle me like I'm a newly hatched Pokémon."

"You're injured, remember." She sat down beside the bed. "Besides, you haven't eaten or drunk anything in hours. You should have breakfast."

On a lark he glanced at the clock on the nightstand. "It's almost dinnertime."

"It's breakfast for you. You're breaking a fast."

Archer could not deny that; it was as simplistic a justification as it was logical. He was hungry too, though he hadn't said so and likely would have denied it, and the food smelled delicious.

"I know the laboratory was destroyed," Archer chatted as he ate, "but Cade spoke as if he had some sort of plan in the works. He still has my Houndoom...and now he has your Suicune. He's got all three Legendary Beasts."

"From what I heard, Giovanni's got a Charizard that's almost as strong as a Legendary," replied Kris.

"That Charizard was stolen on one of Jessie and James' missions and doesn't listen to anyone."

"There's got to be a way to get our Pokémon back."

He wished he could share her optimism. "Even if we get them back, Cade has a way of forcing Pokémon and people to change beyond even their own recognition...and making it seem as if it was their choice all along. Houndoom is a Shadow Pokémon now. As for myself...I don't think I've ever felt so vulnerable."

It was only now as Archer truly reflected on it when the depth of Cade's dominion slowly began sinking in. Frailty lowered his voice to nearly a whisper. "They really could have made me do anything they wanted."

"Archer. ...Archer, listen to me. It's all right."

His breath felt tight, and it was only when she spoke that he realized his hands were trembling. He exhaled deeply, trying to force himself back to the peace of the present. When he met his sister's eyes, the same mild blue of his own, she smiled.

"It's safe in here, but not out there," Archer told her. "He can still get me any time I'm in range of that Poké Ball."

He looked embarrassed by the thought, and Kris piped up, "That's nothing to be ashamed of. You're a victim."

"Pfft – victim; as if I'm helpless or some shit. I'm going to make Cade pay for putting me through this humiliation..." As Archer spoke his eyes flashed with blue fire, and he tried to sit up more only to wince and reluctantly lie back down. "...as soon as I recover a bit," he relented.

"We'll tell Giovanni. Team Rocket owns all the Poké Ball manufacturers now. He's got to know a way to release you without having access to the Poké Ball in question."

"Something's happened to me during that captivity," Archer went on. "It feels like there's a constant emptiness of feeling. At one moment it's as if my emotions are gone, then they'll come in a flood..."

A third person broke into their conversation from the entrance. "All the Shadow Pokémon are like that."

They glanced up as Oleana stepped in, and she elaborated, her tone hinting at a kind of resignation to the findings, "In the Pokémon, the sudden emotional rush usually leads to them becoming hyper-aggressive or anxious, so we've taken to calling it Hyper Mode."

"How do you reverse it?" asked Kris.

"The process was experimental," Oleana told her, "and specifically targeted neurons with the intent of altering them. Granted the emotional changes were a side effect, and it was certainly never intended to be used on a human, but on Pokémon the idea was to irreversibly change their elemental..."

"Wait...what are you saying?" Kris interjected.

"One thing is emotional trauma...another thing is the neurological effect of the energy ray, which unfortunately amounts to brain damage." Oleana's gaze softened, but she spoke as straightforward as ever as she faced Archer. "I'm sorry...neither you nor any of the Shadow Pokémon might ever fully recover."

For a long moment, the two siblings just stared at Oleana. Then Kris wrapped her arms around Archer in a tight hug. "My poor brother...!"

"Let go of me," Archer snapped, trying to wriggle free.

Kris did not. "How could they do this to you?"

"Help I'm getting smothered," he protested.

Kris released her grip on him and turned again towards Oleana. "Wait a second, Oleana...wasn't there a myth about Mew, which said it could heal any kind of injury?" Kris persisted.

"I believe so," Oleana replied.

"Well, couldn't it heal what happened to Archer and all the Shadow Pokémon?"

Oleana looked visibly interested in the idea, although as she thought it over, this tempered reluctantly into ambivalence upon hitting the evident roadblock:

"First someone has to find Mew."
